<Author>JellybeanK
<Content>Excellent Value The High Points:1) Beautiful grounds; lush, well tended gardens, very clean 2) Exquisite beach 3) Good food 4) Great drinks5) Pleasant and attentive staffThe Not So High Points:1) VERY hard beds2) Mediocre (at best) air conditioning 3) Stiff competition for shade at both the pool and beach (Get before 6:00 am to reserve)4) Long ride from airport on very poor road The resort is large so be prepared to do a considerable amount of walking. This resort would not be suitable for those with mobility challenges. The a la carte reservation system is a bit wonky (line ups 2 x per day) but the restaurants were all good so its worth your time to line up. Our group liked the Japanese and Mexican best. but the Italian and Steakhouse were also good. Service was very good irrespective of whether or not you tipped the staff. Little things could be improved - there are more restrooms needed at the beach on the Tropical side. The air conditioning could also be improved.Overall, this resort offers excellent value.

<Author>jclarkHalifax
<Content>Excellent Resort for the price Four of us stayed at the Sirenis from April 13th to 20th. The drive to hotel is not bad at all like others have made it to be. There are potholes of course but I have experienced a lot worse here in the Maritimes. Unless you consider yourself a princess then the drive to the resort will be fine.The check in was quick and painless per say. I was surprised when they wanted a $50 deposit for the room safe key on top of the $3/day rental fee. Keep it in mind when budgeting how much money you will need. My parents got a surprise when they got there. They were upgraded to a suite on the cocotal side which was very nice. It had a sunken jacquzzi tub, two showers, massive size room, bigger patio, and windows everywheres. I got to stick with my one bedroom suite on the tropical side which was very nice but not as nice as theirs. Our room was in the F building on the end which made it a bit bigger than the other suites. We went to a friends room and noticed immediately that our end unit room was bigger. The shower can make a bit of a mess because of the small glass wall instead of a shower curtain. I thought we didn't have hot water but we did, the hot water for the shower only comes on in a certain spot on the water dial.Grounds are amazing. Lots of care taken. Flamingos out front. Two peacocks walk around out front by the shops, be careful because they can scare the crap out of you if you don't see them but all of a sudden hear them. The pool is huge. One end is more quiet on the tropical side. The shallow end on the cocotal side has a bit more action. Chairs have to be reserved early in order to get a good spot with shade. The chair wars will never end i am afraid. Great cocktails. I loved the Miami Vice which is not on the menu but is half pina colada and half strawberry daiquiri. The Sirenis Especiale tastes like an orange creamsicle. The white russians are very good as well. Unless you are an apple vacations customer you don't get beer in the mini fridge only water and pop. Bring your own diet coke if thats what you drink because coke light tastes horrible, no diet coke there.The food was good. I loved the soft ice cream served during lunch by the pool. I brought my own root beer to make root beer floats. The nachos and cheese were good. Loved the mashed potatoes, tasted really creamy. The buffet was the same pretty much as any other buffet at any other resort. Same old, same old, omelette station, rice, fish, beef, pork, potatoes of some sort, fruites, no real salad. We ate at the steak house, japanese, and mexican ala cartes. Liked all three. Loved the Japanese one, best meal I have ever had. I have been to the Himachi restaurant here in Halifax and liked the japanese meal at the Sirenis much better. Had the beef tenderloin at the steak house, order it instead of the striploin and you will thank me. You only get 3 ribs if you order the ribs. The dessert selection is good everywheres at the resort.I brought my laptop because they offer free wireless internet in the lobby. Very good speed. Easy to connect to with a password they give you. I was able to receive emails but was not able to send them for some reason. Hotmail worked fine once I set it up. Kept up on the hockey scores for everyone.Beach is okay but not like Varadero, Cuba. It is fine biege sand. The ocean is rought here but still beautiful. Not good area to snorkel. Did the parasailing for $45 for single or $85 for pair. It was fun a decent amount of time. They take video and pictures to try and sell to you after. Each day some photographers come around the pool area with a monkey or parrots or lizard to get photos with. I beleive the cost was $7 USD. The sports bar was completely empty every day. It has ping pong table and pool tables. It has a bar with a bartender that I am sure is bored to death each evening. Entertainment is pretty good. The MC each night is really funny. Overall I would definately go back to this resort. I loved the set up of the resort. I loved the pool area and the lobby.

<Content>Well worth the long journey My boyfriend and I stayed at the Sirenis Tropical Suites from 14-21 April 2008. We had seen the Sirenis Cocotal advertised for 拢300 pp more, but went with the Tropical Suites. Good job, since all the facilities are shared, there are just separate check in and guest service desks, but you could use either anyway! In fact, I'm glad we went for Tropical Suites as we often were in bed before 10pm, and if we had been on the Cocotal side I think the noise of the entertainment would have disturbed us. Our room was in the building with the reception and buffet restaurants (A), on the top floor. My only criticism of the particular room we had would be that the shower took some time to get warm, you had to guess which way to turn it to get hot water, and that the roof of our balcony was made of palm leaves so when it rained the balcony was out of use for several hours... nice nesting place for birds though!The grounds are amazing and the staff obviously take great pride in them as we found lots of staff consantly tending to the gardens. Two nights one of the frogs in the fountain was turned round... was put back straight by the staff very quickly!We used the pool several times during our stay, great for everyone with varying depths. I don't know how often it is cleaned but there seemed to be quite a lot of leaves etc in it, and a very bad smell when sitting at the swin up bar on the Tropical Suites side. We never went to the pool before 10am, and there was rarely a shaded area to sit which is annoying but I have never been anywhere where that isn't the case. I liked the fact you were given 'towel keys' which you changed for towels to use at the pool/on the beach, and you could change for new ones when they got wet. Some people have said the $20 charge for a lost towel/towel key is harsh but I suppose it just ensures you don't dump them. Maybe this facility should be optional?The beach was amazing, quite windy though. Again there were rarely shaded areas to sit but we tended to walk up and down rather than sit and bathe. I just wish there were less men trying to sell you paintings - we only walked northwards once because of an overly persistent seller. The restaurants - the buffet was OK, I didn't expect anything better. I definitely recommend making reservations for the restaurants though. We tried the steak house (Steak great, everything else not that good), Mexican (good, but slow service), Italian (lovely) and Japanese (fab, just the experience). The breakfast in the morning was brilliant and I always found something to eat if I was hungry at lunch. The drinks were on tap all day, but I agree with other comments that the cocktails were too sweet (and I'm a big cocktail fan) and too much alcohol (yes I did say that!!) I highly recommend going to Reef Explorer (or marinarium if you have kids), we also went to Saona Island (fantastic but a long, long journey) and on a day trip called Outback Safari to local houses, schools, mountains, a beach etc which was fab. Overall I would definitely recommend this resort and hotel - I have said that I wouldn't go back but that's only because I never go to the same place twice!

<Author>gdinardo
<Content>Definitely a 4 star resort A friend and I stayed at the Sirenis Tropical from April 12th - April 18th. Overall we had a great time and I would rate this resort at a 4 star level...with some aspects of it being a bit below 4 star quality.Check in was a breeze for us but I think that was attributed to checking in at 3 a.m. Check in took all of about 10 minutes and our room was ready right away.The rooms are a little shoddy and are definitely in need of a bit of maintenance/upkeep but they were far from being horrible. You hardly spend time in your room anyhow. We weren't as impressed with the housekeeping as other reviews have mentioned but it was definitely adequate.I can't say enough about how beautiful the grounds are along with the pool and the beach. It was the first time in Punta Cana for both of us and it was amazing how much more beautiful the beaches are in comparison to places in Mexico. We didn't have a problem with reserving a hut by the pool. We would take turns getting up at 7 and reserving a spot with our towels and our books and everyone seems to respect this method of reserving a spot. All guests were curteous and kind for the most part. We were both a little dissapointed with the drinks. My friend was especially dissapointed with the lack of slushy type drinks. The general mixes that they use for the majority of their drinks are so overly sweet. I could not handle drinking them and my friend has quite a sweet tooth and she couldn't stomach them either. So we stuck to champagne, beer (very good), rum and coke and the like...the wine with dinner was also quite good. The lobby bar is a great place to sit and have a couple of drinks before dinner. The bartenders are great and they also serve great popcorn if you ask for it. I think it may be for the kids but we had no shame in asking for some also! The food in general was quite good. Everything was very tastey and neither of us had any real complaints about the buffets or any of the restaurants. You can only book one reservation per day but we had no problem getting into all the restaurants we wanted to try. We tried the Mexican, the Steakhouse, Jade (Japanese), Cinecitta (Italian) and the Vegetarian restaurants. Some better than others but overall no real complaints as I said before. Nightlife was pretty good also. There was a show every night usually followed by Karaoke or a live band along with the Casino and the Disco that are open all night. There is definitely always something to do and the Animation team was very good at involving the crowd and making sure that everyone was having a good time.The staff were all very kind and helpful. No one expects a tip at all but it obviously is a very nice gesture to these employees who work very hard. They are always smiling and singing and make you feel so welcome.As I said before...overall we had a great time. For the great price that we booked in at, it was definitely worth every penny. I don't think either of us will be back as we would both like to try other resorts in Punta Cana.

<Author>McHutt
<Content>Good Family Vacation Family of 7 stayed at the Tropical side from Apr.11-18 for our annual getaway. Two of us were in Dominican at Dreams for a wedding in Dec. and based on that positive experience, decided to bring the family back to the DR. Rooms: On the whole, I agree with some of the other reviews in that the rooms are tired looking and in need of some repair. Toilet running issue, water flooded (not leaked) through the ceiling during a rain storm, and this was a ground floor room. Big gap under the front door in one of the rooms which meant we had some unwelcome visitors. On the positive side, the maids were excellent and kept everything extremely clean.Pool: I agree saving chairs is annoying, but unless you join in the practice there is no way to find chairs for 7 people much past 10 am. It was also disappointing that they close the pool at 6 pm which I think it too early. The pool itself was great with both shallow and deep areas, but advise you not to sit too close to the long grates between the seating area and the pool due to the smell. This is where a lot of the unfinished drinks get poured by the staff which tends to just sit in a trough under the grates adding to the foul odour. Be aware that although topless is posted as prohibited by the pool, this does not stop everyone and no one does anything to stop it either. Food: Again, agree with many other reviews in that the food at the buffet was good quality but boring. We had two vegetarians in our family, who were pretty much restricted to the same menu day in and day out on the buffet. Suggest they have menus available when booking a la cartes so you know what to expect when making your 2/3 choices. Experienced several of the a la cartes and found the vegetarian to be the most disappointing with obvious microwaved and dried out main dish coupled with cold cooked vegetables...oh well, at leat they offer a vegetarian restaurant just wish it was better. I would also suggest that they rethink the hours of operation for their food services. Many travellers arrive throughout the day, and although the hotel advertises that the Bohio is open, you can only get a very restrictive menu of nachos, fruit, tired looking hot dogs and burgers. Also we were told there would be coffee makers in the room but this didn't happen and if your rooms are close to the pool, you have to walk a very long way to get that first morning coffee. They should consider coffee stands closer to the the pool. Oh yes, while they do have the machines and advertise lattes and cappucinos on their bar menus, they are not available.Spa: Nice facility. The ladies treated ourselves and had relaxing massages while the men enjoyed the n/c jacuzzi and sauna on several days.Entertainment: Enjoyed two of the shows and while extremely loud, they were entertaining. Two in our party were ages 11 and 16, and unfortunately there is not much for them to do in the way of entertainment. Suggest they invest in a games room/area to attract all ages.Late check out: Check out is 12pm, and given our pick up was 5:25 pm, we appreciated that the hotel offers guests late check out for a fee so be aware in advance if you are budgetting. A sheet under the door day of departure advertised $40 for 4 pm check out, but 3 hours later when arranging for late check out, we were told sorry but the fee just went up and it is now $45. While $5 is not significant, it was the principle and dispite a request to talk directly to the manager, which was denied, they stuck to their guns and said it was my choice to pay the extra $5 or not have late check out. Bad form!Overall: We have been to 4+ properties in several countries (Dominican included) and would have to rate this one a solid 3+. The family totally enjoyed the time away together so this review is not meant to be totally critical but rather informative of the property itself. The grounds are beautiful and the staff extremely friendly. I do hope that the management team acknowledges some of the areas which need improvement as this can only add to their business both repeat and new.

<Author>7Odie
<Content>Very Impressed We stayed at the Sirenis Tropical Suites from March 2 until March 13, 2008. We were very pleased with the resort despite having read some of the reviews. Either the people complaining were at some other resort or they are just chronic complainers, as we did not encounter any of the problems that they wrote about. The resort is well laid out and definitely not huge like some of the resorts in the Punta Cana area. You could enjoy a leisurely walk to all amenities at this resort, which is extremely well kept and very pretty. The staff are always working to keep everything clean. They are always smiling or singing and never pass by you without saying Hola. The animation staff are fun and you can get involved with their activities if you want or just say no thanks and they will leave you alone. Our adult children joined us for the first week of our vacation. They had so much fun that when it was time to go home, they were very sad. Our daughter's boyfriend had never been to an all inclusive resort and he had the best time ever. He got involved with the activities, had so much fun and can hardly wait to go away again next year. They are already saving for it. The pool was lovely and very well kept. The beach was great too. During the time we were there, the ocean was fairly calm. You could walk the beach for miles in either direction. It is not very developed in this area and the beach is just naturally beautiful. The food at the resort was great. We have travelled to many resorts and this resort has had the best food by far. We enjoyed the a' la carte restaurants but were just as pleased with the buffet. They even had lobster and shrimp at the buffet one night. The beach grill had wonderful chicken but the hamburgers were pretty good too. The resort allows vendors to come in every other evening. We found these people to be over priced and pretty rude for the most part. We visited the beach vendors on either side of the resort and found the souvenirs we wanted for alot less money. I found the vendors to the right of the resort to be a little more aggessive than the ones to the left. We had some good laughs with the vendors to the left. We met the twin brothers Paul and Ramon who have the ATV's, deep sea fishing, etc. They were wonderful to talk to. We didn't book any excursions but would not have hesitated if that was what we were looking for. We walked down the beach one night when the locals had a bonfire going. They were fishing and having a good time. They welcomed us, showed our son how they fish with their water bottle and fishing line. They let my son try it and he caught a little crab. Paul and Ramon are business men who want people to have a good time and feel safe. That is what keeps a good business going. We went back the next day and finished our shopping with Ramon's help. I look forward to going back to the Sirenis Tropical and visiting with the twin brothers again someday. As I said, we have been to lots of resorts and this one is definitely worth a return trip.

Here at the Sirenis - even the buffet was appetizing and had a great variety each nite. The al a carte restaurants were also great - we had the Italian, the Mexican and the Japanese. Note re the a la carte - you can only book one per day per room - so go early when guest services opens. The maid service was exceptional. Fresh flowers every nite, lots of fancy folded towels (which we did not get last year at Barcelo). I am very partial to a clean room when travelling, and the fact that I could smell the bleach (or whatever they used to clean with) when I came back to room before dinner was heaven to me! Not a hair or sand in site in the bathroom!Don't be put off by the drive from the airport (approx 60 - 75 mins). The next day, we were told to come back the next day! The next day, after being told again - we invoked the help of our tour rep - and had a new room within three hours. So, if you were to ask me if I would stay at this resort again - I've already registered my VIP card for next year! Ask about it from guest services when you go! These people must love their jobs because they're all very happy and happy to help. We tipped here and there, giving more to the people we saw regularly who really took care of us but service seemed great regardless of whether you tipped or not.Nightly Entertainment: Very good and varied. Fantastic dancers and good humour one night with audience participation act. House band sings in the lobby each night and again after the nightly show. They do their best with the same 10 songs. Keep your ears open for the oddest sounding version of Every Breath You Take you've ever heard! hahaNightclub: Drinks are not free here for all guests, only certain bracelets get free drinks from specific tour operators. Good music, good atmosphere, fun disco.Drinks are good, most had a good amount of alcohol in them. Local liquor though, not much top shelf stuff. I heard that if you ask for Bacardi and Dewalt's etc, you'll get it. I'm not a huge drinker so I was perfectly happy. My husband, being more of a connaisseur, would have enjoyed more top shelf stuff.This is a very solid low-glitz 4 star resort with amazing staff. Don't expect too much in the way of luxury, especially in your room, but you'll have a blast. If you don't have fun, it's not because they didn't try their best. The size of the resort is perfect. The guests come from all over and people watching here is fun. My husband and I loved this place, we found it to be both fun and relaxing and would return in a heartbeat.

<Author>4Geminis
<Content>Nice hotel, not many Americans Our family 2 children ages 7  9 stayed at this hotel March 17 - 24 2008 and booked via Apple Vacations. Very easy destination to travel to, although the Sirenis Resort is almost the furthest from the airport in Punta Cana (1 hour drive). The further from the airport, the rougher the seas - so for little kids, sometimes the beaches can be rough and we had 5 out of 7 days the beaches were either totally closed or caution flags flying. The resort is huge - two resorts in one, the Cocotal side and the Tropical Suites side. We stayed in the latter. Our suite was very small, a little sitting area with a roll away bed and a couch - which is where the kids slept, and a bedroom with door which had two full size beds. Other than this furniture, there was almost nothing else as it would not fit in our small rooms. Both rooms had doors that led to a small patio. We were not in our room very much so the size and lack of decor did not matter. Bring your own pillows as theirs are low quality at best. The resort has a huge pool with many different areas, one was more party side (Cocotal) and the suites side was quieter. Live shows nightly were entertaining and fun to see. Food was good to average; Mexican, Japanese and Vegetarian were the best. Don't waste time on the steak house. We were almost the only Americans at this hotel, except for a few spring break college students also on Apple. This meant that we had to use our limited Spanish often which was good for all of us and the staff could not have been more patient with us on this. Very nice staff. Our Apple rep was very kind but often misinformed. Chairs by the pool or beach in the shade were hard to come by but after a while you get the hang of how to make this happen - put out your towels on the way to breakfast or move chairs later, etc. The hotel was full and it was really never a big issue with us. I would say about 40% of the women went topless, which after a while you really don't notice, my kids never commented on it. We felt the rating of 3.5 stars for this hotel was very accurate. The hotel was clean, bug free, kind staff with limited english, and nice facilities. If you are looking for an American resort in a foreign land, this is not for you. Fortunately, we were not. Probably would try something closer to the airport next time as all the activities leave out of this area so we spent a lot of time being shuttled back and forth.

<Author>sunspreeToronto
<Content>the pool kicks! Just got back from our Mar 6-13 stay at the Sirenis Tropical. The suite was spacious, with a TV in the bedroom and a 2nd in the living room - perfect for families. Not sure why a few of the reviewers complained about the mattresses, its stiffness worked for our backs. No issues with the A/C either. Only peeve here is that they do not have a central filtration system for water in the rooms, so you always need to use bottled water to brush your teeth. (This is not an issue in their kitchens). The pool was by far the best we have ever seen anywhere - and we have been almost everywhere. An accomplished swimmer would be hard pressed to swim from one end to the other in less than 15 minutes. It had great parts for swimmers, kids, and yes, drinkers too. The only knock about the general layout of the resort is that this is a sprawling resort, with probably at least 20 buildings on the premises. If you have mobility issues, you will not like it.The staff was great. I was amazed how some of the entertainment staff was able to switch from English to French to Spanish and even German without missing a beat. Sure, a very small number of them did not speak english well, but if you are from Toronto, you will probably be used to that. Besides, its just courteous when you are in a foreign country to pick up some of the lingo in advance (2 cervezas por favor). The nightly shows were good, but the children's shows were awful. The beach was good, but it is not a snorkelers paradise, to say the least. The choppy waves kept throwing up too much sand to get a view of the limited coral reef. Mind you, it made riding the kayaks, hobie cats, wind surfers that much more fun. Bit annoying they would ask for a $20USD security deposit to use their snorkelling equipment when everything else was free (e.g. gym equipment, etc.). We had no problems getting huts on the beach. Oh, for all you parents with young children, although 5% of women there went topless, it did not distract our 7 year old son too much.The food, however, was not as amazing as the rest of the resort. Not sure why they have so many fancy espresso machines everywhere but can't make a decent capuccino. The buffet restaurants could use a little more variety. Management is miserly in handing out dinner reservations for their restaurants, yet they sit half empty at dinner time. The japanese restaurant put on a good show - but it did not actually serve any proper japanese food. The italian restaurant featured a tiramisu desert that, while delicious, was not tiramisu. Well, its not like there is a little Italy or Japan in DR like there is in the more cosmopolitan parts of the world. This was not a problem with the steak restaurant, but be warned they prepare their steaks in a more Latin American style, than say, The Keg. The churrasco steak was better than their sirloin, for example. We did not try the seafood or mexican restaurants there but the people we talked to there raved about them

We will definitely go back. Well worth the money we paid  more!! Definitely a five star resort!!

<Author>G_C_O_8
<Content>Simply The Best We stayed at the Sirenis Tropical Suites the week of February 23 after vacationing the past 2 winters in Montego Bay, Jamaica. Not to take anything away from Jamaica, but we were both extremely impressed with our stay at the Sirenis and quite likely will return again.Overall: A very impressive resort for the money and one that we would recommend to our friends and family.The room: a 2 room suite (although we spent very little time in the front room), huge closet with safe. King bed wasn't the most comfortable. Fresh linens daily. Bathroom was clean and well stocked. Mini-bar was stocked everyday with pop and water. Our room was N106 very close to the pool area with an incredible view. Balcony with 2 chairs and a table. We heard no noise from neighboring rooms.The food: the food was always very good. We tried 3 of the a la cartes (mexican, italian and seafood) and all were good. Otherwise the buffets always had lots of variety and special features each night. The beach grill was a great choice for lunch.Although included we didn't ever try the room service - guess we were too busy. All restauarants were spotless, service was great and lots of places to sit even during busy hours. Bring your own hand sanitizer - oddly, they don't provide.The beach: This has to compare with any beach anywhere in the world. We walked everyday at least 1 hour in either direction and there was still endless beach to explore.. The main beach area is kept very clean. The locals will approach you as soon as you leave the resort property - just be firm but polite, it worked for us.The facilities: Everything from the check-in area to the casino to the ampitheatre are all in great shape and well kept. Staff are always cleaning something, even the outside walkways are mopped. Our only negative coment would be the exercise room - it was an open air, meaning no air conditioning. The equipment was either not working or needing some repair. We didn't try any of the spa services or the hot tub.The bars: Better than we've ever seen with top shelf liquors available if you so ask. We got to try 28 of the 50 cocktails on the drink card along with beer and champagne. The bar areas can have a bit too much cigarette smoke (especially after dinner) but then again we are both non-smokers.The weather: During our week, we had perhaps 20 minutes of rain and that was while we enjoyed the dinner buffet so it didn't interupt anything. Temperature were between 26 and 30 degrees (we guess, because there are no thermometers)The staff: Everyone, from the groundkeepers to the food servers were very polite and very keen to please. These folks are well versed in customer satisfaction. We tried to communicate in Spanish when we could; their use of english can be a bit of a challenge depending on who you talk to.The transportation: Its about 75 minutes to the resort from the airport but it gives you a great feeling of life in the DR. The roads are bumpy and in bad shape. Someday they will decide to finish the newer highway (which is currently half finished I guess). The airport itslef is a bit confusing and busy in the arrivals area (long luine-ups)Excursions: We didn't take any day trips so we cannot comment.but there are many available. Who needs to leave the resort when its this beautiful.Helpful hints: If you want a cabana and chairs by the pool or beach better get our of your room by 7am at the latest. A one dollar trip goes a long way here, the staff are very appreciative. we left small gifts for the housekeeper everyday (school supplies, etc). There are a few shops on the resort but nothing to rave about. There is really no town nearby to shop at either and even the airport had very limited shopping.

<Author>tee-castleford
<Content>Brill stay at the tropical We went as a group of 18 for a family wedding. The hotel is worthy of its 5 star rating. Book into the themed restaraunts asap as they fill up quick. The entertainments team were brill, day and night. You get beach towels there and they have hairdryers in each room. The cheapy cheapy shops arnt as cheapy as the airport on the way out. Which incidentally is down the steps at the back of the pizza counter, (not just the tiny shop as you go in) The trips to saona island, and shark swimming were amazing, the horse riding on the beach, quads and dominican discovery trips were also fab. take airbeds etc with you as they are quite dear there. Barter to at least half of what the cheapy shops are asking, it can be quite fun. All the staff speak good english, but speak spanish. We left a dollar tip for the maid each day, and tipped the waiters. Dont underestimate the sun, get at least factor 50 for kids.(and take loads of it) The beach is amazing and you can parasail for 45 dollars and the kayaks and catermarans are free. banana boat is 10 dollars. It is a truly tropical place, absolutely beautiful. There seems to be a lively, and a quieter side to the pool, the lively side is on the right hand side, the entertainments team are round there. The food gets a bit samey samey, but if youve got kids they will always have burger, chips and nuggets to choose from. You wont starve, there is alot of choice. The japanese and the steakhouse are a must. If you smoke, get your cigs on the way out as you have a great choice of marlborough, or marlborough lights when you get there. It also costs around 5 dollars for a throwaway lighter. You can get all brands in the duty free on the way home. And its very cheap. They are keen on luggage weights though. Take plenty of 1 dollar notes for tips. Get an insect repellant with a high deet content, there seems to be a bad hour on an evening when you are likely to be bit, and use it when you go on the beach as we got sand fly bites which are really itchy. Even though we never saw any sandflies. The sea is very salty but really warm, and if you like snorkelling, there are coral reefs everywhere. And as in europe, you have to bag the sunloungers and palm shelters early doors with a towel. It was an amazing holiday, would definately go again. if you go before april, take the reps, jenna and carly a pot noodle, they are 2 brill yorkshire lasses. Hope you like rum, they have one called 151. this is due to its alchahol content, its very potent, and a rum called mamajuana, which is supposed to increase a mans vitality. You will usually get offered a drop at the cheapy beach shops, either that or a lucky talisman chain. If you do go on the dominican discovery trip, you will stop by a school, we took sweets and pens for the children, they wernt begging, they were lovely. The bus journey to the resort was an eye opener, the roads, hectic driving and local houses etc are a right eye opener. You will see what i mean. Enjoy your hol. We certainly did.

<Author>KingkongMoncton
<Content>Sirenis=Relaxation and Good times First time traveler to Punta Cana and booked via the internet to the Sirenis Tropical from Feb 16 to Feb 23,2008.The only glitch for the whole trip occurred upon our arrival when we were advised that there was an over-booking situation and our group(roughly 10-15 strangers) had to be put up in another resort for the night until our situation was resolved. We were put up at The Grand Oasis for one night and then moved to the Sirenis the next aftenoon.Although we thought the Grand Oasis was a nice resort, the Sirenis was clearly better and it was a definite step up. The site itselft is secluded, well groomed, and well maintained.The staff is extremely polite and EVERYONE will make you feel like a million bucks. SMILES everywhere from the gardeners, maids, kitchen staff, waiters,waitresses, barman,barmaids. Of course, a tip once in a while goes a long way, but isn't that the case everywhere? I found that giving a small tip at the bar daily provided me with a larger part of alcohol in my drink and trust me..they remember you every time you show up. I recommend that you request your drinks with Dark Rum and really recommend requesting BRUGAL Rum. They are less giving with the BRUGAL brand, but it's clearly a better rum. You will find BRUGAL Rum at the D'REY shops on the beach(I talk about them lower) The pool is big... and I mean BIG! Lots of room to swim if you're into pools. Personaly, I found it too hot around the pool as there was practically no wind to cool you down, however pool lovers were well suited judging by the many people enjoying it. We spent much of our time at the beach, where we were lucky enough to get a hut\umbrella. The trick is to get up early(6:30-7:00) and to go to the beach and tie your chairs with towels to reserve your spot. While waking up that early may seem incovenient, it was nice to have a bit of shade in the afternoon and well worth it. Then again, it depends what you're into.The Buffet food was diversified and had something for everyone. Omellettes, hard boiled eggs, bacon, deep fried toasts(yes a bit FAT, but yummy) and fresh fruits for everyone's taste on top of shakes, bread of all kinds, yogurt, juices etc.. for breakfast.Chicken, rice, fish (I wasn't too impressed with the fish, but that's just me) veal (VERY GOOD) vast selection of pasta every night and then all sorts of other things at the supper buffet.For lunch, we stuck to the beach grill-hamburgers, pork chops, fries, chicken every day, or we went to one of the pool restaurants where there was a buffet with chicken nuggets, veal, beef, chicken, rice, salads and MOST importantly, ICE CREAM! Trust me..it was good.We also had the opportunity to try the a la carte restaurants. The Japanese one is the best. The Steakhouse is good. The Vegetarian is good as well but the Mexican one wasn't good and we wouldn't have gone twice. Apart from the Mexican one, all the others use a LOT of Garlic in their preparation so if you have someone who doesn't like Garlic or can't digest it, you would be wise to advise the waiter. The chef at the Japanese restaurant was kind enough to cook a separate pile of food without garlic for a member of our party who was garlic intolerent.If you want to buy souvenirs, cigars, rum, gifts, jewelry etc.. I realized it was better to deal with the locals on the beach then to shop at the resort's shops at the entrance.It's way cheaper anyway, and you can deal. When you get to the beach, I would recommend turning left and walking towards the D'Rey shops. I recommend asking for Louis(fully bilingual-French\English and tidbits of other languages) the last 2 stores on that stretch give you the ability to negotiate your prices. If you want an even better deal, don't be shy to show up with a bottle of water or even better a Coke bottle for the big boss. That crew is very friendly, talkative and not as aggressive as the others.BRUGAL Rum is found at these shops, and was not findable at the Duty Free shops at the airport, so I would recommend purchasing at the beach shops as the airport stuff was way pricier and it was the stuff we found in Canada ( Bacardi etc)If you make the mistake of walking right when you go to the beach(towards the leaning Palm Tree-you'll know when you'll see it) then I would recommend going directly for shop number 4 and once again, water is welcomed.Folks, we really enjoyed our stay at this resort and would consider going again in the future. It would have been an excellent review if not for the first night sleepover at the Grand Oasis (which I found to be a lower level of establisment even though it was nice)Hope this helps you in your search for a good trip. Enjoy your stay.. we sure did!

As I have traveled throughout the world I realized that a 5-star property in some countries does not often translate into the American ideal of a 5-star property. I read every review I could possibly read and made what I hoped to be a good decision. My tour was booked through USA3000 (Apple subsidiary), My travel dates were from Jan.26 to Feb. 2nd. I paid 699.00USD- 827.00USD including all taxes, transfers and fees. Honestly, I had reservations (no pun intended). I mean this price for 7 days- including nonstop airfare from Cincinnatti seemed rather unbelievable. I reconciled myself to a sub-par experience-quite frankly...but decided to make the most of it. I mean come on...at that price it would be hard to complain about much, right?I contacted the hotel directly before leaving. I think I am a rather shrewd fellow. I explained how I was fully aware that in the tropics buiding maintenance can be an ongoing issue..you know mildew, room deterioration, insects, etcetera. I continued it had been sometime since I had taken a vacation and I wished to address any possible issues prior to departing. I did not insist on anything (typical American mistake)- rather I coolly inquired- if perhaps it wasn't too much of a bother -I could be put into a room away from construction and /or any problems. See... I gave my name a voice...connected personally with my host...and was most respectful in my inquiry. I was assured all would be done to to make my stay as enjoyable as possible. Frankly, I was skeptical. We departed and upon arriving in Punta Cana boarded our coach to the hotel...about an hour or so away. From reading some reviews I was expecting a wagon pulled by a team of donkeys (sometimes Anglos are sooo uptight). The road began 4 -lane and then turned to 2 and yes it had a few bumps...guess what folks you're not in Monaco..and it discourages me to no end how some people can be so negative and tight-***** about everything. Sirenis is just past Dreams. While Dreams is certainly more expensive Sirenis' entrance is hands down more dramatic and beautiful. There is a huge fountain of a mermaid (like the logo). You drive up a long and winding flora-filled drive to the open air lobby, Immediately a bellman took our bags and directed us to the reservationist. In no more than five minutes a friendly hostess appeared with the most delicious and refreshing fruit drink. We were assigned a room within 30 minutes and directed to our room. No bags to worry about the bellman had it all taken care of. The lobby is large, open and airy. As you walk back you pass identical common areas one on eithe side with many people seated playing cards, drinking, just chilling. I immediately noticed the crowd was international and I appreciated that. What do you learn or experience if you stay with the same people all the time-nothing. You pass the first two buffets which are extremly large and then all of this opens into two walkways. The Cocotal is on your right and the Tropical is on your left. I was assigned quarters in bldg, M. Guess what? I paid for the standard room. Turns out my considerate inquiry paid off...we were given a suite on the Tropical side. No questions asked. This would NEVER happen in the US even at a Holiday Inn..you and I know you would pay extra or you would be [--] out of luck. The site is quite large with extensive landscaping, soothing music plays in hidden boxes as you walk down the long walkways past the lodging. First you hear the crash of the waves..then you see the pristine water through the cocout palms (the resort was carved out of a coconut plantation,,,so palms abound). The pool is a continuous behemoth that encompasses the whole of the back side of the resort. Numerous bridges traverse it and beautiful sculpturres of sirens and a mermaid center it. Very striking and unbelievably large. The room was immaculate. In the bathroom (Clotilde) our room technician..I would never say maid...had laid out an array of tropical flowers. They dotted the large shower..which by the way had great pressure and both regulated hot and cold nicely. Also, the shower had tons of spray options...even full-body. On the bathroom counter there was an assortment of toiletries and plentiful fluffy, white, and soft towels and hand clothes. The bathroom is quite spacious. As it was a suite we had a small sitting area with television which opened into a large bedroom with a balcony. We were on the 2nd floor (only two) and our patio had a lovely view of the pool and sea. NOTE: In either Cocotal or Tropical I reccommend you ask for a bldg. as far from the lobby as possible, as this is where all of the noise is. Logically, the further away from the lobby the more tranquil and closer to the beach. Please, leave the person taking care of your room a gratuity...since it is all-inclusive it is beyond me to think this would not just be common courtesy and just the right thing to do in any person's mind. These people don't have the luxury of travel and as you are the ambassador of your country don't be a greedy [--]. I brought neat treats and cookies which I left with my tip. I also brought some small inexpensive things like those comfortable Croc shoes and some underwear for children, aspirin, children's vitamins. You know these people are just like you and me. They just weren't fortunate enough to be as lucky as we are. So think about others a little. So little means so much to people. Another thing...I have been to all corners of the Earth...truthfully..and the Dominican people are the friendliest people I have yet to meet. The mantra was...look you work hard and are here to rest, have fun, and relax....work and troubles are home you are here now and we are here to see you are taken good care of...WE WERE ACTUALLY TOLD THIS BY OUR APPLE REPRESENTATIVE AND BY SEVERAL EMPLOYEES!!! They summed it all up by saying...NO Problem! I have read reviews about the aggravation some people experienced here, and I just do not know how this can be true. Sure enough I had prepared myself to expect it, but it never happened once. Perhaps this has something to do with Apple Vacations. All I can tell you is the rep was always available and so helpful and friendly. A meeting was held the day after we arrived and it was sooo reassuring and helpful. It was my understanding that a party could eat in 3 specialty restaurants and from the posted reviews the lines were hours long to get a reservation. It took me ten minutes to make reservations. The specialties are much better than the buffets- we ate our allotted 3 times and I went to the front desk and they put me in specialties every night...NO PROBLEM! And importantly...NO ADDITIONAL FEES! You can even order room service free and you have an inroom fridge with drinks and snacks free. The beach was pristine and the sand was so cool under foot and the seclusion of the property really added to its charm and appeal. Palms fringe the beach in either direction and there is no congestion of other hotels...to me it was sheer paradise. There are tons of beach chairs. I did not choose or care about the covered huts-perhaps I should have as I got severely burned---be sure -and I cannot be adamant enough- take a serious waterproof SPF..I made a big mistake the sun is HOT! I was so very grateful for the constant breeze...or else the intense sun would have been quite unbearable. There is a large BBQ on the beach with burgers, hotdogs, grilled chops and chicken and fries and drinks. I generally skipped breakfast and at 11:30 each morning the BBQ is served up...delicious and I just ate at the beach. A man would come and take drink orders. If you learn any Spanish remember...fuerte...this means strong or else you will be treated to a rather weak concotion. Also, the resort has a great many employees and their job seems to be to get the guests involved in activities. I do not have children, but everyday I saw the children's camp and each child seemed to be having the time of their lives with the camp counselors. On the beach they play volleyball and ask you to join in and everday they do aerobics with a very fit instructor. I mean it is unbelievable. I went walking on the beach and it was just beautiful...like Gilligan's Island...a cheesy analogy but let's be cheesey shall we. You get what I mean..secluded and palm-fringed . I highly reccommend the banana daiquiri and the Sirenis cocktail...try them and see.In the evenings they have different types of entertainment. You must go to the shows put on by the I think they call them animation team..anyway the theatre is adjacent to the disco and casino (stay out of the casino)- Our Apple rep said they have something called progressive roulette or something, Initially, you bet a small amount and unbeknownst you can end up owing the house a lot of dinero and I don't even want to think what could happen if you don't pay up. Back to the entertainment...these people are surprisingly talented and very entertaining-quite professional. You wll really enjoy it and a bar is right there. Before the entertainment the lobby has great live music- among them a very talented red head and her husband on keyboards..the Captain and Tenille of Punta Cana I guess..At any rate they are fabulous and the entire time a cocktail waitress is taking drink orders, placing snacks and clearing away messes. After the shows they have an incredible discotheque. With Apple Vacations all top-shelf liquor and beer is free...How can this be. I just couldn't believe it. Yes, this review is long. I think it should be detailed...I wish I had had it before I went. I wish for you the same experience I had. Look...don't be sooo fussy and uptight. Talk to people...take a moment to look at things if they are selling..it's what 3-4 minutes..bargain if you want something or just respectfully decline. Say hello to the people you pass and be gracious to your hosts and room attendant. I promise you this place rocks! I will return soon and frequently. There is no better deal to be had...frankly,I still am in shock that I paid 699.00USD plus taxes totalling 824.00USD and did not take my wallet out once in 7 days. I did place some pastries on a plate and take them to a beach hawker down the beach after meeting her for her son. She cried. If you are hesitating between Cancun and Punta Cana I guess it depends on what type of vacation you want...If you want glitz and Las Vegas on a beautiful albeit congested beach Cancun is for you. Of course, Cancun is not Mexico in that it is not authentic at all-it is no different than Vegas. Sirenis is not in Bavaro and some would argue this as a negative. To me it is a positive...the seclusion was fantastic...yet there are tons of people to meet. My partner and I met the nicest couple from Manchester, England-in 50's we are in late 20's and they were just great, fun people. We had a blast at the disco and shows talking. Lastly, I read several reviews where people complained about the language barrier. Again, I think this has more to do with Americans in general thinking that the whole world should speak English. You are in the Dominican Republic. Look not once was this a problem...I really think people hyperbolize. Of course, if you present yourself as a typical [--] then more than likely you will be treated like an [--]. We have much more in common than not. Actually, learn a few Spanish words/phrases...it shows respect and breaks down barriers we so often out of our own ignorance erect. By all means go...and have a blast like I did. This place is magnificent! If I can be of any assistance or you have any further questions just e-mail me. I would be happy to help in anyway I can. Lastly, if you are able to book through USA 3000 or Apple Vacations I cannot reccommend it enough. They take care of everything so you don't have to wory about transfers and additional fees. I in no way expected the treatment they delivered. I have been to Bali, Thailand, Maldives, Fiji, Phuket even Cambodia and Malaysia...I have never toured with abeter outfit. They have their job down pat and you have again...NO PROBLEMS!!!!

<Content>Awesome Resort We spent the week of February 16 鈥?23, 2008 at the Sirenis Cocotel Resort in Punta Cana. We got a great deal from Applevacations which we made even better by going through Traveloni who takes 5% right off the top. We have used them numerous times and have always been very pleased with their discounts and customer service.We got off to a rocky start by leaving 1 hour later than scheduled. We found out on the flight back that the delay was due to USA 3000 having to fly a pilot in from another airport. Once in the air, USA 3000 was awesome. Great planes and great service on the ground and in the air. Only problem is a recurring problem of not enough food for everyone on the flight. Always, always, by the time they reach our seat (usually mid-plane) they are out of one of the selections. This trip, it was so bad, that they were selling the food that was intended for the return flight later that evening. I hope those folks ate at the airport before boarding to go home.Arrival at Punta Cana airport was unbelievable. We have been to the DR 5 times and have never seen the airport so busy. The tarmac was full of planes. Luckily, our luggage was promptly unloaded and the Punta Cana immigration/customs inspectors were not checking/inspecting many visitors. We then made our way to the arrival area and after notifying the Apple rep that we would not be taking their transfer (they always look so hurt that you are not taking their transfer) went with our pre-arranged taxi transfer. We have used Sr. Silva鈥檚 Dominican Airport Taxi service numerous times and could not be happier. They are always where they say they will be and they are always on time. Their vans are new and in great condition with perfect Air Conditioning!! Also, I always bring at least one suitcase of donations for the children and leave it with the driver who delivers it to Sr. Silva for distribution to a school or orphanage. The drive to the resort was nearly an hour, which I expected. Sirenis is the next resort to the north of Dreams (previously Sunscape the Beach). We have been to Sunscape 3 times and the last time was in October just before the hurricane. The road was in bad condition at that time, but it is now deteriorated to be nearly unusable. I love Sunscape and Sirenis but will not be returning to that area until the new road is completed. I will not put either myself, or my husband through that terrible drive with pothole next to pothole.We arrived at least 20-25 minutes before the Apple transfer bus. As we were leaving the front desk, they were walking in and they looked peaked/green from that roller coaster drive on that nasty, nasty road. Check-in was very smooth and efficient. At that time, we were given our room cards, towel cards and safe key (free safe with Apple). We were also given a sheet to request our ala carte restaurants for the week. Another Apple benefit, whereas others had to stand in line at guest services in the morning to request an ala carte for the evening meal. Also, we were given an Apple room service menu, which was free to Apple guests, but had a fee for other guests as per the menu in our room.I had emailed a request for a top floor room. We were assigned to building J, second floor. I was a little disappointed until I looked out the window and found out it was an ocean view room. It was a spectacular view!! Great, spacious patio with a table and 2 chairs. Just make sure you don鈥檛 close the patio door when you are outside or you will be locked out of the room. The room was a comfortable size with two full sized beds. The beds were hard ( but we have had harder beds at Sunscape and in Mexico) with the tiniest pillows. Minibar had Coke, diet Coke, Sprite, water and Presidentes!! Closet was very large with shelves and lots of hangers. The safe, which was inside the closet, was on the small side. I don鈥檛 think many laptops would fit inside of it. Our safe had a hand towel inside of it. Once I removed it, I realized why it was inside the safe. The safe was lined with rust!! Luckily, I had gallon sized plastic baggies that I just put our camera case and valuables in to protect them from the rust. It was a pain dealing with that, but I did not want to give up that view just to get a better safe. The bathroom has an odd little half wall between the toilet and vanity that just takes up space and makes the bathroom small and awkward. Lots of hot water and great water pressure, though. Plenty of towels and once the young man cleaning our room realized we had brought our own face cloths, he made sure to leave face cloths daily. In addition, he would come by around 5 pm, when he knew we were getting ready for dinner, to check if we needed more towels, coke, beer or coffee. He took good care of us and we made sure to take good care of him. Not only did we leave him a nice tip daily, but we also left him baseballs, baseball gloves and ball hats. Just want to mention that our building had an elevator that was very convenient to use if you did not want to or could not walk up the stairs as well as taking your luggage down.The beach was just beautiful. Seaweed was raked daily. Sadly, some folks think it is OK to just toss their cigarette butts in the sand. That is just ugly鈥?These same folks think it is OK to just leave their cups and plates and other trash laying around and the hotel staff has to pick up behind them. That is so sad and so disrespectful on so many levels鈥?.The staff works so hard all day and night, picking up other peoples messes and cleaning, shining and washing.If you want a palapa or shady area at the beach or pool, you have to get up real early. I am an early riser and was amazed at all the chairs that had towels on them at such an early hour (sunrise). Later the first day, I noticed that when folks were packing it up for the day, they were tying their towels to the chairs for the next day. Staff does not remove the towels for the evening. Very interesting chair saving ritual.The pool was top notch. Great design with shallow areas for the kids and deep areas for the adults. Early every morning, workers were cleaning the pool. By mid afternoon, straws and wrappers were floating in the pool. That is not due to lack of cleaning, that is due to lack of manners by some guests!! Two swim up bars. Two beach buffets adjacent to the pool. Very well planned beach and pool area. Bathrooms were located in both beach buffets which were manned with a housekeeper all day. Not only were those bathrooms decorated with flowers, but they were kept spotlessly clean. The food was the best. The buffet did not have a huge selection, but what they had was excellent. Good quality food, prepared well. We would have been happy to eat at the buffet morning, noon and night all week. It was that good. The service at the buffet was over the top. We have never been at an all-inclusive where you were always greeted with a smile and taken care of so promptly. We did eat at the seafood, steakhouse and Italian restaurants that were all very good with excellent service. That is were this resort excels. The people working there are genuinely happy to have you as a guest. Prompt and efficient customer service was the norm.Sirenis is a beautiful resort with a very hardworking staff. But, unfortunately until the new road is completed we will not be returning to that area of Punta Cana again. I would return in a heartbeat, but the thought of enduring that bumpy twisty road again is not possible.

<Content>Not for Picky City People The staff are very personable and friendly. But it does take a long time for tables to be cleared if you eat poolside. As well, there are some minor language barriers. The rooms are decent, I sugest you bring your own pillow and pillowcase, if you dont like your face rubbing on a rough sham  pseudo pillow. As well, the fresh omelette bar in the mornings  pasta bar at lunch is a relief if you like to know how your food is handled. From the a la carte restaurants, a lot of our group liked the vegetarian restaurant (funny thing,, none of us was vegetarian). The drinks are average as well, but not by average Canadian standards. Do not expect amazing international hard liquour, ie. if you ask for a rum/coke, make sure to ask for bacardi/coke, canadian club/ginger ale etc. If you ask, you shall receive. But they don't even have smirnoff vodka....?!?!PLEASE READ: drinks end at midnight, after that you pay $$.Overall, if you're travelling with children, not picky with what you eat, fluent in spanish, you just want to sit on a beautiful beach (that does have lots of dead coral reefs), and swim in the pool, this place is for you. If you are a big drinker, clubber, foodie, enjoy fine arts/shows, enjoy scoring good shopping deals in a foreign city, and into modern music, this place is NOT for you.Some said this was a 4-star resort, but maybe by punta cana standards. I would give it a 3-star. But since this trip was paid by my parents, this was still a great resort to me ;)Cheers! PS. We named it Punta Canada since we met TONS of Canadians!

<Author>IllinoisFuntimer
<Content>Great Resort We just returned from a week at the Sirenis Tropical Suites. What a pleasant surprise for us, since we read alot of reviews about the resort after we booked our trip through Apple Vacations and were a little leery about the trip. As stated in the reviews, the road to Sirenis was bumpy, but nothing worse than the roads in Illinois during the winter. The country side could be beautiful, if everyone did not litter.Upon our arrival, we were given a cool drink while we waited to check-in. Check-in was very easy and took less than 20 minutes. For some unknown reason, our rooms were up- graded to junior suites (there were four of us, two couples, 2 rooms). Our rooms were nice and clean and were located just off the beach and directly across from one of the pools. The resort grounds were really pretty and well maintained. Everyone was very friendly and tried to meet all of our requests. Since, we don't speak Spanish, a few times we had difficulty talking with some of the staff but eventually got what we wanted. For the first few days it was hard to get Diet Pepsi/Coke put in the mini bar of our rooms, but after that, housekeeping always remembered. Even though Sirenis is all inclusive, small tips really help you get extra attention. Two restaurants were located down by the pools and beach which made it very handy to have lunch and not leave the beach or pool area. The food was very good, well prepared and usually fresh. Of the nine restaurants, we ate at seven of them and really enjoyed the Italian restaurant. The four of us could not find any complaints about the resort itself, but some of the other guests were very rude and sloppy, since we could usually find dishes and glasses on the beach or around the pool when we went walking early in the morning. The resort staff were usually out around 7 am to rake the beach, clean the pool and clean the common areas. All in all, we had a great relaxing vacation and would probably go back to Sirenis Punta Cana in a few years since we like to visit a lot of different places and resorts.

<Content>Great beach vacation!!!!! returned recently from a great week of fun in the sun at the sirenis in Punta Cana. Dec 30th- thru jan 5th. We LOVED the ocean, beach, and pool. The resort was great, very clean and good friendly service. The decor in the rooms was a little outdated, but it was very clean and comfortable with fresh flowers in our room every day. Lots of restaurants or buffets to choose from- enjoyed in particular their new Japanese restaurant; eating at the grill on the beach for lunch; ordering room service for breakfast. Many locations to get a cocktail or beer. The beer was good as were the pina colada's and the local drink mamajawana. The nightly entertainment was decent- best show was the Michael Jackson impersonators. Would not recommend this resort for snorkeling - water was too rough although there are coral reefs in the area. Enjoyed the excursions we took to go horseback riding and ATV riding. We booked them thru the restaurant on the beach located next door to the resort. Their prices were half of the tour companies and were much more convenient with smaller groups and more personal service. As far a negatives go for the area- the roads in the punta cana area were HORRIBLE . I would not recommend any bus trips or excursions other than to get to and from the airport. Overall this was a great beach vacation, and great value for the money. I would return to the area again and to this resort.

<Author>under65
<Content>First time all inclusive I would agree with most of the comments from sc00by-doo therefore I will only comment on other points.We accompanied two other recently retired couples flying out of T.O. on Skyservice Airbus 320 organized by Nolitours.Flight:Great service from Skyparx delivered us to the terminal in plenty of time. If you are on the tall side, ask for the seats next to the emergency exits over the wings. Food consisted of a sub-like sandwich, dessert bar and small container of water. You pay for alcohol. Earpieces cost $3 if we listened to the on-board movie but were free on the return trip. Merchandise can be purchased duty-free i.e. Bicardi (1.4L) for $18 CDN and Crown Royal (750 mL) for $18 CDN. It can also be ordered for delivery on the return flight.Airport/TransferArrived at 11:30 p.m. Luggage was quickly processed and our transfer mini-bus was ready to go. It was an HOUR long trip around more pot holes than roads. Some of our members used Gravol to ease the experience. Just remember this is a country that is desperately trying to improve. Our tourist dollars might help.Arrival At 12;30 p.m. there was a buffet ready for us. Our suite (pool view) was clean. Everything worked, including the two TV's.The staff at the front desk spoke English (as well as other languages)TippingWe tended to tip our room person more than others. Our tourist agent suggested that purchases from the dollar store as well as cash might be in order. We brought things that might be suitable for children as well as adults.FoodThe buffets provided a variety of foods for all meals. Be prepared for digestive disturbances. Some of our friends depended on Immodium which they brought along with sunscreen. We were entitled to 2 ala cartes but we had three. Of the three, Italian, Steak and Mediterranean restaurants , we preferred the Mediterranean for its food and service. Reserve early and be on time. ExcursionsWe looked for the excursion with the shortest transfer distance so it was the Sunset cruise. We enjoyed a half hour of snorkeling. Some brought their own equipment. Lots of alcohol was available. The cruise included an on shore lobster dinner.Several of our group had digestive troubles after this day. There are many other excursions available which vendors sell near the front desk. These vendors speak many languages. Sign up early.Beach/PoolDespite what some have said, you will need to reserve a loungeif you hope to have a padded one or one with a synthetic mesh. It appears that people respect a towel on the lounge as an indication of a reserve sign. People will keep the same lounge all day. We kept our towel all week as they were not always available. Remember that a tube or SPF 30 sunscreen costs $18 US at the resort for something that costs $9 CDN. Even with waterproof sunscreen, I still had a tan. If you are bringing children, don't forget to prepare them for toplessnessShopping There is a small mall at the resort that consists of a variety type store, a first aid station and a store that sold local wares. A local store owner about 5 minutes from the resort will pay for your taxi ride if you shop at no other store. The prices for jewelry appeared reasonable. The beach vendors are friendly and expect you to barter. They also like to collect tourist's hats. So why not barter.Children's Play areaOn the way to the small mall, there is a building that houses a play area consisting of a pool and badminton table and other games.In all, we thought that the staff performed their duties very well. Many of the room staff do not speak English so a Buenos dias or a Buenas noches or a Ola helps to bridge the gap.

<Author>Beachbum104
<Content>Beautiful place to visit We stayed at the Sirenis resort from December, 31st, 2007 until January, 8th, 2008-over New Year's. We were six people in total. We stayed on the tropical side of the resort.I am currently 19 years of age so naturally I my opinions may differ from people who have young children or who are older. We did however travel with two 12 year old boys who also had a wonderful vacation. Over the years I have been fortunate enough to vacation to many places in the carribean around Christmas time, so I do have experience with all inclusive resorts.Staff/Services: * * * * We found the staff at the resort to be extremely hard-working people who want nothing but to make your stay at the resort relaxing and very enjoyable. They are very dedicated people. They work six days a week, 10-12 hour days and they always have a smile on their faces and are able to assist you with any problem that you may have. Tips were not expected but they were greatly appreciated.Rooms: * * * *The rooms were very comfortable and clean. I read a review posted earlier on and the people were complaining of uncleanliness and mold in the bathrooms. In our room and the other room that my other family members were staying in they was absolutely no mold in the bathroom, the rooms were kept very clean and simple. The beds were comfortable and it was nice to wake up every morning to sunshine and blue skies, I am from Montreal so it was a nice change for this time of the year. There was a lot of closet space and general space in the rooms, you didn't feel cramped. The air-conditioning and heating worked well. We had a pleasant view of our balcony of the gardens. Our room was cleaned each day very nicely. The only thing to beware of is that you use your towels wisely, we were four people in one room and some days only 3 towels were given. The chambermaids were more than happy to give us more towels it's a hassle to go and find them.Beach/Pool area/Chairs: * * * * * The beach was breathtaking, white sand and blue, blue water. The beach was long enough to take walks on. The animators keep the kids amused with lots of games and sports. The pool area was large and kept clean all of the time. The pool set-up was very unique, many different areas to go in and a pool-bar at each end of the pool. There was also a shaded part of the pool which was a nice break if you got too hot on the beach. Chairs on the beach or near the pool were hot commodities. You definetly had to wake-up early if you wanted one of the large umbrella/huts for the day. Chairs weren't that hard to find. One day we only arrived at the beach at around 2:30 and we found 5 chairs within 15 minutes, so they weren't to scarce. At either end of the beach there were a few stores. The stores on the right hand side of the beach were just as good as the other ones but the people are very aggressive, if they see you coming from 100 ft away they will hassle you until you come and see what they are selling. The stores on the left hand side of the beach were just as good but you didn't feel like you were being forced into buying anything. The people on the left hand side of the beach also offer excursions like horseback riding and ATV'ing. We enjoyed both of them. The tour guides are very friendly and try their best to accommodate your needs. They also helped us find someone who was willing to take us all out on doon buggies, since they didn't offer the service. Food/ specialty restaurants: * * * * I wouldn't say I'm a picky eater, but probably more pickier than some. I was still able to find great food for every meal. I enjoyed a custom made omelet every morning and crepes for dessert every lunch at the buffet beside the beach. The specialty restaurants were pretty good, nothing to spectacular. We went to three specialty restaurants. Mexican, Italian and Steak. The Mexican restaurant was probably my personal least favourite. The Italian food was alright but for some reason the service was very slow at this restaurant. The steak was very good. Making reservations for these restaurants was interesting. You would have to arrive at 8:30 in the morning to stand in line where it would take each person 10 minutes to make reservations. When you finally made it to the front of the line we were told everything was full. But after talking to the person for 10 minutes you find that every restaurant is available. Spa: * * * *  Very typical north-american spa. Very clean and the service was very good. They had just about every service, waxing, hairstyling/cutting, pedicures, manicures, facials, mud wraps. The prices weren't too bad, probably equal to what you would pay at home or less. I enjoyed a pedicure and a facial, both were very relaxing. There is also a steam room and a jacuzzi. Both of these are free. They also have showers. In the spa there is also a gym, with personal trainers.Entertainment: * * * The shows are every night at 9:30, the kids really enjoyed them, they were very entertaining. Before each show they give out prizes to the people/children who won playing the games or sports during the day. The shows are very well put together. Night life: * * * the night life if probably like any other resort. The bartenders are friendly and quick. The discotec opens at 11 p.m. and goes until 3 a.m. Like any other place you have to be careful how much you drink and who you are accompanied with, you have to remember it is a foreign country you are traveling to and just take certain precautions. Other information:There are a few stores in front of the resort (located inside the compound) There is a beach store and a cigar store. There is also a clinic with a doctor, incase it is needed. There is a ATM located in between the stores. I was able to take money out in Pesos one day but the next day it was empty. It's obviously good to bring all the money you need with you on the trip, and of course in american money. No one will exchange pesos or any other currency for you. There is also a park for children and some tennis courts located near the spa. The casino is located near the theater, it's a small casino.  All in all it was a very pleasant stay. Reading some of the other reviews you have to wonder just how ridiculous some people are. If you are looking for absolute perfection, you aren't going to find it at this resort or any other for that matter, it's not a developed country, I'd say they are offering the best they can if not more. I was satisfied with it, I feel I got my money's worth. I would definitely return. Hopefully my review was helpful in some way!

<Author>J-Roc123
<Content>Great Value for the Money Just got back from Sirenis Tropical Suites. We had a two-week stay Dec 15-29/07. We are a family of four who are experienced travellers. We have been to about 20 all-inclusive vacations at various high-end and low-end resorts in the Caribbean, DR, Cuba and Mexico. Our family had a lot of strong feelings about this resort, our fellow travellers and the whole experience, so here goes...... The Good:1. Beach was long, clean and just beautiful. Fine brown sand and no rocks. Red flags were up for a few days, but ocean was still swimmable.2. Pool scene was excellent - clean, large areas for swimming. Shallow areas for kids. Plenty of stuff going on, lots of bars and snack areas to eat lunch, get ice cream etc. Best of all, the pools are very close to the beach so you can alternate back and forth during the day without a lot of walking. Alejandro and Willy at the Beach Bar were excellent!3. Service was EXCELLENT from just about everyone - Restaurant workers (thank you to Juan and many others), chambermaids, Animation team (Action Jackson, Spaghetti), Gardeners, Front Desk - you name it. The people who say the Staff were rude were obviously rude to everyone themselves. Remember the golden rule people! Tipping and gift giving was appreciated, but not necessary to get good service. We brought a lot of children's Christmas gifts down for the locals - this is a very heartwarming thing to do and seemed to go over even better than money tips.4. A la Carte Restaurants - We ate several times at these and found the food to be very good with fantastic service. Contrary to what the brochures say, you can book these every day, one per day. Line ups to reserve were also not bad. Italian, Mexican and Chinese we thought were the best. Steakhouse and Seafood were good also. We heard good things about the Creperie, but did not go. Gourmet restaurant costs $35 extra/person - no thanks.5. Weather was perfect for 2 weeks straight - 29C, mostly sunny, very little rain, nice breeze off the ocean.The Bad:1. Rude tourists from Canada (sad as that is to say) and Europe (not England). I dont know what everyone paid to get to this hotel, but based on the deal we got - I think this place was a steal. Why some people expect the Ritz Carlton in a poor foreign country like the DR and then complain about everything is beyond our comprehension. Yes the place is not perfect - but you folks need to take a chill pill and take some reponsibility for making your vacation enjoyable. Example #1 - you miss your bus back to the airport and then publicly berate others as a result. It is YOUR responsibility to get on the right bus at the right time.Example #2 - no towels or beach chairs - figure out how to get them and you will be happy. Yelling at the poor guy cleaning your room usually doesn't work. 2. Airport Arrival/Hotel check in was terrible - Nolitours couldn't seem to count how many seats on the bus were needed to bring their clients to the hotel - some sat on their own luggage/other people's laps for the 1 hour+ bus ride. We were also not told of an orientation the next day (although I found out by asking others the next morning). I expect a bit more from a Canadian Tour Rep - they just seem to be glorified Excursion Salesman. This is the second year in a row Nolitours did a poor job for us and we will not be booking with them again even if they are cheaper than most. We also waited 3 hours when we got there to get our room keys - not a good start, but it got much better from there.Other Notes:1. Excursions - We went on Bavaro Runners Safari Tour - thought it was a very good day in the Dominican countryside. You get to see a real school, a farm where they grow and make coffee and cocoa, short horseback ride, nice lunch in the mountains, end it with a nice swim at beautiful beach. We heard mixed reviews on the Saona Island tour.2. Rooms - Mattresses are very hard - otherwise we thought they were OK. Yes there was a towel shortage (the Hotel should buy some more) and they did come late, but they eventually came. A combination of a fully-booked Christmas week and people stealing towels did stress the system out. HINT - Keep your blue beach towels overnight so if you want a late afternoon shower you can use these.3. Beach Chairs - Get out early during peak season to get what you want. Reserving beach chairs with your stuff is an age-old custom that you will need to adapt to.4. Bring mosquito repellent - you will need it at night.5. Bring lots of your own sunscreen - $20+ per bottle for bad brands on sale at their resort store. We saw lots of lobster-like people who still can't figure out (or dont care to) how to avoid getting burned. If you are lilly-white, dont use a #2 tanning oil or you will get badly burned, even on a partly cloudy day in December!6. Bring lots of small US bills to tip people with.7. Cant comment on the shows or after-hours scene at the disco or casino - we are not late nighters.8. Watersports - Not good visibility for snorkelling. A bit windy some days for kayaks. It looked like these activities was sub-contracted by Sirenis to another company. Be careful - after a catamaran lesson, one guy asked me for $5/day insurance in case we returned the boats or equipment damaged. Sirenis needs to address this as it seems like an unscrupulous side business to me. 9. Beach vendors are very aggressive - if you have trouble saying no, do not go into their shops. We befriended a couple of them and quickly found out they have very little else to do for gainful employment in this area. We ended up giving them some Christmas gifts and the rest of them then left us alone. We recommend that if you want to give gifts to locals, you should bring hats, shoes, cheap watches. make-up and kids toys.Overall, we had a great vacation and would not hesitate to return. Sirenis Tropical was a great value for the money.

<Content>Amazing time at the Serenis! My partner and I travelled to the Domincan Republic on Nov 22nd for a fortnight.
