Flight was fine no problems made up some time in the air and arrived about 230pm in the afternoon. Having already been to the DR and Punta Canan I knew what to expect on arrival and it all ran smoothly and we were on our air conditioned transfer buses in no time. Yes the roads are very bumpy so be prepared and there are no rules on how to drive it seems and quite frequently they change sides of the road! I would not reccommend driving out there during your stay.Hotel- On arrival we were greeted with a refreshing cocktail and check in ran very smoothly and we set off to our room which was T101. We got everything we requested,a gorgeous sea view on the first floor. The rooms are very basic but very clean and served there purpose well. My only comment is that the A/C was very tempremental so didnt use it much and at this time of the year wasnt a problem. The food was amazing. We used the buffet alot but also tried a few of the Speciality restaurants. We went to the Mexican,Chinese,Steakhouse,Italian and the Medditeranean. Our favourites were the Italian and Mexican. Book well in advance for the steakhouse but its well worth a visit! Sample menus are available at Guest Services for you to look at.Drinks were in abundance too and some of the cocktails were lovely. My fav was the Strawberry Daquiri and my partner loved the Pina Colada and the local drink 'Coco Loco' The staff in this resort were so friendly and helpful and always greeted you whether it be in the restaurant or just walking on the sidewalk! They work so hard 24/7 and keep the resort immaculate. The entertainment staff were fantastic and we made it to quite a few of the shows and would recommend the Dirty Dancing,Grease,Domincan and the Stars shows. They put in so much effort throughout the day but won't hassle you to join if you dont want too. We spent most of our days by the pool which was fantastic and kept very clean. Our only comment was that in our second week they started doing repairs and tore down the bridge which resulted in a lot of noise and mess but I guess it had to be done at some time and didnt affect us much(we just moved further away)We did two trip both which I reccomend. We went by Catamaran to Saona Island which was amazing and the sea was gorgeous(will post pictures) We ate lunch there and sunbathed and then came back on a speedboat which was great fun!The other trip we did was to the Marinarium abnd we snorkelled and swam with the stingrays  nurse sharks which amazing.Overall we had a fantastic holiday and would not hesitate to return

<Author>playalover78
<Content>would go back tomorrow hola!Just got back from a week at the Sirenis Tropical Suites and had a great time. I would rate this hotel a 4 star overall, as was advertised with my tour operator.Grounds: the grounds of this hotel are beautiful. The walkway down the middle played music (which I loved because it reminded me of Canada's Wonderland for you all you Toronto area people). The layout of the resort makes it easy to get to everything.Pool: I'm not a pool person but this pool was gorgeous! It is the longest pool I've ever been to and many areas are over 7 ft. There are also a ton of shallow areas and 2 pool bars at opposite ends. You most definately have one drink finished before you can swim to the bar at the other end of the pool.Beach: AWESOME!!! the sand was golden soft brown and the water was warm and crystal blue. There is a lot of coral with tropical fish (even in close so everybody can snorkle if they wish). Bring a roll from the buffet and feed the fish...they love it and you get some great pictures. The pool and beach always had tons of available loungers.Food: Not too bad. I never went hungry. This is where the hotel would lose its fifth star rating. I am a picky eater and enjoyed every meal. Every buffet dinner had a carving of some kind (salmon wellinton, roasted chicken, turkey, etc), the pasta bar, and then regular buffet items. Lunch at the pool snack bar was the best...nachos and cheese and softserve icecream...:)Rooms: we had a great room. The best shower pressure EVER and an airconditioner that was so cold it put condensation on the windows. The mini bar was always stocked with pop and water. I would recommend brining your own pillow as the resorts is just cotton batton in a pillow case.Service: the service at the hotel was superb. My glass was never empty, wait time at the bars was minimal and never was there a dirty plate in front of me. The staff truly went out of their way to ensure our stay was enjoyable. Horseback Riding: I booked the horseback riding tour offered by the guys who sit near the towel exchange. It was advertised as $45 for 2 hours (5-7pm). I was the only person from the hotel who booked for that day and got a solo ride (which is fine by me). My horse was in great shape and my guide and I ran the entire beach, fantastic! I did however speak to another couple who went the day after me and their ride was not even close to 2 hours. The moral of the story is: the ride and horses are great, just have it in your mindset that you are paying $45 for a little over an hour on the horse, not 2. Well worth it for me as I did get 2 hours of riding in, but most people do not.Overall I would go back to this resort in a heartbeat.

<Author>plas
<Content>Wonderful Vacation My husband and I stayed at the Sirenis Aug.12-19, 2007. It is a huge property consisting of many 2 and 3 story buildings. The Tropical side, where we stayed, consisted of suites. Although the property is not new, our suite was cleaned daily and drinks in the frig were replenished daily. The ocean was fantastic-no rocks, seaweed, jelly fish or other unwanted things. The water was warm and quite calm. Not the best for boogie-boarding, but great for swimming. Every type of water craft was available. Beach palapas (straw umbrellas) had to be reserved early, as a general rule. The pool is gigantic, divided into several sections and that is where all the activities take place. The animation team is good and tries hard to get the guests involoved in many games.There are 9 restaurants on site, available by reservation on the same day you want to go, as well as 2 buffet restaurants, and a snack bar by the pool. The food is fine, not great, and we did not get sick from it. There is something for everyone, including vegetarian and kid's menu. We did not eat out of the property, as it is at least 35 minutes to the nearest small town and we chose not to do that. The property is quite isolated; it's not near any other hotels within walking distance, or even any shops. You have to take a taxi anywhere you want to go off the site.The property has beautiful gardens, trees and walkways. As it is very spread out, there is a tremendous amount of walking, the only drawback. It is not ideal for handicapped people, or those who do not like to walk, especially in the blazing sun (most days were 40 degrees including heat factor),The shows were so-so. We went to three and declined the rest. It is very hot in the theatre and the shows start at 10:00 p.m., by which time I was tired and wanted to sleep. e did not go to the disco, so I have no idea what it's like.There are many bars on site, including in the pool. We would sit in the gigantic lobby after supper and the waitresses would serve you whatever you wanted. They have many exotic drinks which we sampled, including the usual beverages you find in these type of resorts.As we have been to Punta Cana before and did side trips then, we did not do any trips this time. There are many things to visit, but some of the trips are quite costly (i.e.$100 plus US/ person).As we went during the rainy season, we were quite lucky to have only one day of rain, the tail end of Hurricane Dean. It did rain like the end of the world on our second to last day and was very windy. But when you go to the trop8ics in the summer, you takle your chances, hoping to be lucky.All in all, a very enjoyable vacation.

<Content>La Sirenis is an Excellent Value We stayed at La Sirenis July 24-27. Two adults, two children (11, 10). Check-in went very smoothly except we forgot to ask and pay ($2 per day) for our safe key while we were there, so had to make a trip back to the front desk. Staff was very gracious.Best part of this resort is definitely the beach. Water is warm, we swam a lot. Spent our afternoons under the palm trees on the beach. Beach area is kept clean by staff. The grounds are well maintained. We did not have any problems with bugs.We had a two room suite in the T building near the beach. Good location although it is a bit of a hike back to the main buffet and entertainment venue. Our children loved having their own TV at night to watch sports and the Disney channel. Mini bar was well stocked and we left a note for the maid to leave extra water which was no problem. Had towel creations every day and our room was clean and well maintained.Food at the buffet was good to excellent. We enjoyed the pasta bar. Desserts are not great. Enjoyed the variety of juices, drinks were plentiful and service was good.Brought dollars for tips but didn't see that they made a big difference. Staff was always very accomodating even without a tip; however we wanted to support the locals who work there.Pool was clean, wished the pool and bars stayed open a little later. I think 6:00 pm in the summer is too early. Again, beach is gorgeous with plenty of chairs and shade. We never went out early to reserve a space and it wasn't a problem. Snorkeling is not great but we enjoyed the catamaran.International crowd of visitors. If you are from the US seeking an American style vacation, you might be disappointed. Staff probably spoke more English than the other guests. We enjoyed the many nationalities who visited--British, French, German, etc. There was a small group of rowdy drunks at the pool bar several times, but not too much of a distraction. Michael Jackson show was a hoot!We paid approximately $150 US per night for the hotel and thought it an excellent value for the quality that we received. It is not a five star property but it is a solid resort with many good features. I wouldn't hesitate to stay again or recommend it to others.

<Author>beachbaby087
<Content>Paradise!! My boyfriend and I stayed at the Sirenis Tropical in Punta Cana for our summer vacation and it was unbelievably gorgeous! The grounds are very well maintained, gardeners are always out keeping the grounds in immaculate shape and are more than happy to climb a tree for you for a coconut. Pool was gorgeous, very very big and was at just that perfect temperature. If you want to get a chair around the pool that is in the shade you must go early though, they fill up quickly. Buffets were great...food tasted very good. The beach was beautiful, however the most central area to swim in the ocean had a bit of seaweed floating around but if you walk about 2 minutes down it clears up. The staff at this resort are probably the most friendly people you'll ever meet!! We made very good friends with Phillipe and Fedor (bartenders) at La Pergola bar...they made our stay about 20 times more fun as they were sooo hilarious and kind. The drinks were amazing, especially one called a Marco Polo and the bartenders are definitely not cheap on the amount of liqor....you're glass will be about 3/4 liqor and a splash of juice or pop unless you tell them otherwise. We did get a helpful piece of advice about the drinks from our travel guide....any drink that has creme de coco i believe it was called such as the Coco Loco drink are best to stay away from as the creme de coco is considered a laxative there!! The only thing I would have to say that I didnt like about this resort was that the front desk never seemed to have any small american bills which was quite a problem as most of our bills were 20s and we wanted some smaller bills to tip the bartenders and other friendly staff so make sure to change your money earlier. Besides that though this was an amazing resort, we would go back in a second so dont listen to any of the bad reveiws.

<Author>Isleofwighttraveller
<Content>Don't believe the negative reviews We returned on the 13th March after two fabulous weeks at this hotel. Before we left I had read some of the reviews on this site about our hotel and I must admit they worried me, but having been I do wonder if they were writing about the same hotel! It was clean spacious and the food was excellent, both the quality and the choice. Each meal had something for everyone in our opinion, you could even has bacon, sausage and eggs if you wanted, but I recommend the omelettes cooked as you wait with whatever fillings you like. Lunch was taken at the pool restaurant and we had salad most days, although there was a hot meat too with chips etc. Evenings there was everything you could wish for including a roast every night. The rooms were spacious with a lounge area, bedroom with 2 queen size beds and full bathroom, although we couldn't get the plug to work in the bath! Large balcony where we sat most evenings before dinner watching the sun go down. There was plenty of choice of pools with ample sun beds, but we spent every day on the beach, which went on for miles, probably the only criticism of this hotel is that there were not enough sun umbrellas, but I do think this is the case at a lot of hotels. The staff could not do enough for you even though all meals were buffet style the waiters/waitresses were on hand with the water, wine and whatever else you wanted at every meal. There are 7 speciality restaurants, that you do need to book for, only the gourmet restaurant is subject to a further charge. We tried the steakhouse, chinese and italian (twice) and they were all excellent. The grounds are very well tended and beautiful, they are quite large and we spent many an evening strolling round (if only to walk off all the pounds we had put on with the excellent food) This is a fantastic hotel and we would recommend it to everyone and we will definitely go back in the future.

This poses a problem as there is twice as many people but not twice as many facilities. We then had to stand in line, in the lobby, while one desk attendent booked the large bus load of people in. We finally arrived at our room to find we had no electricity. Fumbling in the pitch dark we called the lobby and they sent an electrician over. Half hour later, the lights went on just to discover the patio door lock was not working. Leaving was no less arduous. We had to leave the hotel for the airport at 11:30pm. However, they made us check out of our room by 12 noon. <Author>sirtravelalots
<Content>more than adequate We arrived at the Sirenis Tropical on February 5th for 1 week stay. We opted to take a taxi (50$us) as we didn't want to take a tour dropping off other travellers and wanted to start our vacation ASAP... We also have 2 kids (7 and 4) and didn't want them to have to travel for too long. Yes the road is bumpy but you can deal with it for 45 minutes... When we arrived to check in all went smoothly... No, you don't need to ask for the remote when you check in! They laughed at us when we did! As a reader of other critiques of this hotel I was expecting the worst! While checking in we did overhear 3 (!) other guests in the process or having just switched rooms for various reasons... On French tourist was having a sit-in because the countertop in her bathroom had fallen on her foot and she was furious... The only complaint I can make about the check-in is that I usually handle check-in while my husband chases the kids... well i started the process but el-macho employee insisted on deferring to my husband! Also, it became confusing because more than 1 employee handles the check-in so you don't really know who to turn to... Having said that -- these are minor complaints.. Check in lasted all but 15 minutes... The Sirenis is a very large complex... (Do yourself a favor and bring a carriage for any toddlers!) Our Junior Suite was clean and efficient... Yes the toilet leaked (evidently a common problem there!) but nothing a towel on the floor couldn't solve... Other than that everything worked, the shower was strong and there was always hot water... The maid service was efficient.. Clean towels everyday... Floors swept and mopped... We waited three days before giving our maid a tip for the week... So we can't say that the tip was a factor. When we arrived the mini-fridge was not working right away -- something to do with the electricity having been off in the room for too long...we really needed it though due to antibiotics needing to be chilled... overnight it was up and running! The AC worked splendidly... Two units one in the bedroom and one in the living area.. The Satellite TV worked well.. Disney and Boomerang for kids... CNN et al for adults. Our building was the farthest away from all, closest to the beach. There are paths that lead to the main activities areas and covered pathways for long walks back to the reception main area. The pool (s) were very nice.. accessible for all ages... Cleaned every morning... Didn't see many filters for that size a pool but... The smim-up bars had everything.... Obviously tipping helps you get faster service... even a smile... The food was excellent.. Much better than: Crown Paradise Club, Puerto Vallarta + Villa del PalMar, PV unfortunately not very kid friendly! Hamburgers and hotdogs at lunch and for snack but not at supper (def no chicken strips...) Having said that there was a pasta bar nightly, as well as french fries on a daily basis.. Long line ups because there are not enough employees stationing the egg and pasta bars. But hey, you are on vacation... The staff in the restaurants were always friendly and understanding towards parents and kids... The desserts were great and the breads --- oh the breads were lovely! We did not try any of the restaurants and it is true that supper is not served until 7:00pm... But it is buffet so you can get a plate of food within 5 minutes. We did not catch any shows (too late) but those of you with kids just know that you will be just as exhausted after a day by the pool and beach to crash by 8:30pm!! The beach was stupendous!!!! Gorgeous, clean, soft sand! Turquoise water! Bring your own beach stuff however (they do not have any boogie boards and limited pails and shovels!) There was ALWAYS lounge chairs whether at the beach or by the pool.. There was ALWAYS beach towels except maby if you were showing up at 4:00pm since they do not take out any new ones (hut closes at 5:00pm) We don't know if we were lucky with the week that we chose but this is what we saw: constant gardening, grounds maintenance, major painting (sanding and varnishing of suite door frames for goodness sakes!), new chairs and tables for the verandas (replacing plastic ones), coconut picking.... you get the idea! Whatever happened back in the fall regarding the grounds, it is obvious that they just planted new grass ,new trees, new hibiscus, you name it! If I were to complain about anything -- it would not be against the hotel per say...( I am torn between rating it 3.5 or 4 stars... ) I do have to say that although they claim to cater to families with kids, the kids center was way way too far away!!! My complaint would be against bad tourist manners.. People butting into the buffet line because they just want salad (unfortunately the whole line starts there!) The pool could remain cleaner if: we ALL picked up our glasses from the edge of the pool and put them in the garbage or up somewhere else instead of allowing them to be kicked over and spilled into the pool water (hmmm, not very appealing sludge on top of the water surface by the end of the day...). Also, there is a product available internationally called swimmies.. These are diapers for the water! There were quite a few families that would keep their kids in diapers UNTIL getting into the pool and then removing them for the kids' swim... not cool... And my favourite anectode of the whole trip... There is a photographer that walks the grounds with various pets for picture taking.. Most popular is the little monkey... Well one tourist (will not mention nationality!!!!!) took the monkey in her hands for the picture... Well the monkey decided to, shall we say, make his monkey business at that exact moment.. So what does she do????? She dumps it in the shallow pool (yes, where all the kids are frollicking and the adults are taning) and then washes her hands! She then returned to her lounge chair to continue to lovely sun tanning! Needless to say, we were all mortified!!! How can you blame a hotel for uncleanliness when you have tourists who think that because they sat on a plane for 20 hours that they have the right to do whatever they want? If it wasn't for this limited number of incidents then we would have nothing to complain about! We like to travel to different destinations so I do not know whether we would return to this hotel per se... But all in all it was a very enjoyable week! We definetely got what we paid for in a positive way... We also got to relax, whereas at the Crown Paradis in PV there is no place for parents to sit (never mind lie down) around the Disney themed kiddie pool...

I drank baileys coffee.Now for those of you not quite getting the picture, it's ok but by far not somehwere you will remember. Luckily, the beach is nice and the sun shinning. <Author>chalicec
<Content>It's not as bad as the reviews, I actually liked it :) Having read some rather contradictory reviews about this resort, I almost cancelled it before my travel and having stayed there for two weeks with my boyfriend I feel compellted to give my review.Firstly, I would consider myself well travelled and I have fairly high standards of living myself. I have stayed all over the world in a variety of accommodation that rates from 5 Star Duluxe to 1 Star so I consider myself able to gauge a good 4 / 5 star hotel.My overall verdict on this hotel is that it is competitively priced and as always, you get what you pay for. I didnt pay as much to stay here as I have paid to stay in other 4/5 star resorts in the Dominican and therefore I have to say that I feel this resort offers good value for money. This resort is vast and therefore it is really buzzy and it is full of atmospher. So again I feel that what it lacks in luxury (as you will see within my review is one of my disappointments) it gains in atmospher.If you are on a budget and you want 4 / 5 star facilities such as a a spa, tennis courts and several restaurants, small casino, you are going in a group of families, or have a family that you need to keep entertained this place would be great because it is large enough and impersonal enough for you to kind of get lost in it and do your own thing . But, if you are going for a couples holiday where you want a bit of peace and quiet and a touch of luxury, well above average food and want to stay in a cosmopolitan resort frequented by a variety of nationalities, not just English, don't go here, unless as I have said you are on a budget and just want a break in the Carribean.So what's good and what's bad and should you go there?What is particularly good about this resort is that there is a lot to do, it's spread out, the beach is absolutely lovely and it's right on the beach!!! the casino is small but there is one, the night entertainment is limited but the team that put on the shows do so spectacularly, there is a disco again it is small but there is a disco, there is a gym which is sufficient, there is a golf and shooting area (which is tiny) but it is there, there is a good games room and they have a good daily entertainement programme so the place is a buzz and there is always something to do. The water sports on the beach are extensive and run most days. The excursions and trips are well organised. There are several restaurants (all of which I found very very average and stuck to the buffet after being disappointed by 4 and having heard similar stories about the remainder) and tired of cueing to book the restaurants, the drinks are good, I didnt get ill on the food once, there was always ample choice in the buffet, breakfast is great and the staff are really really friendly and nice and all speak English. As there are so many people there it is easy to meet people, it is relaxed with no dress code and absolutely no pretentiousness. I found the crowd mostly English with a handful of Europeans and Canadian.The rooms were very very clean and towels were changed daily and the pools and resort were super clean.So what didnt I like about it?The rooms are very very tired. We stayed in the Tropical Suites which I gather are newer and bigger but it was a very small suite and there was not a touch of 4 / 5 star luxury. It was very clean but tired and I would struggle to give the rooms 3 stars.The lounge area which is just off the reception area is huge and harshly lit and in the evening this is the only area for relaxation.Had I have been there with my family I probably would have loved it but it was busy, loud and there were insufficient seats for the number of people (although I was there over Christmas and New Year when apparently it is busiest) still I found the lack of variety a bit bland.The local and champagne is really horrible and otherwise expensive, so pack some of your own or pay incredibly over priced local rates for imported wines.There are not enough sun loungers to accommodate the number of guests and we often had to lay on the beach on a towel or go out at FIVE AM to bag a bed, which I would not expect at a 4 star resort.This resort operates a system whereby you have to book the speciality (non buffet) restaurants one at a time and only oneper day. This meant that at any one time there were often cues of upto 25 people trying to book a table for a restaurant which often took upto 45 mins to make a booking and in my opinion not the kind of set up you would expect in a 4 / 5 star resort and not something I enjoyed doing on the 4 days that I decided to book. Despite all of the above, if I wanted to go on a cheap Carribean break again and didnt have the money to stay at Secrets, Sunscape the Beach, The Grand Ventanta I would go back here because overall it is above average. However this time around I would know what to expect and as a result my expecations of the luxury associated with a good 4 star (like the Gran Ventana which I have stayed at and Secrets) would not be so high.If you would like to ask me a specific question feel free.Meanwhile if you have booked, no matter what you like or dislike, the beach, the fresh air, the sun and sea is consistant and I can guarantee, this much you will love :).

<Content>An excellent value hotel I feel compelled to write something on this site after my stay due to having read some very mixed reviews about this hotel.The hotel probably isn't 5 star by our standards (more like a 3.5 *) but if it had been I'm sure I would have paid at least twice the amount. There's a club on site but you do have to pay for drinks in there.Here are a few tips for you if you're thinking of going:- take plenty of mosquito repellant - take plenty of suncream toiletries etc - there is an on site shop but is very expensive (it cost us 拢7 for indigestion tablets).- tip staff where possible as this is a very poor country- take care when using the cash machine - there is a scam going on where you put your card in and it seems to disappear then a guy appears and point to a stuck on sign telling you, you need to key in your card number 3 times.- take care if going on quad bikes - 2 people came off on our trip and also children will try and run along side you and for money (very dangerous) - don't give children money as you will be swarmed by them and the Domincan people ask you not to as it encourages their children to become beggars- take the trip to Saona beach, safari tour and acquatic tour Finally, if you go here expecting to be able to roam around with a promenade and large shopping centre in walking distance - you will be disappointed. <Author>dogmahone
<Content>great holiday We have just returned from a really good two week stay from 16th to 30th August. We were a party of six, including two over-70s and two younger teens and we all loved it. I have read mixed reviews on this hotel but I think our rep's advice was sound - remember that you are in the Caribbean and everything happens at a much slower pace than we are used to. So 5 minutes 'Dominican time' is not literally 5 minutes. Accept this before you start and you will have few problems.The Sirenis is very well designed and the grounds are beautifully maintained. Employees are constantly washing down the walkways and even clearing small twigs from the grass. There are beautiful flowers and our children loved the flamingoes and geckos.Something we really appreciated was that the hotel, the grounds and swimming pool are so large that you never had the feeling of being in a crowd and never had to queue, either in the buffet restaurants, bars or pool bars. There were plenty of sunloungers but to guarantee one in the shade you needed to get up early and reserve them with towels!!There are lots of palm trees on the beach that offer some shade though.The food was good - we preferred the buffet overall because the quality and variety was excellent. The speciality restaurants are not as good but we used the Mexican, Steakhouse and Seafood just for a change of scenery really. The buffet food is freshly prepared and replenished frequently.One of the things which we loved was the genuine friendliness and helpfulness of the staff everywhere - at the bars, the restaurants and around the hotel generally. We were served promptly, with a smile, and never had the feeling that we were passed over for regular drinkers or good tippers. The waiting staff in the buffet were fantastic.Our one criticism of the Sirenis is the shabbiness of the rooms. We had booked two junior suites for the six of us and in both we experienced faulty light bulbs, which broke again soon after fixing and, more seriously, water coming through the bathroom ceilings and flooding the floor (in both bathrooms and on our final evening our ceiling appeared to be about to collapse under the torrent of water!) This was attended to promptly but repairs were patchy to say the least. However, the rooms were cheery and spacious and we weren't in them much. We did go prepared with many one-dollar bills for tipping and we did tip regularly, but we all had the feeling that this was not a factor to the service. For instance, we never tipped at any of the bars and always had good service.I highly recommend a 20 minute walk along the beach in either direction - absolutely beautiful and even though it was high season there was hardly anyone else around.We did a few activities - the Outback Safari is extremely well organised, with a strong focus on safety, and really interesting and fun. The Bavaro Splash trip was ok but crowded. We twice went out on the quad bikes hired from the beach and this was one of the highlights of our holiday as we got to see so much.This was a really successful holiday and I would recommend this hotel for those wanting a very relaxing holiday.

My companions were happy to return to the buffet which offered superb choice and convenience.Pool area is lovely but the beach is the best! I read previous reviews which influenced my view of the swim-up bars and the use of the bathrooms so I spent very little time in that vicinity... not a problem for the hotel but certainly raises questions about the habits and standards of the guests! We didn't really bother with the activities, the shows were good especially those which were non-dance.I would highly recommend this complex as excellent value for money and a relaxing Caribbean experience, to be repeated as often as your budget allows. Just be aware that this is the rainy season and the humidity levels are very high.

<Content>Nice Vacation - June 24 to Jul 1 - Toronto Canada Just got back from a 1 week vacation with my wife and 15 yr old son. We had a very good vacation. I think that the negative comments are from people that are overly picky and not willing to work with people.  The bus trip is an hour long with 1 stop at Sunscape the beach. It is on rural roads with a lot of bumps and turns. Not really that bad. You can see the new highway being built and I am sure it will cut 20 min off the trip in the future. It will also open the area for a lot more hotels. I find that if you attempt to use even a little bit of spanish with the staff, it goes an incredably long way . They warm right up and become very friendly and attntive to your needs. We always received good service this way and often would slip them a dollar at the end of the meal or when leaving the bar. I never found that they were looking for tips, but they sure appreciated them. The next time they saw us they would fall all over us. Often I did not tip as I was by the pool with out any money. It did not matter , and I always got good service. The food was great at the main buffet for breakfast and dinner. Lots of variety and always hot and or clod as required. We ate lunch always by a restaurant by the pool. Also great variety for salads and pizza. We ate at the Mexican, Steak House and Italian. All great meals and woth the wait to line up 3 times for reservations. I wish they would let you book more than one reservation at a time so you did not have to go back. We did the reservations right at 8:00am while my son was sleeping in. Usually a 15 to 20 minute ordeal. The property is kept very clean and manicured. The pool is very deep and about the same temperature as the ocean. We never used the towls at all as it was always warm ( 32 C) and we dried off all the time. We had no problem to set up loungers in the shade at the beach as long as you were there by 9:00am. The beach is great for swimming and snorkelling. The clean it up( sea weed, cups, debris etc) every morning by 7:00am. The roped in swimming area is very large and gets about 5 ft deep about 100 ft out from shore. There is an old reef about 50 ft beyond the swimming area . It was great for snorkelling. We took buns and bananas out to feed the fish. There were hundreds of fish all around us and a lot of variety. We had geen flag 5 days and yellow for the last 2 days. The clientele was approx 60% British, 25% French , 5% German and the rest was Canadian and Dominicans. There was a lot of topless bathing at the beach and even around the pool area. We went to 2 shows ( Michael Jackson and Grease) they start at 10:00pm. They were fine to see and the kids did a pretty good job of dancing and lip-sincing. The animation staff did a good job at the beach with dance lessons, spanish lessons, volleyball, aerobics etc. We used the Sports bar out in front of the main receptio area a number of times. We shot pool, playe ping pong and played fooseball. We only window shopped at the stores on the hotel property as we were not interested in souveniers. My wife waled along the beach about 20 minutes to Sunscape the beach. She felt safe , as there were always a number of guests walking along the route. I walked as far each way on the beach to where the vendors have there stalls set up. They come down to the water to try and get you to come up and look at there merchandise. A firm no is all it takes and they back off. I would go back again as it was very good value for the $$ we spent. I would rate it a a four star . It was not as lush and glitzy as a five star. They also had no shrimp or lobster at the meals , like a five star usually has. That is OK for us , as my wife and son do not eat much seafood anyways.

<Author>Fireworks2015
<Content>Great experience, to be repeated as soon as possible To start with the overall conclusion, our stay was excellent and surpassed all of our great expectations. We had a wonderful week of holidays early in June and reading many of the criticisms, we can only infer that staying there during low season avoids many of problems that may exists at other times. Still, we are more than amused reading about problems with being understood and about politeness. We cannot conceive that the skills and the attitude of the staff changes with the season. Therefore the view on politeness and language skills must depend strongly on your origin. And from a German view at least, there was no reason for complaints whatsoever.Having read that it would be hard to be understood by the staff, we had our Spanish language guides with us and were stopped much too often by German replies when our (nondisptutable) accent was recognised. We would have never ventured to expect such an open attitude of the hotel staff to foreign languages (also French, English) in the Dominican Republic, especially as hardly any North American hotel would have to idea to serve their customers other than in the staff's mother tongue.We read in French and German guide books that the people in the Dominican Republic are among of the most kind persons that you can imagine. And we noticed that this statement applies to the hotel staff. We gave tips only for the key services and saw that people were happy to receive, but the quality of services did not really depend on them. We noticed that any effort in having an open level of communication (including some Spanisch words) was answered by friendly smiles.An important help is indeed to book a safe (for 2$/night), as the windows do not close too safely. This reduces any risk of loss and gives a better feeling. The staff is searched when leaving the grounds, so there are no doubts about their correctness. For water sports, it is very helpful to use the general damage insurance (20$/week). Apart from this contribution, the unmotored water sports are free of charge. If in doubt, please contact the head of the water sports group (the captain) who is very helpful. And my personal favorite: test the tennis lessons (to be paid): their value is outstanding!If we began to describe the attraction of the food, we were risk not to stop the description.Sure it was rather Mediterranean style than American, but it was hard to miss a meal because the variation of each day was so exciting. Recommendation: Try the fruit (passion fruit, mango, melon, ...), vegetable salads and above all the rice dishes!The hotel is very much suited for a relaxed holiday, especially if you are a family with children. For us, it is sure we shall return as soon as possible!

<Author>Sally9
<Content>14 Nights in the open prison On the outset the hotel is lovely, immactulately kept, impressive lobby and good standard of rooms (if not a bit tired looking) and a mini bar which was stocked every day, but thats about all that is good about this hotel. I have never had such poor service from a hotel, the staff, particularly the bar staff are rude and arrogant. It takes forever to get served and when you do, don't expect a 'hola', expect a 'what' they will then proceed to literally throw the drink at you, basically they are after tips, if you don't tip, then they don't want to know, they will then refuse to serve you again. Tips apparently are included in the price of the hotel,. but don't be fooled, they are hungry for the tips, but don't want to work for it. You are not treated like a guest and not made to feel like you are on holiday. There is absolutely no atmosphere in the hotel and the animation team do very little to encourage you. All you see after dinner in the bar area near the lobby are a lot of desperately bored people who tend to go to bed early as there is nothing to do. Leaving the complex isn't advisable, when you do the first thing you hit is a brothel then a 'plaza' of shops which are a complete an utter rip off. My advice is don't walk there alone, take a taxi and make him wait for you while you shop and also take your jewellery off. There is a sign saying do not walk beyond the shopping plaza also, take this advice. Other than that there is absolutely nothing else around, the hotel is in the middle of nowhere. Inside the open prison, there are about 7 speciality restaurants, which I can say are very good, the food is to a good standard, you do have to queue each day to book these, which really bugged some people but we were lucky and managed to get in most times. The pool area is also excellent and kept very clean, but get up about 7am and put your towels out as beds will be taken. I have never been on holiday before and wanted to go home, but I did here. Whenever someone was going home guests were all jealous as they were desperate to go home. Unfortuantely we had bad weather the second week and there was literally nothing to do, no entertainment etc. Overall complaints were being put in by people about the hotel, facilities and rude staff, but the management did not seem to care. This hotel is in no way a 5 star hotel, it looks like one, but there is not care or attention to deal or anyone going out of their way to ensure you had a fantastic holiday. If you are venturing to this hotel, I can only hope that complaint forms and formal letters of complaint when returning to the UK do some good and guests have a much better time. families of the staff were also invited to stay at the hotel during our stay and caused complete chaos, apparently this is a common thing at weekends. They basically get preferential treatment over everyone staying and take the pool area etc over. Its also worth knowing a bit of Spanish to stay at this hotel as a lot of the day restaurant staff don't speak English, its also really useful in shops too as they will literally try and rob you blind on ridiculous prices for gifts and doing it in Spanish seemed to be appreciated. All in all I was disappointed with my stay, we, like so many others paid a lot of money to go to this hotel and I feel cheated and annoyed at paying so much. 7 nights would have been bearable but we were there for 14 nights and it really started to get to us after a while. I hope other guests have a better time than we did.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Had a great time! A trip to remember! My boyfriend and I just returned from the Dominican Republic early this morning. We stayed for one week (April 6 - 13) at the Sirenis Tropical Suites and had a great time, despite the horribly cramped plane ride from Vancouver to the Domincan, and then the bumpy and long ride to the hotel. Nevertheless, once we arrived at Sirenis we were greeted with a refreshingly delicious drink and the staff had all of our information and room keys prepared for us. Although we had asked for a room on the top floor, they gave us a ground level suite which didn't really matter in the end - stumbling up stairs when your sloshed isn't exactly safe after all!Here is what you need to know before travelling to Sirenis/the Dominican:- The Sirenis Tropical/Cocotal is located on the same site. A majority of the time the Tropical front desk is empty (located on the left once you enter) while the Cocotal front desk (located on the right) is packed full of people. If you are staying at the Tropical Suites, make sure you go to the correct front counter otherwise you'll wait in line for no reason just to be told to ring the service bell at the Tropical front counter.- The only difference b/w Tropical/Cocotal is that in the Tropical Suites, your bedroom is seperate from the 'lounge' room, which has a small table, couch and a mini fridge. We didn't really find much use for this area, however if you like your space then this will work well for you. (Also, rooms are cleaned daily and fresh towels are provided on a regular basis.)- Bring LOTS of bug spray!!! I cannot stress this enough!!! We saw some nasty bites on some people and got quite a few ourselves - remember, you're in a tropical climate meaning a lot of mosquitos. Be prepared!- Make sure you pack all of the essentials (ie: shampoo, tooth paste, deoderant, etc.). The prices of these items are extremely over-priced.- Food was ok. After awhile, you get sick of eating at the buffets. We went to the Mexican and Steakhouse a-la-carte. The Mexican was really good, but seriously, don't even bother with the Steakhouse unless you like eating steaks at Denny's and prefer fat rather than meat on your ribs (how utterly disgusting!)- Both the beach and pools are stunning! My boyfriend and I had no problem finding places to sit. Of course all of the shaded areas are taken up quickly - when it's sunny, it gets damn hot! Early birds get the shady spots, so don't complain if you wake up at 10:30am and there are no more shaded areas!- The staff are incredibly friendly and humble. Even when they don't understand what you're saying or they can't speak proper english, they really appreciate when you try to speak spanish (eventhough its probably the worse spanish they've ever heard). They all try very hard to accomodate your needs. At the bar in the main lounge, we always kept our eyes out for Juan Carlos - he's the best! You could talk with him forever! - Don't be afraid to barter everywhere you go! You'll hear a lot of I'm cheapy cheapy or I give you low price. Everyone jacks their prices up to fool tourists into overpaying. Don't be a fool - start very low and work up. Walk away if they pressure too much.- The excursiouns are great! We definatly recommend Saona Island, Caribbean Festival and the SpeedBoats.Overall, we had an amazing time! We met so many people from all over and made a lot of friends. Only complaint about Sirenis is the nightlife. If you're a night owl like we are, the Bavaro area is the place to be, so stay somewhere there. If you wanna relax and have quiet time, go to Sirenis - the hotel is very secluded. Remember, the Dominican Republic is a 3rd world country. If you're expecting high class, you will be disappointed. Go to the Dominican with an open mind and you'll have a great time! We did and we had a blast! Sorry for the long review, but hopefully it helps paint the picture! Cheers!

flowers and towels in the shape of swans.We left them a tip each day as well as different lipsticks nailpolshes creams etc. They really liked getting little gifts each day.We only had 1 rainy/drizzly day and we spent the day walking on both sides of the resort buying little souvenirs at the beach huts.Most of the vendors were friendly a few were too pushy but most were alright and we soon caught on to the haggling done here.You usually pay a quarter of what they are asking and I did manage to get some genuine larimar for a fair price.Breakfast for me personally was the best meal and the omelettes were great~!!I only went to 1 a la carte- the steakhouse and it was not great but the buffets had a great selection at each meal and the pork that was carved right in front of you at diiner was fantastic.The dancers were super at the evening shows although the props were bad because we have to realize this is a third world country and they make the most of what they have.The staff work very hard and very long hours because the dancers teach dance lessons during the day or work various activities around the pool during the day and yet they can still smile while dancing on stage at 10 in the night.The people of the DR are the friendliest people I have ever met always smiling with hola to everyone they see.We had a lovely room in building L halfway between the beach and the lobby and the buffet restaurant.The Banana- mamas were great but not very potent the way I like them.They kept the bacardi and baileys under the bar but they would gladly give it to you if you asked.Just make sure you bring enough cash because I wanted to buy a gold larimar ring at the jewellery store but Ineeded extra cash.There was 1 interac machine in front of the complex down by the shops and it was out of order for our last three days there so I didnt get the ring.I thought there would be more than 1 interac machine especially with a casino. but no way and the bank was open at different times each day.But those were minor inconveniences compared to the beautiful beach pool immaculately manicured grounds and beautiful people.I too have travelled and found this resort to be PARADISE Dont listen to the negative reviews!! <Content>Don't believe the harsh reviews! I just got back from the Sirenis Tropical and I have to say, before leaving I was tempted to change resorts because of the recently placed terrible reviews. I can honestly say there was never a dull moment.The only reason I am not giving this resort an Excellent mark is because of the front desk service. This is one area that the hotel needs to work on. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>First time at all inclusive - honest observation This is the first ever all inclusive hotel and caribbean hotel I've been to. First of all, though it states that this hotel is above 4 stars and they self proclaim 5 it definitely is not. By my standards (Canadian) it's is probably a 3 or 3+ at most. Think of living quarters to be like Radissons or 2 or 3 storey motels. After talking to various other guests I've gotten a few mixed reviews but here are my observations.Rooms:I got a great room. On the second floor in the K unit overlooking the beach with a balcony. I think I got this room because the day I arrived I emailed them to say it was my first time doing an all inclusive and travelling by myself and would like to have a second floor (away from ground bugs) and close to the beach. I got them both and I was quite happy. Rooms were clean with tiles but will always feel dirty as the air is usually humid so it will feel somewhat moist and sandy...so it's advised to wear a sock or indoor slippers at all times. Ammenities were adquate, large closet room, was room was clean. I think the drain in my tub was bad as water did not go down fast so everytime I showered it would pile up. Beds are a little stiff and I did tip the maid at the start, 5 bucks and she made sure I got my extra towels and water in the fridge. Bring a scented candle as the place smells musty. I had a few ants in my room so I had to rid the with my bug spray.Food:Buffet was adequate. Reminded me a of cruise buffet food...kinda like cafeteria food. I appreciate their effort to mix the food up and try to to make it seem so repetitive. Food is a little bland and if you're adventureous and not picky I think the food is adquate. Omlettes were great..but had a long line up. They tried to make every night a different theme so they did try to mix things up. Remember to bring your own bottle water for the meals as they will serve you tap water. The restaurants were good. Nothing spectacular and had enough variety if you wanted it. Not every one of them are opened everyday...each day only a few of the restaurants would be open. Some people I talked to liked the food and some don't. To each is own. Remember to wear no beach wear to dinner to the buffet or restaurant.Beach/pool:The beach was nice and clean. You had to wake up at 6am at least to reserve ur own beach chair or lounger. Place ur own room towel on a chair and put something personal to mark it. Then put a chair on top of the lounger to mark it. Though the hotel forbids this everyone does it and have not been enforced. There are not enough chairs and shady spots to go around so you are forced get up early and find a chair and an ideal spot. It sucks to have to wake up early every day just to reserve. Can never really sleep in. Beach was nice with clear water. Women liberally take their tops off. At the pool they were clean but only one pool bar which was kinda small...sits like 6 ppl or so, so you had to find an opportune time to go up and grab a drink. They held a few activities on the beach in the morning with loud speakers....sounds like those sale announcements at flea markets...which at times when ur resting and maybe sleeping..ur startled and can be a nuisance if you want peace and quiet.Activities:The hotel keeps a schedule of activities hour by hour. Some of the ammenities like tennis courts, spa and gym are quite off the premise (far from the pool and living quarters) and they are not open all the time so you have to make reservations. Like tennis is only open from 8-12 and 4-8. The shows are like high school quality productions with low budget props and performances. These shows are always before the disco opens so you're kinda left to watch these shows before you want to disco. There are no off the premise activities like pub crawls or go to town excursions as part of their routine activities. These have to be offered by your vacation provider...and most times these are not available. My rep was rarely seen and only operated at selective hours. Make sure you go to opening briefings as they do give you valuable information. Your vacation provide does offer excursions outside of the hotel. I went to Saona beach...definitely worth going to. It's a paradise beach like something you only see on tv. A littel pricey but the experience is worth it.Hotel/staff:The hotel I believe got such a high rating because of the casino. The hotel is nice but not nice enough for a 4 or 5 star. As you enter the resort premise you will see Sunscape and that resort seems much grand than this resort. Knowing spanish is definitely an asset but not a requirement. The staff will know enough to get you by. If you know french it is a benefit. I found most of the guests were from Quebec so at times seems like you're in somewhere that is colonized by French people. Remember to get your safe key the next morning. The staff is friendly and are always smiling. Almost all staff will say Hola to you as you walk by them or if they come by you. I find a smile can get you a long way. Overall hotel experience is that I would say fair. The hotel is located quite far from the airport going through poor townships and roads that seem to be unclaimed with tonnes of potholes and speedbumps. It's such a laid back atmosphere and seems like a complex of many radisson motels nestled in a garden with fountains, flamingos and little fishes. The resort is a family resort also popular for couples. Not a place for singles to go to.Overall the weather was amazing. The sun is fierce but the breeze is great. I went alone so I felt quite lonely there even with so many people there. Mainly I did not speak French and the people are quite cliquish. As a single traveller, I think a destination that allows you to wander and observe (close to the city or town) would have been beneficial. Shopping is non existent. The neighbouring shops along the beach are a nuisance. There are quite a water activities to join and participate which can keep you busy. I found the quality of food, room, ammenities and living quarters do no warrant a 4 or 5 star so don't be fooled by it. The hotel tried and I think did a good job of making their guests happy. I don't think I would come back as I do know, have seen and want to try a higher quality resort. If you're looking for a budget resort and the price of this resort is comparable...do consider it. If the price is comparable to other 5 stars...don't bother.

<Content>Wouldn't go back! If you've never travled before to a tropical resort, you may be fine staying here. However, if you have traveled and are acustomed to 4+ or 5+ resorts, you will be very disappointed with this one, as it is maybe a 3-star (at best)!We had no incidences at the airport or finding transportation to the hotel. The drivers and guides were pleasant and courteous. The woman guide on our way from the resort was very out-going and amuzed us during the trip to the airport. She spoke fluent English and Spanish.Upon our arrival we were ushered to the check-in counter. The man at the counter spoke very little English and didn't understand any questions we asked, as far as confirming our room type. He gave us a the key card and a packet which had a map on the back of it. He circled the building and told us H107 and pointed down the sidewalk. Now, keep in mind, it was dark and we were tired and we had to find our room, on our own - rather than the bellhop walking us to our room with our luggage. We managed to find the room and were disappointed immediately and went back to the front desk. We then had the same issue with being unable to communicate our problem that the room was not ocean front (although I believe they think ocean front means if the room faced East, regardless of how many building were between us and it, it was ocean front) nor was it non-smoking or a queen/king size bed. We were told to come back @ 9AM tomorrow by another man at the counter. We tried for 3 days to change rooms to no avail - honestly, they saw us coming and without even looking, told us nothing was available. We were also told nothing about the property, i.e., when the pool was open or closed, when the Restaurant opened, where to get beach towels, or about the security deposit box and how to rent one).The first night, being about 80+ degrees, we immediately realized the A/C was not working properly. We asked the maid the following day when she came to clean our room, how to work the A/C and she motioned that she could hear the fan and apparently that meant it was working. Thank goodness for the ceiling fan as that was the only way we survived in th room. We decided to let this go as it was bearable for the most part.As for the room - it was not clean, in fact, the same dead bug lying next to the entryway when we arrived was still there when we left. The air smelled of stale smoke and mildew as if it needed to be aired out and then the lack of A/C in the heat/humidity just made matters worse. The beds were like concrete slabs with cinder blocks for pillows. There were also many ants in the room - if we left a drink on the table inside or outside, it was over-run with ants within an hour, as well as walking around on the floors, chairs, etc. inside the room. On the up side, the maid was pleasant and friendly. She did make the bed with clean sheets each day, cleaned the bathroom and provided clean towels. It was just the depth of cleanliness which was lacking (bugs stuck in webs in the corners of the rooms, floors not cleaned, etc.).The beach, as advertised, was lengthy. However, once you passed the portion in front of the resort, you were approached by the locals to buy something from them which made it more annoying than it was worth -- you'd get by one and another one would approach. It was increasingly difficult to be polite, as we just wanted to walk and enjoy the sand, sun and ocean. I realize this isn't anything the resort can do something about, but it really took away from that selling point and one of the reasons why we choose the resort in the first place. It was also very unkept - the resort didn't rake the sand theentire week we were there ... there were cigarette butts all over and garbage. The resort also neglected the chairs and pads - many were brokenand the cushions (left out and blowing around) smelled of mildew and mold. We also found there were not enough huts to shelter people from the sun - which, if I'm not mistaken was specifically mentioned in the description of the resort. It was noted several places that reserving chairs was NOT allowed and therefore we did not do that the first morning after our arrival, as we have done at every other resort. That was our mistake, because by 7AM when we went to walk the beach and grab chairs - they were all gone. We then got up between 5:30AM - 6AM each day to reserve the chairs, find decent cushions (some appears to be newer than others) and a hut if possible -- otherwise, we wouldn't have anyplace to relax until late afternoon when the early risers were going back to their rooms.As for the staff itself, the waiters/waitresses just seemed to be untrained and were very limited. They had, what appeared to be waitresses, walking in the lobby where people gathered to drink/smoke prior to the restaurant opening. They carried trays and would wipe the tables where people had placed their drinks, as well as pick up empty glasses. However, these women were NOT waitresses, since they barely spoke English and certainly did not understand English. We had to go to the bar to get drinks if we wanted them. This also held true for the beach/pool. There weren't any waiters/waitresses walking around providing drinks. So, depending on where you were located, going to one of the two bars on the beach was a 3-5 minute stroll in each directions. The layout of the resort was poorly designed and too spread out.And lastly, the food. It was mediocure at best. We did only eat at the buffet. However the other people we spoke to stated the Steakhouse should be closed it was so bad and the Italian restaurant had absolutely terrible service. The choices were very limited - thank goodness for the croissants and fruit @ breakfast! It took 10 minutes on average to get our first cup of coffee and Only on one occassion did we get a refill. On a positive note they did indeed, as advertised, have top shelf liquor and the bartenders knew us by day two and we didn't even need to request our drinks. The grounds were well kept as far as the lawn, flowers and the pool was immaculate. The weather was great! All in all, if we were expecting a 3-star, our expectations would have been met, but this was listed as a 4+ star in our brochure.

The rooms on the Tropical side were very roomy. One bedroom separate from a sitting area. Huge wall closet. Clean and quite comfortable. The bed was fantastic. Not one sleepless night. Food was well displayed hot and served in a very clean environment. Some people had complained about the food not being hot, likley because they took forever to return to their tables to eat, because they were still trying to get more on. It was very good, never boring. We had Italian, Steak, Vegitarian, Crepery and the Mexican. The only one we were not so happy with was the Mexican because it sat so heavy afterwards. Totaly our fauly. The menus were very easy to pick from. All great food. We both shared each others meals at all five restaurants. Not one meal was dissapointing. We had the buffet one night because we did an excursion (never again.) it was hot when it needed to be and was cold where it needed to be. The buffet was great for breakfast. We had the cereal most mornings as it was great and I am not a cereal eater. It had no preservatives and was a real change from the cardboard that sits on store shelves for a year at home. Goats milk is easy to take as well. We needed alot of it for the coffee. Half coffee and half goats milk. The beach was the better that the resort 20 minutes north and the other 30 minutes south. Terrific soft sand and none of the fleas everyone squaks about. Not one pest to be seen other than ants in our room the day after we left a yogurt container in the garbage one night. They went out with the bag and never saw another. Do not go anywhere else to shop as the beach vendors are truly the cheapest. Do not buy right away, leave and come back until you get good prices. The normanl as I found out was about 20 to 30 percent of what they ask. I got $280.00 worth of stuff for $115.00. Start real low. And do not be afraid to walk away. The entertainment was great, They work so hard and are fun to be with. Any one of them will talk with you and carry on conversation. This place is truly a great place, from one end to the other. We are not big drinkers and found that service in the bars was under par. They will walk around doing nothing rather than serve you if you do not have a dollar in hand. I got them back a couple times. Hold the dollar in your hand and walk away when served, especially when you just want water for the room. Josephina was a terrific maid, she did towel and flower arrangemnets on her first day with out knowing us. We took a coffee pot for our room as there is not one. We did not use it as the coffee was drinkable. When we left we cleaned out all our creams shampoos and other things for weight and gave it to her. We also left the unused and new coffee pot. She was so happy. She wrote us notes every day thanking us. The grounds are fabulous. Do not be afraid to walk outside the gates at the entrance or down the beach. It may look scarey but everyone is so friendly. They understand when you say youy are to tired and want to just walk. No Gracias goes a long way when repeated. If you want real good service fun times and even a kids club for kids this is the place. It is a true Paradise as Nelson the bus guide said. Better deals can be got from vendors if you tell them you are leaving tomorrow. They panic. Do not hesitate at this one, it cost $100.00 more per person because I waited a day. It kept going up as we checked on it. It rose over $350.00 per person in a month. Have a ball.

<Author>Blue-eyes-too
<Content>Enjoyed Sirenis for beach, pool and public areas My husband and I vacationed Jan 21-28 and had pretty good weather (although windy every day and almost a gale on the last day) with some light rain on 5 days and heavier rain one day. The beach is beautiful, the pool area very pretty, the lobby a tropical delight. The tennis courts were the best I've played in years - especially the time they were raked and topped just before we played at 8 a.m. one day. The relaxation massage at the spa (30 minutes $25 U.S.) was adequate. Food was average - repetitive food at buffet at both lunch and dinner. But the chicken and pork were very tasty and best fish was the grouper with white sauce at a supper buffet. The a la cartes we booked (two guaranteed with Signature) were not worth it - o.k. pizza at the Italian and chicken and small (canned?) shrimp at the Mediterranean. Rooms were run down although clean, shower had good pressure, many lights not working, air conditioning functioned well. Ant problem but they stayed on the floor. Staff - some friendly, many indifferent. And difficult to get bartenders attention even when we tipped regularly. As someone said above, we wouldn't go back because there are so many resorts to explore. It was overall a positive experience. By the way, if you are with Signature, don't risk buying entry to the VIP Lounge ($23 U.S. per person). The bus was late and we ended up not using it since we only had 30 minutes after 2 hour line up to get to the Skyservice ticket agent at the airport.
