<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lots of info for families My wife and I (both 29) and our daughter (2 years less a week 鈥?i.e. she flew for free!) went to the Sirenis (pronounced See-ren-us) Tropical for a week from Jan 2-9, 2006. This was the first Caribbean all-inclusive trip for either of us. We flew out of Kitchener-Waterloo which was a very convenient, new service. Because we didn鈥檛 know much of what I鈥檓 about to tell you, our week got off to a bumpy start. However, by the end, we definitely didn鈥檛 want to come home. This review is extremely long (sorry!) but full of good tips, and I鈥檝e tried to divide it into sections to help you find what might be most useful.Resort Layout 鈥?great!The Sirenis Tropical and the Sirenis Cocotal are supposedly two separate resorts but they share everything without restrictions. There鈥檚 a long walkway that divides the two halves but everyone has access to everything at the amalgamated resort(s). Each resort is comprised of about 20 buildings that generally have about 12-20 rooms each (see more on rooms below). On the Tropical side, I would highly recommend building Q or S (fight for this with your rep or at reception!), which are very close to the pool and the beach. Of course, that means they are also farthest from the main buildings and buffets but, as discussed below, they serve lunch near the pool so it鈥檚 only twice a day you have to make the short hike up there. It鈥檚 hard to describe everything, but at one end (the 鈥榖ottom鈥? of the resort is the long, free-form pool and the beach/ocean. At the other (鈥榯op鈥? end are the main buildings, which include reception, the buffet restaurants and some of the other resort amenities (e.g. casino, disco, a couple a la carte restaurants, etc.). The long walkway (about 150 metres/yards) connects the two areas and walkways to all the accommodation buildings run off the walkway. The resort grounds are really well kept, with lots of nice landscaping (including flowers, palm trees everywhere) and people working on this constantly. As I鈥檒l mention below, I ventured down to the much more pricey Secrets Excellence and, for resort amenities and aesthetic appeal, it鈥檚 not better in any way.Pool 鈥?perfect!We found the pool to be perfect. It鈥檚 basically shaped like an hourglass. However, it鈥檚 nice because buildings (where they serve lunch and have a bar during the day) jut into the 鈥榳aist鈥?of the hourglass (connected by a bridge that goes over the narrow part of the pool/river that connects the two ends) so you can鈥檛 really see the other side of the pool. At our side (Tropical), it was very quiet but on the other side (Cocotal), they were constantly running games and events 鈥?rather noisy but appealing to some, I imagine (and you can sit anywhere you want, of course). Both sides have a great swim up bar and easy access down to the beach. Of course, as others have described, there do seem to be a somewhat limited number of loungers by the pool (especially the kind with backs that go up and down). We were often out to put our towels on a pair of loungers as soon as we woke up (e.g. 7:30 am) and never had any trouble finding what we needed (we never tried to get beach loungers 鈥?being by pool was better 鈥?but it may have been more difficult there). You can then leave for several hours (e.g. to eat breakfast, sleep some more) and nobody will bother your towels 鈥?same for any bag you leave there, though I wouldn鈥檛 recommend leaving anything valuable in it. Beach/Ocean - not badThe beach is fairly wide. The sand isn鈥檛 white (but who cares really) and in many spots contains a lot of tiny sticks/brush (not the kind that would hurt anyone, but somewhat uncomfortable for toddlers to walk on). However, those spots are easy enough to avoid. As for the ocean, it鈥檚 fairly rough (i.e. waves more than a foot tall if you were more than 10 metres off the beach) and very few people braved any of the watersports that were available. Once you get out about 5 metres, the water is pretty much over your head (no big deal, but just be aware). However, before you get to waist deep, pretty much everywhere that we went, you were walking on coral. Therefore, I鈥檇 recommend bringing/wearing sandals. However, if you go to the far, far left side of the beach (Tropical side), the sand in the water is much nicer and it鈥檚 quieter over there as well.Other Stuff At The Resort 鈥?pretty good (see info on restaurants further below)There鈥檚 a casino with about 20 slot machines and 5 tables (2 blackjack, 2 for a type of poker, 1 roulette 鈥?usually $5 minimums). I played one night and met lots of interesting 鈥榖lokes鈥?from England and France. As others say, drinks are free for gamblers at all times, including after midnight. Didn鈥檛 see the disco (opens around 10 pm) or the spa. Tennis courts looked good. Workout gym is adjacent to spa and definitely adequate (about 5 cardio pieces and 5 weight machines 鈥?nobody there ever). The so-called sports bar near the front of the resort has ping-pong and pool tables and an adjacent bar 鈥?not that great but adequate.Along the front avenue into the resort are about 8 small shops (clothing, cigars, drug store, convenience store, etc.). However, they really didn鈥檛 offer much. The cigar store guy would bargain with you but the others had awful prices and not too much selection. This is unfortunate because there鈥檚 not really anywhere else to buy stuff nearby. Somebody mentioned a small plaza a 5-minute cab ride away but, when we went past it on our way back to the airport, it looked like it mostly just sold art and souvenir items (much like the beach vendors do). If you鈥檙e looking to buy rum, cigars, souvenirs, I would really recommend going to the 鈥榞ift shop鈥?on the beach to the left of the resort (left if you鈥檙e looking at the ocean). The main guy over there is awesome 鈥?speaks tons of languages and easy to bargain with. I got a bottle of good local rum and 10 of the best cigars for $20 (beware that the rum bottle might break easily). They also do massages and braiding over there for about half the price you鈥檒l pay at the resort. As well, you can buy duty free at the Punta Cana airport (e.g. $9 U.S. for a 1 litre Bacardi light!! 鈥?much cheaper than on the plane even).Room Layout 鈥?awesome!One main difference between the Tropical and the Cocotal is the room layout. At the Tropical (where we stayed), the space is divided into three rooms. The relatively large bathroom has a toilet, sink and tub, all made of a pretty nice marble-like material. Beside the bathroom is a sitting room (about 12鈥?x 12鈥? with a futon-type couch, two small tables, a window, and a desk. The third room (about 12鈥檟 20鈥?contains two double beds, two night tables, two large closets, and a small desk/dresser 鈥?not too many drawers). Both the bedroom and the sitting room have doors that open on to a decent-sized patio that has two plastic chairs and a table. All in all, we were thrilled with the room. We found the separate bedroom/sitting room layout (didn鈥檛 see this advertised anywhere else) is especially good for families with younger kids (or for dads or moms who like to come home later and don鈥檛 want to wake everyone up on the way in!). One other difference is that the Cocotal is three levels per building whereas most of the Tropical is only two levels each. There鈥檚 no iron in the room (or available anywhere) but nobody cares how pressed your clothes are (even less than I thought they would). Restaurants 鈥?not bad, but not greatIn my wife and I鈥檚 opinions, the buffet food was edible but not great. We actually didn鈥檛 really gain any weight, which should be unheard of for an all-inclusive vacation! The breakfast was pretty good if you liked omelettes and the dinner buffet always had a pasta bar and a carved meat that wasn鈥檛 bad. But the rest of it was just okay, especially if you鈥檙e expecting American/Canadian cuisine (not sure if this is more widely available at other resorts or not?). However, more than a couple people we talked to said the food is far worse in Cuba, unless you鈥檙e at the best of the best resorts. And related to that, the food at the Secrets down the beach was fabulous the one time I was fortunate enough to sample it. Anyway, this was one of the biggest disappointments for us, at least for the first few days until we managed to get into the a la carte restaurants for several of our last nights鈥?dinners (see below). As for the a la carte restaurants, there were many and we managed to eat at the Italian once, Mexican once, and the Steakhouse twice. All had great food (but beware the rubber cheesecake at the steakhouse) and the service was a very welcome change from the do-it-yourself, sometimes-large lineup buffet. However, as others have written, it is often a very difficult to book into the a la carte restaurants, and usually involves an hour lineup. As well, at least during the xmas break week we were there, there seemed to be no guarantee you would even get into a single one! (preferred booking times were even supposed to be part of the Signature Club package, but that didn鈥檛 seem to be the case at all). However, after having little luck (only one 8:30 reservation), I complained to our Signature rep and she got us. We then made friends with Jimmy, one of the head restaurant guys (find him!!! :), and he hooked us up with an extra night in the steakhouse and better times for us for our other reservations. We were sure to thank him with a few dollars and one of the baseballs we had brought to give out to extra special staff. If I can make any suggestion to try to ease the pain of the a la carte process, I would definitely try to get some sort of a guarantee out of your tour company before you go, because it鈥檚 tough to work these things out once you鈥檙e already there. Another concern for us was that the a la carte restaurants didn鈥檛 open until 6:30 (if you could get that as your reservation time) and the buffets not until 7:00. For people with kids or toddlers (including ours who is in bed by 7:30), this was very inconvenient, especially when they don鈥檛 have any sort of takeaway container available. At the bars, they only have one kind of beer (Presidente) but it鈥檚 a good lager/pilsner (especially when it鈥檚 free and free-flowing at almost all hours of the day). I鈥檇 also recommend the Sirenus Especiale (like a frozen creamsicle) or Banamama (just like the strawberry-banana smoothies I make at home, but with booze in them!). Beware the pina colada because it鈥檚 supposedly a natural laxative (and you鈥檙e unlikely to need any help in that department!). And if you want alcohol in any drink, you have to ask for it (e.g. 鈥淏anamama with run, por favor鈥?. Other tips:-get the safe for your peace of mind (safe is located in closet)-One other suggestion is to move the TV from the bedroom to the sitting room if you want (maybe especially if you have kids and you want to watch TV at night).-when checking in (it will be pandemonium), get all of the following to save you trips back to the desk later: TV remote control, safe key ($2/day)-when checking out, you have to return all of the above items, along with your towel cards so be sure to get these by taking your towels back to the towel hut before it closes (5 pm) on the day of/before your departure (opens at 9 am)-air conditioner only runs when room key is in the slot by the door, so leave it there when you go out (we got an extra card at reception no problem)-some airlines have strict luggage limits (both dimensions and weight) for both checked and carry-on bags (equivalent to only about one large bag each for the checked bags). Our airline (through Signature) was Skyservice and we almost got charged an extra $7 for each of the 5 kilograms we were over the total bag weight limit for our carry-ons. However, they asked if some of it was food (and it was), and they strangely let us go because of that reason (?). -we had no issue with diarrhea or mosquitoes. Watch out though because they tear through the resort on trucks around 6 pm every evening spraying some gas that a farmer said was used to get rid of bugs on crops. It supposedly won鈥檛 kill you unless you鈥檙e directly in its path, but this is a definitely possibility given how reckless they are.-at the Punta Cana airport, food is somewhat reasonably priced (e.g. $4 for pizza slice). Terminal two (look for it) is air conditioned and has a great kids park connected to it. -The bus ride to the resort from the airport wasn鈥檛 really all that bumpy, but still try to sit close to the front of the bus if possible. On the way to the resort, the bus鈥?washroom was very dirty and had no toilet paper or paper towels. On the way back, it was locked and nobody (driver, tour rep) had a key! A family sitting about 2/3 of the way back had both of their kids get sick in the aisle as a result. I鈥檇 expect better from a Signature affiliate but we managed to survive the one hour trip each way.-Similarly, don鈥檛 expect too much out of your tour company reps. The signature ladies were very nice but didn鈥檛 seem to have too much influence over the hotel (and I feel that way even in spite of what one managed to do for us with the a la carte restaurants, as described above). They mostly seem to be there to sell excursions and keep everyone organized. As well, we picked this hotel because it was a Signature Club resort, but most of those benefits didn鈥檛 really pan out. Finally, here鈥檚 a list of some things you may wish to bring with you that you may not have thought of:-鈥榰mbrella鈥?stroller if you have an infant or toddler 鈥?can be very handy at the airport and around the large resort (at the airport, don鈥檛 check it with your baggage because you can keep until you get to the stairs to the plane)-(alarm) clock 鈥?no clock of any kind in the room-cable cord 鈥?as mentioned, we moved our TV from the bedroom to the -short extension cord 鈥?could be handy? (see next point)-electrical converter 鈥?they don鈥檛 mention that this is needed in the brochures and it isn鈥檛 necessarily. However, out of the three electrical devices (e.g. shaver, hair dryer, camera battery charger) and two extension cords we brought, none of them would fit into any of the outlets. Some other people from Canada said some of their appliances鈥?plugs would fit, but others would not. If you look at the 鈥榯ongs鈥?on the cords of certain devices (at least those in Canada; maybe elsewhere), some will have one tong that is wider than the other. These won鈥檛 fit! After buying a $3 converter from the resort store which also wouldn鈥檛 fit our cords, we borrowed a cheap converter from another Canadian family that did the trick (thanks you kind folks from Hamilton!). -slippers 鈥?floor is tile throughout all the rooms and kind of hard and cold-water, beach toys 鈥?hard to pack, but very expensive and limited selection there (i.e. $14 U.S. for a small bucket  shovel)-chocolate, other favorite snacks 鈥?in short supply and expensive (e.g. $4 for a tiny can of Pringles)-same for sunscreen, medications, etc. (as a general rule, don鈥檛 plan to buy anything there unless you want to pay through the nose for it)-insulated mug with lid 鈥?you鈥檒l read that others recommend this for bar drinks, but it鈥檚 also good idea for your morning coffee because the only 鈥榯akeaway鈥?cups they have at the bars or buffet are tiny plastic ones -items to tip maid or others with 鈥?e.g. lipsticks, items from your country, etc. 鈥?and bring lots of $1 bills for this purpose as wellAnyway, I think that鈥檚 it (finally). Sorry for the novel. Feel free to email me at andyk1000@ hotmail.com and I might have a couple other insider tips or some pictures if you鈥檙e interested. Also check out Debbie鈥檚 Dominican travel website as we found it had lots of good tips. Have fun!

<Content>what i thought I just got back from this resort. Like a lot of ppl i was worried after i read some of the negative reviews, especially since my wife is pretty picky. Despite some iffy weather(rained everyday for about 15 minutes) it was not that bad.Yes the food could have been better (no variety from one day to the next), yes the service could have been better (no one would ask us if we wanted a drink), and the rooms were average.For me the trip was about relaxing which it was, my wife and her sister and myself all had a good time, nothing to overly complain about.I've heard the saying it's a third world country which it is, that's why i never really expect a lot.This is my second time to D.R.and this was 10 times better then my first visit (Puerto Plata)would i go again? Yes, because of the location, but not to Sirenis, i never go to the same resort twice (others to explore).As far as i'm concerned, all the ones who have been overly negative about this place, probably should have spent doubled or even triple the money and stayed at 'Secrets Resort', for the money this place is worth it.As far as this resort being too big?? walking isn't bad for you.This was my wife's first 'resort holiday', she's only done cruises which is probably what we'll stick with from now on.So anyone else planning on going here and is still undecided or is booked to go...just go, relax, enjoy the sun, enjoy the surroundings (which is amazing) and you'll love it.

<Content>Not a bad hotel but not a 5 star hotel! I visited Sirenis Hotel between 2nd January 2006 and 9th January 2006 with my girlfriend. Our problems started when it took 75mins to bring our bags from reception to our room. The first day we realised that if you want a sun lounger by the pool/beach you have to go down at 6-7am and put your towel over a sunbed to reserve it (surely a resort this size should have enough sunbeds!). After alot of complaining and arguing we were able to increase this to a pretty average 3 bookings out of 7 nights. The staff at reception spoke virtually no english and were unhelpfull to say the least, the bar staff were equally unfriendly (i've never been to an all inclusive hotel where the bar staff were more interested in getting you away from the bar than speaking to you and having a laugh). Overall defintely NOT a 5 star hotel. We paid over 拢2,500 to go to this hotel for a 1 week stay but this hotel SHOULD BE NOTHING MORE THAN 3 STAR. If your looking for an all inclusive hotel in the Dominican Republic go to Sun Village in Puerto Plata. Its 4 star but miles better than Sirenis Suites! Sun Village is a bigger hotel, has plenty pools/sun loungers, access to all of the speciality restuarants, friendly/funny bar staff...overall they make you want to come back again (there was me thinking that was the point!)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great food! My husband and I stayed at Sirenis Tropical Suites over the new year and, after a rocky first day, the rest of our holiday was great. When we checked in (with only one clerk working to handle a full bus load -- not the greatest planning), we found that our room had been double booked and I had to go to get another room. It was even more confusing because there are two separate hotels -- Sirenis Tropical Suites and Sirenis Cocotal Resort. Everyone kept asking were we on the Tropical side or the Cocotal side and I had no idea. Not knowing the difference and arriving after dark (so we had no idea which way to go) didn't help. Eventually the manager took us himself to our new room and from Day 2 to the end of our 2-week stay, we had absolutely no complaints. One thing you do have to be aware of is the infamous beach lounger run in the very early mornings... my husband went down to the beach before sunrise (usually between 6 and 6:30 AM) and even at that early hour, people were scurrying about reserving their beach lounger chairs. If you happened to show up at the beach after 9:30 or 10 AM hoping to find a lounger, you were out of luck. The hotel brochure said that beach lounger chair reserving was not permitted, but it was NEVER enforced. (It also said that ladies were requested to not go topless at the pool area, but THAT was never enforced either). Once you get into the groove of how the resort works, it's well worth the trip. The food at the buffets was fantastic, always fresh, always lots of variety and the by-reservation-restaurants (of which we only tried 2: creperie and pizza -- both fabulous) were equally good. Food presentation was always exceptional. The only drawback we found in our 2 week stay was the ever-present lineup at guest services where you had to reserve your tables at the reservation-only restaurants. It was usually lined up at least a dozen deep whenever we went by (or was closed) and you were only allowed to make one reservation per day. It was just easier to eat at the buffets instead of the hassle of the lineups. It seemed that the guest service representatives weren't very fluent in English, although in fairness, most of the guests at the resort seemed to be French (I'd say about 70%) with the balance being British, Australian, German and a smattering of Canadians. It gave the place a much more foreign flavour than we expected.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Make it your own... Read many reviews before I went to this resort just a couple of weeks ago. I regretted it as I believe there are only two types of people who write these reviews, those who are really unhappy about something or those who are way to overly exultant.The bottom line is you have to decide for yourself. So instead of telling you how terrible or how great my trip was here are a few tips you might find useful instead:1.It鈥檚 a pretty big resort, so if you intend to find new friends you can and you probably will. The same goes for all age groups. 2.If you are looking for shade by the pool or the beach, I would suggest you reserve yourself a spot with a towel (by 9AM), then go for breakfast or back to sleep.3.If you are looking to be active throughout the day, go to the right (when you face the beach). Most of the animation activities are there including the equipment rentals. 4.If you want a quite area, I would suggest you go to the left side on the beach, not by the pool. Many kids are around the pool. 5.When ordering coco loco or pina colada and you want it with alcohol, make sure you ask (Con Ron鈥︼亰) or 鈥渃on vitamina鈥濃€ith some bartenders6.If you want to be an effective communicator with the staff, learn some Spanish. When in ROME鈥?br/>7.If you care to watch TV in your room and need a remote, ask at the reception for the remote control at check in. 8.If you like to snorkel, take a bit of a walk to the left of the resort. Walk for about 10 mins and there you will find a nice, clear and less murky water for snorkeling (best snorkeling either in the morning or later afternoon when it鈥檚 less windy, wavy) 9.If you sail, you can take out a catamaran鈥est time is when it鈥檚 less wavy but you can鈥檛 control that, so just have fun. As the coral is really close to the shore, I would advise to opt in for the insurance ($5). It鈥檚 worth the investment. 10.Kayaks can be a lot of fun. Some pretty big waves form a few hundred feet away from the beach, and you can have some fun surfing the waves with the kayaks. Don鈥檛 forget your life vest. You don鈥檛 want to flip onto the coral鈥?br/>11.Drinks鈥f you are a late partier but don鈥檛 want to pay, I would suggest to pound a few down before midnight. After then, you can buy drinks at the Disco ($4 US per drink) or go gamble at the casino then drinks will be free12.Some Casino facts. If you play in US you will win or lose in US. If you play Pesos, you will win or lose Pesos. My understanding is you don鈥檛 want to be stuck with Pesos. The US-Peso exchange rate is not in your favour.13.Restaurants. There are a few special restaurants. Make sure you reserve a spot early in the morning. For some you can reserve between 4 and 5PM for next day. I heard the Steakhouse is not great as the meat is overcooked (a must in a third world country). People raved about the Italian and Chinese. I personally preferred the buffet. No need to reserve anything.14.There are mosquitoes, so take some repellent with you. Especially noticeable at night. 15.Get a massage on the beach鈥or $20-25US per 30 mins it鈥檚 a deal. Don鈥檛 go to the Spa, they charge much more. 16.If you are impatient with slower than usual service, you can always accelerate it with a few bucks鈥?br/>I hope these are good, so ENJOY your trip but most likely relax.Cheers

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lock up your belongings This was the first visit to this hotel for my boyfriend and I and we were both having a great time until the third day when we noticed some clothing had gone missing from my suitcase. The complaint to management had done nothing and they very clearly sided with their staff, saying that they were not responsible for anything that wasn't in the safe. We were not impressed, as we had been tipping the housekeeper very well up until that point. This was not an isolated incident either, as the family two doors down from us also had some items missing from their room as well, most notably a diamond necklace. It's no wonder the housekeepers are as gutsy as they are and take those risks because they know they can get away with it. My advice: keep all of your clothing locked up in your suitcase and close the drains in the tub and sink at night to avoid finding cockroaches in your room in the morning.

<Author>KatWebb
<Content>Definately not a 5* Having stayed at a 4 star in Punta Cana last year (the Occidental Grand Flamenco) and having the most fabulous 3 weeks of my life (even though there were negative reviews about it on the internet), I decided to ignore the negative reviews of the Cocotal and was sure that it would be fantastic.However, the first room we were allocated on arrival on Mon 16/5 had light fittings hanging out of the bathroom ceiling with water pouring through, we went back to reception and were allocated another room which had extremely brown water like sewage running from the taps. The hotel admitted there was a problem but did not move us until Thurs 19/5 - a long time to go without a bath!There were other issues such as birds in the restaurant landing on, walking all over and eating the bread and fruit, one night a cockroach on the ham, food poisoning from the Mexican (every person that ate the chicken and beef there on the same night I went all fell ill), the lobby area had a constant stale/mouldy smell and the chairs smelt badly of body odour, the blue lights that they have to attract and electrocute the cockroaches were placed right outside the speciality resaturants and you could not enter without getting swarmed with them, etc. etc.Another warning is to never lie directly on the sun bed mattresses as they are infested with mosquitoes and the resort itself has a huge problem with mosquitoes. Despite using 3 cans of insect repellent I got 86 bites! Our rep who was only coverning at the Cocotal had been in the Dom Rep for 5 months and never had a problem with bites, but after a week at the Cocotal was herself covered.On the plus side we did meet some fabulous people (Hi Kate, Mike, Hayley and Rich if you read this) and the Spa and Casino were excellent.If you want a drink after midnight when the lobby bar closes, just place a 100 peso bet in the casino and you get free drinks until it closes.Fermin (on the entertainment team) was the nicest, friendliest bloke I have ever met and some of the bar staff, waiters and waitreses were also amazing (Frank, Sucre, Henry, Joselyn and Erika deserve a special mention).Unfortunately we had a bad start to the holiday and other little problems that we would probably have overlooked under normal circumstances just seemed to be bigger. The hotel was very busy when we stayed and they had torrential rain for the week before we arrived and for the first week of our holiday, so maybe this is why the standards were not so good.If you have booked to go to this hotel and have stayed at other resorts in the Dominican before, then prepare to be disappointed (it is nowhere near as good as the 4 star Occidental, Bavara Beach or Bahia). I would only rate this a 3 star in comparison.If it is your first time in the Dominican, just beware of what food the birds have been walking over and hopefully have a great time.DO NOT JUST BASE YOU DECISION ON THE REVIEWS ON THIS HOTEL AS THE SIRENIS COCOTAL IS THE SAME!! PLEASE ALSO CHECK OUT THOSE REVIEWS!Feel free to contact me if you wat more info.

<Author>circuit.training
<Content>Our second visit This was our second visit to Sirenis Tropical Suites and it was every bit as good as the first.Rooms: Clean and spacious with air conditioning, ceiling fan and fridge which was re-stocked daily with soft drinks. It's worth tipping the chambermaid early on if you require specific drinks such as 'Cola Light/Diet coke'.Restaurants: All restaurants were good. The steak house is fantastic. However, the booking system was very slow on some days. The buffet was great for kids as they could try everything and leave it if they didn't like it. There was soup, pasta, chips, chicken, salads, rice. casseroles, fresh fruit and cakes and various theme nights too. We prefered the thematic restaurants (Mexican, Italian and Chinese) and are worth a visit if you can book.Entertainment: Seemed good, but we didn't join in the games. Fitness: The gym was well equipped and includes: hand weights, weight machines, two benches and two chest press benches, peck deck, hamstring bench, three cycles, two steppers and one treadmill. There is also space at the back for shuttle runs, press ups, stomach work etc. There is a water cooler. It is open from 8-12 and 4-8pm. However, it can get very warm so training early or later is best - it is not air conditioned. The staff are friendly and helpful and Ishmael (the instructor) spoke reasonably good english and was learning the language every day. As we enjoy circuit training at home the facilities here were perfect for us to continue our training - much to the amusement of other users! The rules are: Over 16's only, appropriate gym clothing and sports shoes. (However, we did see some people in flip flops!) There are tennis courts (4 we think) floodlit too and a five a side football pitch.Spa: Didn't get round to using it but was very popular and looked very nice (it is adjacent to the gym).Location: Very isolated, so for anybody looking to explore apart from the trips would be disappointed. This is ideal for those who wish to spend two weeks sitting by the pool or a beach doing nothing with everything inclusive.Travel company: First Choice: They have recently re-designed their aircraft by reducing the number of seats. This means there is a great deal more leg room and the seats have a 7 personal TV screen. The programmes were ok - but to get the best ones and the kiddies games cost 拢5 per head on outbound and inbound flights. The extra seating space combined with the service from the crew made the journeys very pleasant. If you are thinking of travelling premier class: there are toilets located in the premier class cabin which are used by all passengers. This means that you could be sitting next to the toilet whilst enjoying your extra courses and courtesy drinks! If travelling premium class make sure you are specific about where you sit. Punta Cana Airport:This year we paid the extra ($23.00 a head) to go in to the VIP lounge. Whilst the food was disappointing - ham and cheese sandwiches, prawns with dip, quiche, fruit and pastries, there was plenty to drink (all alcohol and soft drinks). It was air conditioned and we had access to the internet and a TV. The toilets were also much better, clean and luxurious (compared to the main lounge). Please note that if you are travelling premier class you do not have access to this lounge - you must pay the additional fee.Tipping:There is no obligation whatsoever to tip any of the staff and nor do they appear to expect it. However, as mentioned in one previous review the average earning is appropriximately $150 a month. Therefore, if you feel the service you have received is worthy of a tip then $1.00 is more than acceptable. The forgotten few include the toilet cleaners by the swimming pool, the pool attendants and the gardeners. If you are thinking about leaving a tip ensure you take plenty of $1.00 bills with you as it is very difficult to get larger notes changed at the resort. But if you need to then the best people to ask are the bar staff or the bell boys.Summary: Whilst we are thinking of going to another resort as a change next year, we would definitely come back and would recommend it to others.

<Content>Not quite paradise A party of 4 adults and two children went to this hotel from 3rd August to 17th August 2005. The trip to the hotel is about 80 minutes, a little bumpy, but the time goes quickly as you look over the Dominical countryside. Check-in went quickly and we were in our rooms with our baggage in no time. This hotel is well spread out and I would not reccommend to anyone with walking difficulties, however there are ramps for wheelchair users. We found the rooms quite adequate,plenty of storage space and always kept clean. The food in the main buffet was good always plenty of choice. The themed restaurants were also good and made a pleasant change to be waited on instead of the cattle market at the buffet.There is always plenty to keep you occupied at this hotel and the staff work very hard and are always smiling and singing. There was nowhere to sit in the evenings to enjoy your beer without sweat pouring down your back. The evening entertainment venue, although outside, was known as the sweatpit. The airport of Punta Cana is very quaint and that鈥檚 the only way I can think of describing it! It鈥檚 like a huge wooden hut, but it鈥檚 really beautiful. When you get to the entrance there are hula women who maul you and you have a photo taken with them. Then you go to the desk where you give them your $10 each and they give you a card to fill out for your visa. Be patient because it鈥檚 really busy and the form takes about 5 minutes to fill in (which seems like a lifetime when you鈥檝e just had a 10-hour flight!) Then it鈥檚 onto getting baggage, which took about half-an hour 鈥?working on Dominican time now! Once got baggage quite easy to find our bus, someone was there with clipboards and they tell you the number of the bus. Don鈥檛 let any people take your bags for you, its literally 200 metres from door to door!The bus ride was a welcome. Air-conditioned and lots of space. The rep was nice 鈥?David Cox. Who bore a uncanny resemblance to Robin Williams! I was fully prepared for the bus ride, but I鈥檓 glad to say was nowhere near as bad as anticipated. I did feel really sick but that was due to the plane ride, although I鈥檓 sure the bumps didn鈥檛 help! Once at the hotel we got our bags off and went to queue for check in, we was given a fruit drink (think it was some sort of juice and grenadine) which to be honest tasted like crap but was welcomed all the same!At check in we gave our names and was checked off and given our room keys, we then had to queue again to be given a hotel map and explained where our room was. The one thing I would complain about was that on booking our holiday we requested a sea/pool view and I even e-mailed Sirenis a month before departure and they said we could have one. But our view was just of other buildings, the sea nowhere to be seen! Anyway, we put a sticker of our room number on the suitcases and a bellboy brought them to our rooms. We gave him $2 (a $ per bag is standard apparently). Our rooms were easy enough to find with the map, it was about a 10-minute walk from the main lobby. Room: walk in through door and bathroom is on left. Nice marbled sink, have big mirror, shower and toilet. We never had any problems with hot water. Straight on is the lounge with a 3-seater settee and a chair. It has a desk and underneath is a mini-fridge stocked with bottles of Sprite, Coke and Water. A word of warning, the water was a year out of date and every time we drank it we felt ill and had to dash to the toilet. Of course we didn鈥檛 realise it was the water until the last week! To the right of that is the balcony which houses a small table and two chairs. Nice to sit out on in the day or at dusk but not in the evening because of all the insects that swarm near the lights. The bedroom is to the right when you get in the door, which held 2 large double beds. A large television, a desk with 2 drawers and a chair. And a large wardrobe (doors are a bit dodgy) and a safe in the wardrobe. We did like our room but felt annoyed that there wasn鈥檛 a sea view and annoyed that it wasn鈥檛 as big as expected, I鈥檝e seen the pictures on websites where the room is huge with marble floors, well don鈥檛 expect that and you should like it!If you look hard enough you can find flaws, like cracks in the marble and the buildings having cracks, but that鈥檚 only if you鈥檙e pedantic, otherwise you wouldn鈥檛 notice. From he sea end it鈥檚 a little whirl pool which didn鈥檛 work it then leads onto a huge baby pool which is only about a foot deep (if that), then goes deeper to the swim-up bar then its kinda narrow while you tread water to the bigger part where it鈥檚 like 8 ft deep but is huge. Then you have to clamber onto the bridge and crawl under it to get to another huge pool. This has the mermaid in the middle of it where people went to sunbathe or take a break before carrying on! <Content>Relaxation in paradise My boyfriend and I just got back from a week at this resort, and had an absolutely outstanding time. The resort boasts a beautiful beach with gorgeous palm trees and cabanas that provide shade. It鈥檚 outside of punta cana proper, so it鈥檚 very secluded. The pool was great and we enjoyed the fact that there are two swim up bars.We were upgraded to a suite on arrival, and the room was spacious and clean. The d茅cor in the room and the complex overall was pleasant if slightly cheesy, but we weren鈥檛 there for cutting edge interior design so weren鈥檛 bothered.The grounds were lovely and very well maintained 鈥?a tropical paradise with shallow pools, palm trees, and hibiscus growing everywhere.The food was good 鈥?no complaints from either of us. The booking process for the a la carte restaurants was a pain, as you had to line up early to get anything, and by the time dinner rolled around you might not want to go at the reservation time you had picked. The food was good however in the two a la carte restaurants we tried 鈥?the Italian and the creperie.We had no problems with bugs, despite the fact that my boyfriend usually attracts mosquitos in droves. We didn鈥檛 end up using the repellant we鈥檇 brought. A couple I met from Britain had been feeling ill all week, but realized it was their malaria pills rather than the food, when others in their tour taking similar pills were also ill (no one else I met was sick from the food, and we were fine). Given that malaria is not supposed to affect this area of the country, and that malaria pills come along with many unpleasant side effects, I鈥檓 glad I didn鈥檛 get around to buying them before our trip. We were told by our rep not to drink the tap water in the rooms as it isn鈥檛 purified, so we used the bottled water in the mini fridge (it鈥檚 also freely available at the hotel鈥檚 many bars) to brush our teeth and were fine. All the water served in the restaurants, used in ice, or used to wash food and fruit in the hotel is purified and we had no trouble.What impressed us most about this resort, besides the beauty of the beach, was the outstandingly friendly staff. We had wonderful service from our maid, who accommodated our requests for extra water  diet coke in the fridge. Almost all of our servers in the restaurants were outstandingly friendly and helpful. I was also pleasantly surprised to discover how relatively safe the country is, especially compared to many other beach destinations, and especially given how poor the country is. There is security onsite at the resort, but you don鈥檛 have to feel uncomfortable leaving the grounds. It鈥檚 probably best to rent the safety deposit box ($2 per day), which we did, as it gives you peace of mind for valuables.Tips weren鈥檛 expected, however we chose to give $1 each day to the maid and $1 each time we received good service in the restaurants. Tips were always appreciated and greeted with charm and warmth, a much warmer reaction than even a very generous tip would get at home.There are several tennis courts, and there are young boys employed to play with you in case you don鈥檛 have a partner. I used the gym facilities which are small but adequate, and had a tread mill, weights, weight machines, and stationary bikes. Be aware however that the gym is not air conditioned, so it鈥檚 best to plan your workouts for the morning or evening. The adjacent hot tub looked nice, and was very popular, although I didn鈥檛 use it. The massages and facials offered were relatively expensive and given the prices were comparable to home, I didn鈥檛 bother.Our package was with Sunquest, and the onsite Sunquest rep 鈥?Felipe 鈥?was helpful and pleased to provide information about the country. He was also very knowledgeable about Canada, having lived in Toronto for a number of years. I did an excursion to the capital city, Santo Domingo, which I enjoyed very much. It was however best for those who are keen on history and culture, and does involve a long bus ride (3 hours). There were many other excursions available (snorkeling etc.) and I heard lots of positive comments. The excursions are relatively expensive however 鈥?they range from $60-90 for a 陆 or full day.FYI the other guests are mostly Canadian and British, as well as Spanish, French, and German. This hotel doesn't have a contract with a US tour company, so there are very few Americans (although there are many Americans at the 2 hotels 25 minutes in either direction).This resort provided everything we were looking for, and is well suited for couples and families. It is however very quiet at night, so if you are looking to party, this is probably not the place for you. We didn鈥檛 even bother checking out the cheesy on-site disco (El Bonche) where you pay $5 for a drink. There was a small casino which I know others frequented. The evening shows are pretty cheesy. However, relaxation rather than nightlife was our main interest, and this hotel delivered exactly what we wanted 鈥?to relax on the beach in beautiful surroundings. We would definitely consider going back to the Dominican, and would also consider this resort again.

them unless they are really unfussy eaters, my 2 children ate fries  bananas for 2 weeks, we were so glad to see chicken nuggets oneday. the breakfast omelettes are nice though.chinese, peking duck was ok but everything else was too salty ( and i like salt ) mexican was bland, creperie the teenagers enjoyed, italian is just the same spaghetti  lasagne you can get at the buffet. the gourmet restaurant is quite nice, my husband had lobster, i had mango  duck, im not sure if id have paid $25 per head, it was part of my wedding package.id have stayed another week if the food was a bit better.disco isnt bad if you like spanish music (i dont mind some) but drinks are pretty expensive, youre better off going to the casino with a few dollars to gamble if you want a late drink, they are free if you are playing tables/machines. the lobby is the only place to drink in the evenings if you arent eating in one of the al a carte restaurants, the buffet only serves beer or wine, and the lobby bars close at midnight. i have mixed reviews about this resort, for the first 7 days we had a lot of stress and problems but that wasnt really the hotels fault, more airtours, the only thing that lets this hotel down is that they dont cater for children in the restaurants and a few of the staff can be rude, i always treat people in the same way i expect to be treated and thought that reception staff were there to help or solve problems....on the whole id rate this a 3* plus, and although it seems in this review that i was unhappy with my holiday, i didnt want to come home.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very happy with the Sirenis We stayed at the Sirenis from April 8-15th. We had read the reviews and we were prepared for a few shortcomings, but at the end of it all, we really had no complaints at all. Please bear in mind that this is the perspective of a couple of adults who have both travelled to tropical locales in the past. I think many people have some very North American notions of what a five star hotel should be. You're comparing apples and oranges, so get over it.As other reviews have indicated, it is quite a lengthy trip from the airport to the hotel, about 75 minutes. The road trip in itself is quite an eyeopener as you can see how these people really live. It's a very different world. The resort is very nice. We stayed in the Tropical Suites which I gather are a little larger than the rooms available on the Cocotal side. Other than the difference in rooms, I believe that we all had access to the same amenities.The resort is very large. Our room was in a 2 storey building near the main reception, so we had a little bit of a walk down to the beach/pool area. There are no shuttles on this resort like you might find on others, so be prepared to walk a bit. The room was quite nice: a living room that had a couch, chair, tv on a sideboard that encased a small fridge. The bedroom had a couple of double beds, a dresser and a full wall of closet space that was divided into thirds  2 thirds hanging space and 1 third shelves. The safe was in the closet. The middle door of the closet was a full length mirror which was handy. The bathroom was nicely finished in tile  full tub and lots of space at the end of the tub to either sit, place for your shampoo, etc. The shower worked very well and lots of hot water. They provide you with 2 bath sheets and 2 smaller towels, no facecloths. They also supply you with 2 beach towels, but we brought our own. We also had a small balcony that had a couple of chairs and a little table.I had read in other reviews that people had experienced some difficulty with the outlets. We brought a hairdryer, curling iron, an electric shaver and a small clock for the bedroom (there is no clock provided). Everything worked except the curling iron. If your plug has one prong larger than the other, then it may not fit in their outlets. I was also a little surprised to find out that the resort does not have irons/ironing boards available. So, either bring a small travel iron or be prepared to wear things a little wrinkled. Relax...you're on vacation!!!My boyfriend is an early riser and we got on to the reserve your place routine that you find in so many of these resorts. He would go to the pool/beach and snag a couple of chairs. I'd get ready, we'd have some breakfast, and then we'd go down to the pool. If you bring your own towels, your reservation is clearly evident. Otherwise, you may have to leave something else there to identify your spot as many people use the Sirenis towels supplied. Problem with this is beach towels are large and heavy  take up a fair bit of space in your luggage.We found the food more than adequate. We put in our time in the morning line-ups and made a couple of reservations at the a la carte places, but we quite enjoyed the buffet. They had roast chicken one night, salmon wellington another, roast pork another. Yes, there is some repetition in items available at meals, but we couldn't understand people who stated in reviews that the food was terrible. If you are looking for outstanding food, go on a cruise. We did the trip to Saona Island and that was fantastic. Many people equate Punta Cana with powdery white sand beaches. I believe this is true for areas/resorts that are on the Caribbean side. The Sirenis is on the Atlantic side, and the beach is very nice, but nothing like Saona Island. This was tropical paradise. The day trip cost $80US per adult, but when you take into consideration that this covers the bus trip, a boat ride to the island and back, a buffet meal on the island and all you can drink, this was a good deal. The boat ride to the island was on a speed boat, and we came back on a very large catamaran. The beach was that beautiful, white powder and the water was absolutely turquoise. If you do only one trip, this should be the one.If you are a shopper, be advised that there is very limited shopping available. When we did the day trip to Saona, the bus stopped at a shopping area but I found the selection of merchandise to be very poor. However, I did not go there to shop so this was not a big deal.We were very pleased with the trip and hope that you enjoy the Sirenis as much as we did. Cheers!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Two Weeks of Paradise I really don't know what all these people are complaining about. First off I have worked in several tourist linked jobs and when people come to Canada you expect them to speak our language. Yet, when you go to another country you expect the resort employess to be fluent in English? Guess what, there are people from other countries visiting there too, so do you want them to be fluent in those langauges as well? They do speak several languages, just not fluently. This resort just had a major hurricane come through last season, so they are doing some fixing up, there wasn't a day when I didn't see someone doing work on the grounds. We had are wedding down there and there were a total of 16 of us, no one really wanted to come home. My wife and I were really taken care of, it was unbelievable. If you are thinking about having a wedding somewhere, this would be an excellent choice. The food was excellent, between all of us we managed to make it to all but two a la cartes, not one person complained. The buffet was awesome, they make you omlettes and smoothies on the spot in the morning, and pasta with your desired extras for lunch and dinner. We would definitly reccommend the excursions that we went on, which were the Safari Outback and swimming with sharks and sting rays. Although, we did not see sting rays the trips were amazing and the people were very friendly. As far as the resort people are concerned, if we had a complaint they were quick to jump. For instance, we were talking to one of the guys, and when my wife said Everything is good except, he immediatly jumped and was going to fix it, until he realized that that she was saying ...except, we are leaving today. As far as getting sick, everyone is quick to blame the food, yet they forget they go out in the sun all day and get sunstroke or they take full advantage of the free booze and get sick from that. There were several in our party that got sick, but none of us would blame the food. None of the sicknesses came at the same time, and people were always trying the same foods. Usually they were getting sick after a day of being in the sun without a hat. To further this point we had three paramedics in our party and not one blamed the food for the illnesses. Okay, well now for that white sand I keep hearing about, guess what people, the sand was there a long time before the resort, so don't blame the resort because there is no white sand. If you want white sand there is some beautiful stuff over on the Carribbean side, we went there, but the the beach is packed with resorts and piles of tourists and vendors. Where as our beach was generally quiet with just the people from the resort, and was kept very clean. The employees were always working on the pool, grounds and beach, the place was beautiful. If you do go down and you think the beach on the resort is a mess, just walk down past the shops outside the resort grounds and you can see how ugly it could be. A review would not be complete without mentioning the entertainment. If you wanted, you could be kept busy from about 10am to midnight with all their activities. Also, these complaints about the casino having a couple of machines, there is in fact 20 machines, I counted, honestly how many can you play at once? It was never busy in there. Our party plans to return to this resort as it was an amazing time. However, if you are looking for the Ritz, some fancy meals, and a personal servent that speaks English then maybe you should go to the Ritz. Well thanks for reading and I hoped I helped you.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Had A Great Family Vacation After reading some of the negative comments about the hotel ,my wife and I were concerned about going to the Sirenis Tropical Suites with our two children who are 2 and 3 1/2. Although the bus ride was long (yes it is one hour) we were very pleased with the service, meals, cleanliness, beach, pool and activities. We were there from March 17- March 24. The Suites rooms are a definite bonus and worth the extra $150 for the week. You could put the kids down for a nap and do your own thing in the adjoining television room. The cribs for the babies are rather small though. About half the size of a traditional crib you would get in North America. If going with a baby you might want to ask for another comforter to use as the pillow as the plastic one that comes with the crib makes alot of noise. The crib came to our room within five minutes of our request. When we couldn't figure out why the aircondition wasn't working within one of our rooms they were there in five minutes. Hint, the air conditioners work on censors, if the windows, doors or screens aren't shut correctly the air doesn't work. Therefore in our case it was working, we were just incapable of figuring it out. All in all the service from all the people at the resort was excellent. We requested a beach/pool room if one became available and on the second day we were in the room of our desire. Not too many places make that promise and follow through. The food servers and workers were all friendly especially with our two young children. I don't know what the other people are complaining about. Do they just want the workers to be smiliing at all times and be at your beck and call. Be real, they work very hard for peanuts and in the meantime they see some pretty inconsiderate and insensitive tourists. In fact if my family and I had any complaints it was about how some (not many) of the fellow travellers leave litter on the pool deck or beach front when the trash can is two feet away. However, they do a great job keeping on top of the mess these slobs create. Activities ran everyday and they looked pretty good. We didn't manage to take part in many but those that did participate looked like they were having fun. The events ran on an hourly basis. Rooms were cleaned everyday. Two large double beds, lots of space, and a good size separate living room with a T.V and a stalked mini bar with bottled water and pops. Do not drink the tap water as it is not potable. The ice cubes are fine as they are from distilled water. None of us became sick from the water or the food. Not a five star hotel suite like in Toronto but nonetheless as good as your going to get for a four and a half star in a country like the Domenican, Cuba or Nassau. The beach was nice, not the best but still good, it is brown sand and the water is more of a dark blue. The waves were pretty forceful so watch the little ones as it knocks them over. Also watch where you enter the ocean as some areas have coral and it hurts the feet. You will notice where it is as the water is a much darker blue in those spots. The beach is endless. I walked for a full one hour in one direction and still didn't get to the next resort. It is pretty barren out that way and the locals try to get you to go to buy items from their stalls which are about 100 yards inland. They are friendly but I would suggest leaving anything valuable at the resort if you want to do some beach walking. The food was plentiful, there were many interesting dishes. Those people who said the food was awfull and bland must have gone to a different resort because my wife and kidswere always happy with the selections. Fish, poultry and pork dishes were great. Their rice dishes were especiallly good. We only ate at the buffet restaurant and were pleased. We didn't try to reserve anything at the specialty restaurants so we can't comment on them. Tips, try to get suite in the S or T buildings if you want to be by the sea and pool. Leave tips for the people cleaning the room and those serving you at meal time. They only make 50 bucks American a month. If you have gently used clothing, toys, school supplies and make-up for the women it is also appreciated. It truly is a poor country and you will see it on the drive to the Hotel. Bring key Spanish phrases to help you communicate with your room cleaner. The personell at the front all can communicate in English. However, be patient with them they truly try their best to accomadate their guests. Although we took the medication for malaria we did not see one mosquito on the resort and nor did we get bitten by anything else. If you are travelling off the resort it might be wise to take your meds though. 24 hour doctor was just outside the front door of the resort and was very knowledgeable. There is a pharmacy in the same complex if you run out of sunscreen. Put on your suncreen as the sun is quite strong. My daughter and son really loved it. They had so much fun. We would go back again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>First and last time we'll visit We stayed at the Serenis Tropical Suites in Punta Cana between Feb. 26 and March 13 and we were quite disappointed with the place. Thank God we went with the other 3 couples. We made most of our fun together.  Given the number of English-speaking Canadians that travel to Punta Cana, we were amazed that no one spoke fluent English. Communicating was extremely difficult and made it hard to order food, drinks and service. The resort promotes that their staff speaks English. If that's true than they sure as heck were not willing to use it or didn't speak it very well.  Most of the staff members around the resort, apart from the entertainment staff, were unfriendly and rarely smiled. The cashiers and dealers at the casino never cracked a smile the whole time we were there. They tried to cheat us on the room arrangements. Our travel agent arranged for us to be in the same building with King size beds, etc. They had us spread all over the place and several of the couples only had double beds. Only after going back to the front and haggling with the staff did we get the correct room arrangements.  The resort advertises International drinks. It wasn't until after 3 days later we finally figured out how to get them. We saw some guy with a VIP band get a Bacardi's instead of Normandy at the swimup bar. When we asked the bartender she told us all the bars keep the International booze under the counter. From then on we had to be insistent each time we asked for an International drink. Even then you had to keep an eye on them. Several times we caught the bartender pouring Normandy even after we insisted on Bacardi or Barcel贸. While trying to use our long distance calling card we were not told there would be a long-distance calling charge to reach the toll-free service provider. The evening before check-out we approached the customer service desk to pay our invoices. We waited 45 minutes to be served. When we finally did get served, we disputed the extra long-distance charge. We were directed to the operator's window where the representative laughed at us and said we had to pay. We went back over to the service desk and requested to speak to a manager. When the manager showed up he offered no retribution or apology for the error.  On a scale of 1 to 10, I would rate the food and restaurant service as a 5. You couldn't even eat between 5pm - 7pm. You had to wait until the buffet restaurant opened at 7pm to have supper. The beach was okay but the sand was a coarse and brown, not the fine, white sand you see at other Punta Cana reosrts. The ponds around the resort would have been nice had they not been so full of algae and crud.  On the positive side, we did enjoy the room, the massage spa and the 7 1/2 foot deep pools. We were pleased to make the acquaintance of a few fun and friendly people, like the bartenders at the casino and main lobby bar as well as a few of the waiters in the buffet restaurant.  Overall we found our stay less than fair. I certainly wouldn't recommend the Serenis Tropical Resort over the Occidental Grand Flamenco. Like I said, we had fun but it was only because we reserved to the fact we couldn't change things and decided to make our own fun. Be careful who you recommend the Serenis to.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Its Out of This World!!! I stayed at the sirenis tropical suites with my partner from 23rd Feb until 10th March. We are both in our early 20s and we though the hotel was amazing!!! It spoils you rotten. Its my first time to the carribean and i thought the place was totally stunning. The beaches, hotel and the staff couldnt have been any nicer. I felt like i was walking about dreaming for the 2 weeks i was there.The flight from manchester was 9hours which went in ok. They were both very good though the safari makes you realise how lucky you are and just shows you what a luxuary hotel you are staying in when you go to the typical dominican home.Honestly if you are booked up to go to the hotel you cant be dissapointed. If youve booked this hotel dont worry about the bad reviews because i did. This is an honest opinion its great and you will really really love it!!! So look forward to it because im booked to go back next year and cant wait!!Take care all.xx

<Author>Burnsie_8
<Content>Sirenis with Kids....Great! I have just returned from a week @ the Sirenis Tropical Suites with my family. After reading reviews on this property I felt it was necessary to post a review upon my return. We are a family of 5, an infant of 21 months, a 5 year old, a 4 year old and 2 seasoned travelling parents.Family notes:The suites side of the property is well suited for families and there were alot in evidence there the week of our trip. The North end of the freeform pool was where we predominently spent our time. This side of the pool was away from the animation/action side (opposite side). There are alot of shade huts but you are close to the rear of the restaurant service area as you go to the washrooms so try to stick to the ocean side of this area if you are picking a hut.Plan for an afternoon snack as the buffet restarants only open @ 7:00 pm and the earliest you can book an a'la'carte resturant is @ 6:30 pm. There were always enough highchairs when we chose to eat and the staff is excellent with the kids.Staff notes:Tip early in your trip, but be sure to check when the staff are finished their shift as they are on 11 days then off 3. Tipping is certainly appreciated although all staff we encountered were friendly and polite and willing to communicate. A little Spanish is also appreciated so print off a sheet of Spanish phrases and practice on the flight. Facilities notes:The pool is similar on both ends and has a gradual entry that is perfect for kids. The pool closes @ 6:00 pm each night and is chlorinated and they are busy cleaning the following morning. Didn't make it to the disco, casino or much else for that matter, check other reviews for that stuff.Room notes:Suite rooms are clean and have ample room. The safe is located in a large wall of storage in the bedroom. There was more than enough room for clothing and bags for a family of 5. The a/c was ice cold if you wanted it that way. A nice balcony is accessable from a patio door in the bedroom or a glass door in the living space. The bathroom was clean and fully tiled with a great shower and low bathtub for the kids. Water from the taps was unpurified so don't drink it. The plugs/electricity was the same as home although the sockets are deep so plugging in a laptop or other type of transformer might be difficult. The mini bar only contained water and pop but was refilled each day. The tv remote worked and there was about 8-10 english channels to choose from including HBO and Disney for the kids. The a/c and all power is controlled by a gadget beside the main door and you need to leave a cardkey in it for the power to operate. We chose to leave our 2nd cardkey in it for the whole stay so that the room was always cool when we returned from the days activities.Beach notes:You can walk the beach for 1/2 hr in either direction without seeing another resort. Sand is not power but the kids thought is was great for making sandcastles. There is a small roped off area for swimming. Be careful when swimming outside of the area because there are lots of coral mixed in with sandbars. The surf was always fairly rough and the wind was appreciated although the flags were more yellow than green during our stay. There are flea markets on either side of the resort just at the boundaries.Kids club notes:Our kids did not go to the club all the time but they did go a few mornings and afternoons. There is always a board by the buffet resturant on the Tropical side that says what the club will be doing each day but be advised that they tend to change what they do on a whim. We would typically check the board but would always check with the club staff to see what was up for the day. Take your childs birth certificate on the first day you go as the staff verify the childs age when they first sign up. The club also puts on various shows with the kids after dinner so sometimes the activities of the day where focused on what the evening show would be and practising for the show. I know our kids enjoyed being in the mini fashion show but I think they were a little bored practising for it all afternoon. All in all our kids enjoyed themselves when they went to the club and they loved the counsellors that ran it.Food notes: The property is clean and you can always see someone cleaning or working on the grounds.Other notes:Take small bills for tipping with you! You will have a difficult time finding change and even changing travellers checks. I ended up chasing the bellman down a couple of afternoons and he would give me some $1 bills for my larger bills.Tip early in your trip but check when the staff are leaving for their off shift.Do not leave towels out at night as they will be collected up, get up early and play the towel game like everyone else.Tip your waiter in the a'la'carte resturant and he might let you order from the opposite resturant.Leave a cardkey in the pad to keep your room cool all day.

All and all We would not hesitate to recommend this place to our friends.

<Rating>5	5	5	-1	5	-1	5	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent trip!! I travelled to the Sirenis Tropical Suites with my husband and 2 children, aged 10 and 14 - we stayed for two weeks, starting Dec. 9th. I used to be a travel agent, and have had the opportunity to travel widely in the Caribbean - this was our second trip to the Dominican. We stayed on the south side of the island before, and it was great too. I loved this resort!! I was a bit nervous when I read some of the reviews, but we had a great time! It's certainly the best resort for families that I have come across in my travel career. Be prepared for a long ride to the resort, but the roads are nowhere near as bad as folks have made out in previous reviews. It's rural, folks! You're not travelling on a 4 lane highway - thank goodness!! It's a great opportunity to see the real Dominican - how people live and work. Pretty neat, actually!The pool is stellar!! The best we have had at any resort we've ever visited!! Absolutely huge - lots of shallow areas for sunbathing, a pyramid complete with fountain in the middle of the deep, that you can sit upon, bridges, shady areas, super areas for doing lengths, jacuzzis, kids areas - just excellent!!The food was indeed bland, but I never heard of ANYONE getting sick - unlike most trips to Mexico and other places. Breakfast is good, and the made to order omlettes and smoothies were a hit with my family. The a la carte restaurants offered great meals - we enjoyed them, and booked as many meals there as we could. We didn't seem to have any problems reserving, and the resort was full when we were there. The only real complaint we had about the food was that the lunch buffet at the snack bars never varied - it was exactly the same, day after day for the entire two weeks we were there. Got a bit boring.The bartending is superb at this resort! Very, very friendly bartenders who get around in many languages - excellent!! And the lobby bar is really one of the highlights of the resort! It's a big area with loads and loads of seating, where you can sit with your kids and have a cocktail before dinner (alcoholic or non). A great place to meet people and just hang out! We spent a lot of time there. They have entertainment there most nights too - live music, a piano bar, a karaoke evening. All good fun!The rooms were very, very clean and comfortable. We liked the suites because of the living room - nice to have the extra space.The beach. We are avid snorkelers, and were a wee bit disappointed in this area. It's an extremely safe beach, with a great roped off area for swimming that does NOT receive the big waves. Perfect for kids! One of the safest we've been to. The sand is groomed and lovely!! Lots of huts and palm trees. And the beach is amazing for folks who like to walk. You can walk for at least 20 minutes in each direction before you come to another hotel. There is nothing but palm trees and a few little shops along the way - absolutely fantastic for walking. We really enjoyed that! (You will be hassled by the odd vendor who will try to convince you to come and shop in their store along the beach - they're quite aggressive and you just need to give them a firm no and they'll leave you alone). As for the snorkeling, there is just a bit too much sand being churned up to have really good visibility, at least anywhere close to shore. There's lots of fish there, but you can't see them really clearly. We were pleased to see big schools of needle fish - really pretty! Snorkelling was better on the south side of the island. The water is a lovely green in this area (not turquoise), and this is a really nice, natural beach. We really enjoyed it! The water and sand were very clean!The one MUST DO in my opinion, is the trip to Saona Island. I've taken side trips in virtually every destination I've visited, and this is hands-down THE best side-trip I've ever done!! It is long, and it is pricey, but absolutely, absolutely worth it!!! You take a coach ride for approx. 2 hours through the hills and valleys, through sugar cane fields, and through the historic town of Higuey - all really neat to see. Then you arrive in the Bayahibe area on the Caribbean coast and board a gorgeous catamaran for a leisurely ride out to the island. Saona is reputed to be one of the world's Top 10 beaches and I believe it! It's like something out of the South Pacific. Amazing!!! Turquoise, turquoise water, snow white sand, and beautiful low palm trees. A natural paradise. It's a national park and is clean and pristine. They serve you a great lunch under cabanas, right out on the sand (try the grilled fish - really good!), there is an open bar, and the snorkeling was great. On the way back, they take you by speedboat which is a riot! Then they stop at a natural pool, way off shore, and you can snorkel for starfish - FANTASTIC!! They even serve you drinks out in the ocean there! The staff is unreal - loads of fun!! I cannot recommend this trip enough!! If you only take one, I'd do this one!!One last thing about the Sirenis. The staff is horribly underpaid! These people are poor, and they travel long distances to come to work. They work 20 days on and 3 days off, and some of our staff even had that time off cancelled (last minute) so they missed Christmas with their own families. We were told that most staff earns $1 USD per day. (It seems the bartenders are paid a bit better, and earn approx. $140 USD per month). Still awful!! Don't be afraid to tip, people!!! A dollar or two go a long, long way with these folks!! We found that the staff were just delighted with a small tip, and they really work hard! Also, we took one suitcase down with gently used kids clothes, some school supplies, and some toiletry items. We had absolutely no problem finding people who really needed these things. They were just so surprised and delighted to have these gifts. We took everything in one extra suitcase, and then used that suitcase to take home souvenirs that we purchased in the Dominican.We never met a single American at the resort - it's primarily Canadians and Brits - the Brits were GREAT!! Very polite and a lot of fun!Weddings!! We saw 3 while we were there. This resort seems very, very organized when it comes to weddings. Everything seemed to run really smoothly, and they have a gazebo out by the beach for the ceremonies. The photographer walks around the stunning grounds with the bride and groom and snaps photos - also out on the beach. The people we spoke to who got married there were very happy with the service they received. Take US $ with you - really important!! And if you intend to tip (which I hope you do!) take a bunch of small bills with you just for that purpose!Oh, and the internet access is excellent. You can purchase an access card at the desk for $6 US, which gives you 30 minutes of internet ($10 US for 1 hour).DON'T shop at the stores at the entrance to the resort - total rip off, as others have noted! Ridiculous!! $7.50 US for a small bag of chips. Don't bother!! All in all, a great resort!! Super staff, good food, lots of fun!! We'd go back!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>No second time around. As I read the wonderful 4  5 star reviews, I wondered which Sirenis Cocotal they had stayed at. Not the one I stayed at Dec 17-24, 2004.I have never written a review before, but felt so disappointed with this hotel that I feel compelled to share my experiences. This was my 5th trip to the Dominican--I have stayed in Puerto Plata, Juan Dolio and Punta Cana so I do have some knowledge of the resorts there.I will list my disappointments first: the food was terrible and I am not a picky eater. Other people to whom I spoke while I was there were kinder and gentler in their criticisms, such as, The food here is a challenge, isn't it?. The beach buffets were the worst. I never went through the hassle of trying to book the premium restaurants as every morning there were l-o-n-g lines. Of all the other resorts I have visited in DR, this was the worst food--canned corn? Everything was grey in a grey sauce. Fortunately, I could load up on the wonderful bread and rolls and cheese at breakfast in the morning. I felt the hotel was trying to save money by offering such insultingingly bad food of the lowest cost and quality. And who was in charge of the kitchen? Has the manager never experienced good food. Sorry, to go on so long about this, but it was a bad experience that blindsided me.I've always scoffed at people who run to the beach first thing in the morning and lay down their towels. But after two days of not being able to get a palapa (I am very fair and have to stay in the shade) or find enough shade from the very trimmed palm trees, I, too, became one of those people I hate--one reason is that there are not enough beach lounges with adjustable backs so that one can sit upright and read or just watch the passing scene. There are many, many flat lounges w/o adjustable backs and most poeple did not want them, but had to have something to sit on.Never went into the ocean although I love it. It kicked up dirty water around the beach. I prefer the South Punta Cana's turquoise waters and sugar beaches.Hotel shops: License to rob. The outlets at the Sirenis would not accommodate my US plugs--so I had to buy a converter at the mini-mart. Cost? $8.00 US. Fuhgedaboudit.Tennis. I went my first afternoon there. I am a single traveler and travel alone. I always go to the tennis pro and ask if they can set me up with doubles (I am 73 years old with a 3.5 rating). At all other Dominican resorts, they have been so helpful--setting up games with other guests or bringing in tennis players from the community--and each day I would give the pro $20 US because I appreciated his efforts so much and to share with the other players, if local. The Sirenis pro said no, they don't do doubles there and he showed no inclination to help out. He assigned me to play singles with a young woman who had not played for a year and did not know how to keep score and he told me she would be my partner for a week. Lucky for me I met a woman and her husband who set up some doubles for a couple of nights. And that was the end of my tennis attempts. Too bad--the pro could have earned an extra $120 just by being helpful to a tennis-loving guest.Distance from airport and everything else: an hour and a half because of stopping at a couple of other hotels on the way--but still, way too long. I have taken tours on my other trips and would have taken a tour this time but when it takes 1 1/2 - 2 hours just to get to a bus to take one to the boat to go to Saona--that's a waste of time. Next time I will stay at a place 10 minutes from the Punta Cana airport.Punta Cana Airport: The world's most disorganized airport.Casino: this should be called a casinette. It had one roulette wheel, one poker table and one blackjack table. The all-female staff must have been taught to treat the clientele as suspected criminals, as they frowned at everyone all the time and looked at us all suspiciously. But it helped pass the time. Words of praise: All the Dominican staff--waiters, housekeeping, groundskeepers--were the best. They work long, long hours and get paid very little. My housekeeping person, named Sonia, took excellent care of me and kept the room spotless. All my contacts with the Dominican staff were pleasant and I was much impressed with their smiles and warmth.
