<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location and resort We stayed at Sirenis Tropical Suites for 2 weeks from the 2nd December 2004 and had a really relaxing break. The entire resort is very well maintained - including the beach. Food and drinks are freely available in either beach side locations or main restaurants. Depending on your tastes, the food tended to be somewhat bland but perhaps that's what most visiotors wanted. The breakfast omelette chef and smoothie makers deserve gold medals for their patience in dealing with guests in a wide variety of languages. A good selection of foods for breakfast - the best meal in our opinion. Lunches were also good, if a touch predictable, - available at beach side or main buffet restaurant. Desserts and meat were the weakest section on the menu. We found that some of the Canadians wouldn't eat the beef because it's not grain fed like it as at home. Being British, we generally loved the flavour (like our beef used to be) but it was a little tough. As you travel around the island, you see free-range cattle everywhere. Lamb and to a lesser degree chicken were not quite as well represented. The pork, however, was superb. If there is a roast, make sure you don't miss it. It was also rather nice to sip cocktails at any time of day after breakfast. Another good point is the bar staff were really good at dealing with eccentric people like us and provided milk for us to take to our rooms every night because we like to drink a glass before going to bed (settles the stomach for the next round of cocktails following day).We were not aware on booking that the hotel is divided into 2 sections - the tropical suites offering a suite of rooms and Cocotal offering en-suite bedrooms. It did not matter really - great place to be anyway. people with children may prefer the suite just because it's more space and the suites are in smaller 2 floor blocks rather than larger 3 floor.The staff were really good fun and teased the guests (nicely). There is a fair amount of varied entertainment at the hotel including aqua aerobics, keep fit, Spanish lessons, dance lessons for the Merengue, etc. Your holiday can be as peaceful or busy as you want it to be. The majority of guests seemed to be from Canada (and we discovered that we really like Canadians), the ones we met were friendly and outgoing, the next largest contingent was British, then a collection of other nationalities including Polish, Czech, Spanish. If Louise and Howard read this - greetings, we really enjoyed your company.Late evening entertainment includes performances at the outdoor theatre, casino, bar singers. People mingled well and there was always someone to talk to. The kids club appeared to be brilliant and well organised. We watched a performance of Aladdin put on by the kids and enjoyed it. We would like to take our grandchildren next time based on what we saw of the kids club. There are shallow areas of pool and children's pools but no lifeguard on duty so you do have to monitor your own children. Parts of the pool are very deep. Watersports like snorkelling and kayaks are free - and staff are helpful. There is a spa with pay for massage and pampering but at 80 dollars per hour was a bit more expensive than we would pay at home.If you're planning on going on any trips - we went on the Monster Truck trip which was extremely interesting and memorable - we saw cockfighting arena (demo without blades, and yes we did tell the guide that we didn't approve of that in the UK), a voodoo witch doctor, local homes and school (take school supplies for the children or books in Spanish - the tour company is funding a library). Some airlines allow for you to take extra baggage free if its for charitable causes. We also went on the shopping Bonanza which offered a greater choice of goods but again main items seem to be piantings, stone artefacts, jewellery (much cheaper in departure lounge at Punta Cana although limited choice), rum, cigars, and knick knacks. The departure staff at check in were very strict on weight - we were 3 kg over and they wanted $10 per kg. We also had several bottles of water with us because you hjave to be at the airport 3 hours before your flight which we offered to ditch but they weren't interested in the water and waived the charge.Overall, lovely location with a good climate; it was generally around 80 degrees which is comfortable. Great beach, pleasant polite staff, we'd return. Good value for money at the resort. Traders try to get you to pay extortionate prices - just buy your rum, cigars, vanilla etc at the airport. Postcards took about 5 weeks to arrive back so not worth sending.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great family resort Sirenis Tropical Suites is a great family resort. We just got back from a week in the sun punctuated by a some spectacular rain storms (can't help the rain). We had a great time!Sirentis is one of a few hotels dotting the shoreline about an hour from Punta Cana. The Dominican Republic has an interesting approach to road costruction that ensures that you will have plenty of time to see the countryside on the way to the hotel. Our bus guides were helpful and enthusiastic. Note: very few of the staff are truly fluent in English so a little Spanish and a little French (for the Hatian staff) will go a long way.The staff are polite and helpful, particuarly the fantastic crew of bartenders in the pyramide bar in the central foyer. Try the caiperenas (basically a glass of limes in white rum - sort of a dominican Martini).There are two sides to the resort - the Sirenis Cocotal and the Serenis Tropical. Cococtal is more traditional hotel rooms. Tropical is suites ranig from one bedroom (bedroom, bathroom and living room with a balcony) to multi-room suites for large groups. Each balcony has two doors from the bedroom and the living room. Many of the living room doors are stuck shut. If you request it, however, they will come and install a handle. It is well worth it. The pool goes on forever with great kiddie pools at either end and good snacking restaurants on either side for lunch. The pool buffets are packed full of fish and seafood as well as pork and chicken. I found the beef to be a little tough most of the time. It is easy to eat well at this resort.The beach is spectacular but not the best for very little kids due to the pounding waves from the atlantic. This is not the calm Carribean shore, which is both good and bad. The waves will be a ton of fun for older kids with great swimming areas set up to keep things safe. For teenagers and adults there are surf catamarans and surf kayaks waiting at your disposal. Snorkelling is not very compelling due to the surf conditions. The wind off the atlantic keeps even the hottest day comfortable. With a beach like this, moonlit walks are a must. Fortunately, babysitting is affordable and reliable. The going rate is $10 USD per hour. While expensive compared to regular dominican incomes, the women who do this are among the friendliest and most outgoing of the hostess staff. Ask for 'Noemi', she is warm, friendly and very responsible. Be considerate in your hours, these ladies will be up again at 5am preparing for breakfast.Do not shop in the official shops near the driveway of the hotel. They are WAY overpriced. However there is a good medical clinic there and, if you are lucky, you may see the three peacocks that hang around the shops for some reason. The real shopping is to the left and right of the hotel along the beach. The prices you are quoted are WAY overpriced here too but extremely negotiable. You should expect to pay between half and a third of the quoted price.Great activities - horse riding on the beach - this is not a trail ride. Instead, the tour will adjust to your ability. I had a spectacular tour up the beach by myself sometimes at a full gallop. Beginners were taken on a more trailish ride. Remember to tip the guides since they don't receive the money paid for the horses. I heard the four wheelers are great too!Take the Soama Island catamaran trip to the caribean side of the island. It's worth every penny.There are a few things that this hotel could still improve on. The a la carte reservation system is a hoax. The very first morning or afternoon if you can, tip the guy at the reservation desk and ask to make bookings all through the week. Amazingly, space becomes available. If this isn't your speed though, don't worry, the food at the buffet is great too. Service at the restaurants can be spotty. The kids club for 4 to 6 year olds is really just babysitting and was hardly used . Lots of activities for 7 to 10 year olds, though. The bars at the hotel are concentrated around the main lobby bars. This makes it convenient to bump into your buddies but it gets a bit crowded near the bar. Later on the disco opens and the party really begins.Overall, you should have a great trip.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>My review...... I returned last week from 2 weeks at the Sirenis Tropical Suites, so thought I would write my own review after reading some of the others and being worried about what I would find!!The flight from Manchester was on time, and geting through Punta Cana airport was easy and stress free. Check in at the resort was quick and our room/suite was large and clean.The beach was nice, with lots of cabana's (is that the right word?) and beds. Unfortunately the sea wasn't much good for snorkelling simply due to the fact that it was quite choppy sand was being churned up constantly. The Hobie Cat's were good fun, although be careful you don't get ripped off - when we went to enquire about them at the beach hut, we were told we had to pay $5 insurance in case we damaged the boat, although when we actually did go to take one out, there was no mention of insurance (quite rightly seeing as we were all inclusive!), so think someone was trying to pull a fast one there.I never found the pool or pool area to be dirty, although it is to be expected that there will be a few empty glasses around by the end of the day.The grounds are very well kept - never a blade of grass out of place. The outside pool/pond things didn't smell at all, although looked a bit boring for the fish!!The food was okay - nothing special, but you're not going to starve. The omlettes were good at breakfast, and the banana milkshakes were delicious.It was a bit of a hassle trying to book the other restaurants, and to be honest I did find the Guest Services staff fairly arrogant and a bit rude, but it certainly didn't ruin the holiday.We had nice meals at the themed restaurants - we tried the Mexican, Italian, Chinese and Steakhouse and don't have complaints about any of them.The shows left a bit to be desired, so we only saw one, but we went to the Casino most nights which was a good laugh and stayed open til 3. We didn't try the disco, but from speaking to other people, we're glad we didn't bother as they said it was tiny, with terrible music, and you had to pay for your drinks.If you're drinking alcoholic cocktails such as Pina Colada's and Daquiri's, remember to specify that you want them with alcohol when you order, as they tend to make them without unless you ask.There is a gym, which has a stepper and a bike and quite a few free weights, and the spa looked nice, but we never went in.We went on the Saona Island trip - the island was beautiful, but be warned if your rep tells you it takes an hour to get to the place where you meet the boat - it takes TWO hours on a coach, and then there was quite a bit of waiting around to get on the boat.We also went quad biking, but found the people at either end of the beach to be about half the price of the people that sold it from within the hotel. It was really good fun - we went to a natural lagoon, and to Mackay (sp) beach, and through loads of countryside, and it cost $50 for 2 people for 2 1/2 hours which was very reasonable. We went with the vendors at the watersports end of the beach.We also went to Manati Park (there is a free bus that runs from the hotel). It's quite small, and you only really need a couple of hours there. We found that everyone went to the same shows at the same time, and then sort of carried on round the park in the same direction. We went the opposite direction to everybody else which was much better, as the zookeepers will let you go into the enclosures with he birds, iguanas etc if you're in a small group (tip them a dollar or something). We were also allowed to go into the stables, and wandered round for about half an hour with one of the stable hands telling us as much as he could about the horses, in broken english.One thing I would say is that I found it suprising at how little english a lot of the staff could speak. I'm not one of these people that thinks all countries should go out of their way to speak English or anything like that, but seeing as the resort catered for mostly English speaking guests, it was very hard to communicate with about 75% of the staff.So all in all, it was a nice resort - not 5 star, perhaps a 4 star. But the negative things I've commented on will not ruin your holiday, so if you can get a good deal, give it a try, although if I went back to the Dominican, I would definately pay extra to stay on the Carribean side of the island, purely for the snorkelling and swimming.

<Author>gerridee
<Content>A lovely place, beautiful beach We spent 2 weeks here from Nov 11-24th 2004. All we did was relax by the pool and walk on the beautiful near deserted beach. If you're into getting involved and socialising there were games near the pool, a packed lobby bar (with nightly entertainment), a small casino, disco etc., but we went for RR, which we got. The Junior Suite was a good size with 2 rooms - bedroom and sitting area, a bathroom and balcony. Great view of the ocean from where we were and close to the pool/beach. Our room had 2 double beds which we pushed together. Staff were excellent all round, grounds were kept clean (but ponds could do with some work), food was good, did I mention how great the beach was. Never got sick from the food/drink - I think people who go on about this tend to perhaps imbibe a bit too freely. We only had a couple of cocktails for the entire fortnight - we liked the Sirenis Special - a orange based, coconut milk cocktail similar to a Pina Colada. Weather was good on average temperatures of 28-30 degrees (minus a couple of tropical showers here and there and one full day of rain) - sure beats the cold and perrenial grey sky over London. The resort wasn't full when we arrived but was by the time we left. Never felt crowded in the least. There were many French Canadians, Spanish, French and a few UK guests. Not much English is spoken so if you don't speak Spanish, take along a Spanish dictionary/phrase book - it helps. There were a few shops at the front of the hotel compound and shacks on the beach selling paintings, wraps, touristy knick-nacks. Expensive but bargaining expected. A very nice resort, great for families or couples.

<Author>AliciaStevenson
<Content>A thorough review Would I recommend this resort to a friend or stay there again? NO. However, let me start off by saying that my vacation was excellent and that the resort, while questionable, did not result in a ruined vacation. I write this review, my first ever, as an honest heads up to those people considering this resort.1. The pool and beach were excellent and very clean. There was no problem with the pool water as reviews had suggested. I saw them cleaning the pool once in the morning and usually at night. The beach is clean and free of garbage. Although it is important to mention that this side of the island has rougher water compared to bayahibe and the more caribbean locations. The only problem with the pool was the lack of chairs and cushions... you need to be up and staking out your claim on a chair before 6 am to get a spot with an umbrella and cushions.2. The rooms were clean, well stocked and the maid was excellent. Our towels were always fresh and the bed turned down at night.3. The food was definitely a big question mark on this vacation. Breakfast was usually good with decent variety in the buffet. Buffet for lunch and dinner was definitely dependant on the day, good or really bad. The theme restaurants usually had very good food ( I highly recommend the Creperie and Italian) but there is very little description of the food so you take your chances on what is coming. The biggest disappointment with food was the snack bar... you can only eat so many bland fries and burgers.By the way if your from Canada and used to Alberta beef stay away from meat dishes as they are VERY well cooked to kill bacteria because of different food standards in the DR. Steak only comes well done.4. THIS RESORT IS EXTREMELY FAR AWAY FROM EVERYTHING. Trust me the map on your brochure isn't exactly accurate. The resort is next to 'Secrets and nothing else. This will mean very long bus rides to and from the airport as well as any exursions you may take. Usually excursions involve transportation on an open air truck and this can be a very long ride if it starts to rain and the roads suck (trust me, every road has potholes the size of craters). This also means expensive taxi rides to go into the nearest town to shop or look around.5. Because the resort is isolated you have to rely on on-resort entertainment. The night shows are terrible (think junior plays with less set design and plot). So if you don't do the disco or casino bring a book and a good friend to keep you entertained.6. It should also be noted that the Suites and Cocotal sides are not really separate. Both resorts are really just one separated by a long sidewalk and some scummy pools (something to watch out for when stumbling to the room after too much free booze). They share all the same facilities so the only real difference is price. I recommend that if you do want to stay at this resort to choose the Cocotal side as it is cheaper and you get almost the exact same product. Side note: I higly recommend the Outback Safari and Saona Island tours. They were both excellent and very well run. The scuba tours are also great.

<Content>You Get What You Pay for We spent the first week in August at the resort. We had not planned a trip but we got a heck of a deal out of Toronto. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Had a brill time I have just returned 24th August from the Sirenis Cocotal, with my husband, 2 kids aged 9 and 6. We had a good flight to La Romana airport. When you land you then had to queue up outside the airport to get your pay your $10 dollars each person and fill in your temp visa, this was a bit of a nightmare everybody trying to scramble for pens and tables to fill them in. Then came the bus ride to the complex. The bus was air conditioned bus was only small and the roads are horrific, the journey took 1hr and 45 mins which I will tell you was hell you felt every bump and by the time we got to the complex I felt ill. We were greated with a fruit drink and checked in quite quickly. You could of got the bellboy's to take your luggage to the room but my husband and I carried them ourselves.The rooms are quite big ours had 2 double beds and a single in. It was very clean and nicely air conditioned. The maid came every day but sometimes she didnt stock the fridge but my husband would go to the stock room at the end of the floor and get what we needed. We also had a knock at the door at 8.30 am by the maid which some mornings was not welcome. We had clean sheets and towels most days.There is food 24 hours a day if you want it. The buffet restaurant was excellent, plenty of dishes to choose from. We did use the themed restaurants which were also excellent. The only complaint that I had would be that you had to wait for drinks too long in the restaurants, they always brought you fresh water straight away but you had to wait for any other drink. The pool was fantastic with the swim up bar which my kids loved. You could easily get sunbeds but struggled for parasols, if you got up early 7ish you could have got one, we later found out towards the end of the holiday if you tipped the guy in the towel hut at least $20 he would get you your beds and parasol everyday. The beach was beautiful and we went snorkelling which was great. My kids went in the kids club, but it was repetitive and my 9 year old got bored the 6 six year old enjoyed it more. The reps were great girls and were brill with the kids.The entertainment at night is quite repetivite also there are a group of dancers (good ones) which do routines most nights. There is alot of different nationalities so I understand that it is difficult to entertain everybody, but it could do with a couple of professinal shows per week. The animation team were very hard working. There was something to do all day if you wanted and it wasnt pushed in your face if you didnt want to take part.We did 2 trips the outback safari and the marinarium which were both fantastic. I would definately reccommend the marine one you went snorkelling with sharks and rays. A little scary when a shark swam under you but it was worth it.The weather was fantastic we did have a few showers which were quite heavy mostly at night and the ones in the day lasted for 10mins and then it was red hot again.We had a brilliant time and would reccommend this complex to anyone thinking of booking in the south of the Dominican republic.

<Author>hatguytoronto
<Content>Not a 4+ Star Resort If you think you are going to go to the Sirenis Tropical Suites Resort and expect top presentation, great food  great service, think again! Forgetting the bumpy bus ride to the resort (about an hour from the airport along pothole roads) as most resorts will have some sort of bus ride, the Sirenis needs an upgrade too. The Tropical Suites  the Cocotal Resort are actually the same resort which makes this place that much bigger. The walkway from the main reception/buffet building down towards the pool  beach (right through the middle of the resort) are planks of rotting wood and cracked cement with ponds/streams/fountains in the middle filled with dirty water and probably sick fish (lots of algae)! The rooms are spacious but there was mildew in the showers, broken showerheads  cracked tiles. As like the other comments I have read, the maid service is good if you are good to them. The beach we found to be pretty dirty and pretty crowded. If you want a good chair (with cushion), or just some shade, you need to get up pretty early to reserve your spot (no later than 7am I was told). The water was nice though, especially for snorkelling, but be careful of all the coral in the area. The pool area was nice too but almost impossible again to find a chair after 7am. The swim up bars were nice touch but lots of kids in the area if you plan on sitting there.As for the food...the buffets were pretty poor quality and you would be lucky if most of it was warm. At peak times, good luck getting a table! The variety was also lacking, especially at the 2 pool snackbars. Always the same stuff. The themed restaurants were great but getting a reservation to one was not an easy chore either.Overall, we did have a nice time because the weather was fantastic and we went on a few excursions to keep us busy but we were very dissapointed in the class of this resort. We actually rated this resort as a possible 3-star resort.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Place lovely - hotel dissapointing This was the fourth time we have spent our holiday in the Dominican Republic. We love the people, the tranquility and escape from our hectic lives Sadly for us, this hotel turned out to be a disappointment. A good choice of restaurants, but these lacked atmosphere. I still can't understand why the steak house and the French restaurant shared the same 'premises'. On a number of occasions, both buffet restaurants were obviously short staffed. There were many instances were we didn't have knives and forks and when we went and asked the waiter he told us he didn't have any! I'm not sure what he thought we could do. In fairness, the staff were rushed off their feet. My advice to anyone who decides to go there would be to visit the buffet restaurant at the latest 7.45p.m. in order to avoid the rush hour! We found it best to get our own drinks from the bar and take them with us into the restaurant, as five or six times we wern't offered any with our meal - again, due to the fact the staff were so busy, clearing and setting tables. Generally, the food was fine. Also a fairly good snack bar.I was disappointed with the beach. It needed to accomodate guests from the sister hotel (Sirenis Cocatel) as well and subsequenlty was more crowded than we have been used to in the past. Beach huts were provided, but if you wanted one of these you needed to go down to the beach at 6a.m. to claim one or you wouldn't stand a chance. Also, the first week there was a shortage of sunbeds. There wasn't any natural shade from palm trees as these were continually cut back. My husbands' comment was - 'They look like toilet brushes!' If you have children you need to be aware that there were four dogs roaming about the beach. I suspect they belonged to local people but one was a cross rottweiller and obviously more rottweiller than cross. The dogs did seem to be friendly but I couldn't help but be very concerned as there were alot of children on the beach. We did see one of the dogs relieving itself on itself someones beach towel. After that we complained to our holiday rep.The sand under the beach huts was not as clean as we've had in the past. One day I collected a cupful of cigarette ends (this wasn't unusual), a toy soldier, a felt tip pen and eight straws!!!!!!!!!!!. The tide doesn't come in as far as the huts and so there isn't any natural cleansing. Needless to say, people should clear their own rubbish but sadly they don't. I don't smoke and so I didn't find this very nice. Maybe the hotel could consider providing rubbish bags for people to put their rubbish in although plenty opf rubbish bins were provided on the beach itself. If not, then the hotel needs to be responsible for raking the sand daily, although its a shame that people can't be more considerate. It could consider putting polite notices in each 'hut' asking people to care about the environment.The accomodation was good but it was spoiled by the fact our patio door didn't lock and the covers were missing off all but one of our electrical sockets!! THe cable from the TV wouldn't reach the socket and so they had removed the cover and pulled the cable out of the wall. The covers were hanging on the cable, making it look like a charm bracelet. We reported this but it wasn't fixed before we left. If children are to share your room beware of simlar problems. We had very few complimentory toiletries. Over the two weeks we had six soaps, four shampoos and one shower gel. Not bad you might think, Only I didn't take shower gel with me as I intended to buy it there,. Wrong!!! The shop has VERY limited toiletries and nothing at all in the way of medical supplies. In fact it has very little of anything. So make sure you take pain killers and plenty of provision for that holiday tummy! There is a medical centre there but our rep told us it was $60 dollars for a consultation and then you will be charged for medication. Check you holiday insurance - your treatment for that holiday tunmmy could be very expensive. I never did get any shower gel! There are about four other shops there selling clothes, cigars and crafts but you will get around them in five minutes - again very little stock.The entertainment was very good. A choice of a show - the usual Dominican themes and also a piano bar in the lobby at night. This was excellent. There is also a very good reasonably priced internet access. Technology is here at its best - you can get a newspaper from your own country printed out! I've been the hotel is three years old, but I feel it is showing signs of wear. Its own rating is five star although our holiday company rated it as four star. We think three star is nearer the mark. Many facilities are offered but many of them didn't reach the standards that we have had before for similar ratings/cost. We missed tea/coffee making facilities and all the little touches that we've had in the past. Sirenis have a number of hotels in Ibiza and Mallorca. This holiday for us was Spain reaching The Dominican Republic.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>7.5 out of 10 overall i just returned home today from a week's stay at the sirenis tropical suites resort, and had a great time! the bus ride to the resort from the airport was a bit like a safari - over an hour long and over brutal roads and through trees - almost like a jungle. it was very bumpy so if you get car sick take some gravol. once at the resort, the staff greets you with a glass of cold fruit punch which is quite refreshing after the long bus ride to get there. if you are lucky, your room will be ready before you get there. however, we arrived and it was not ready for another hour so we got some lunch. the buffet food that day was horrible. very poor selection and none too appetizing. i ate a plate of mashed potatoes for lunch that day. however when we got our room, the day got a lot better. our room was in the T building and was right on the beach. our patio faced the ocean and had a nice view of palm trees. it was awesome. the beach itself was pretty good - a bit too much coral in some places but still swimmable, and very long. definitely good for long walks. however on either side of the resort's beach boundaries are local markets where they try to suck you in to buy souvenirs. the locals may seem intimidating but they are actually quite friendly. the maid service was great - treat them good with a tip here and there and they will fill your mini bar extra full and give you extra towels. overall the food was the lowest and most disappointing part of the resort. some days it was average and other days i would rather starve than eat what was there. breakfast is by far the best meal of the day. as far as the themed restaurants go, the mexican and chinese were the best. the bartenders are very personable and mix really good drinks. the entire staff there is friendly and work very hard to please their clients. be prepared to get up REALLY early in the morning to grab your beach chairs for the day. they go really fast especially the ones under the huts or right by the pool. the pool was big but not always as clean as i would prefer. the lobby bathrooms are brutal. no airconiditioning and poor ventilation. my favorite part was the disco. the resort has its own club and its great! especially on thursday, friday and saturday nights when the domenican people who work at the resort are allowed to attend. they are the life of the party and are fantastic dancers! would i go back? in a heartbeat! while i was disappointed in the food, i did not go there to eat. i went for a good time, alcohol and sun. those three things are the resort's strong points and i had a great time. i just got home today and already miss it!! if you can get a last minute deal on this resort it is definitely worth it!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A great trip, but a large resort. Was at Sirenis with my wife from June 20-27. I give the resort a good rating for these reasons: the Beach is beautiful, some rock, but plenty of room to swim. The sand is not white, but light gold. The water is a green turquoise, not a blue turquoise. Not very turbulent water. Lots of small fish for snorkling. Many needle-fish. What we really enjoyed was to walk along the beach, miles of it. The only resort near by is the Secrets Excellence. We enjoyed their beach for part of one day. Great if you love larger waves. Next for the staff. Very friendly! We had a very nice suite, 2nd floor wish ocean view.What you should know before deciding on Serinis: Very large complex. Serinis and Cocotal is the same resort. The complex itself is not very cozy. Not enough color to our taste. Bland. Wide open. Even though very remote, no quaintness. Definetely lacking in romantic character. More a family build place. Except for the beach area.Food we found to be bland. The best a la carte was the Mexican, by a long shot. The buffet is average on some nights and worse on others. But probably common with other resorts. Best food: Breakfast buffet, crispy french fries, pinneaples are incredibly tasty, and local Presidente Beer, great dark coffee.At reception, make sure they give you correct Pesos change for your American dollar. Twice I was short-changed.In all, a very good time. You'll enjoy the weather, the beach and the people. If your looking for a romantic getaway, you might consider a smaller resort, or choose, as we did, a low-season period.For an amazing Caribean experience, take the Isla Samoa trip, you'll not regret it, if you can hack the 2 hour bus trip.

<Content>Great Honeymoon Well, we went to the Tropical Suit on the 6th May for our honeymoon and had a wonderfull time. I can see some of the points in the otehr peoples reviews but i guess you can only compere with what your used to. The staff range from a bit arrogant, to helpful and happy. The only staff i found to be a bit 'off' were the reception staff and the guards. All the other staff were helpfull and happy looking. The rooms were good although the air conditioning was a bit weak and the tv was a bit 'hit or miss'. The food in the general 'day to day' restaurant was excellent and the choice was fantastic. The speciality restaurant was ok but nothing special realy. The pool was great and the bar staff at the pool bar were friendly and would mix whatever you like. The grounds are constantly maintained and look great with coconut trees everywhere so you cant forget where you are. The lounge area roof leaked a lot when the rain came down but what do you expect from a hotel in the republic. Drinking unlimited drinks and smoking cigars in the huge entrance lobbies whilst the lines of fans hummed above and the sail cloth canopies flapped in the warm winds made it feel like we were in some 1920s film. The beach is a magic place to be at night looking at the stars and listening to the sea lapping at the sand. All i can say is that if your expecting 'Hilton Hotel' luxury, go to the Hilton, if your expecting a great holiday with sun, loads of white sand, quiet secluded areas to chill out and great food served by friendly staff, then this is the place to be.

<Content>Nice break. Just arrived back from Sirenis Tropical Suites where myself, the wife and two and a half year old daughter spent sixteen days. We booked the holiday last minute off Teletext. we had a great deal by price cutting between firms, saved just over 拢500 inc free ins. for the child. (if its Dom.Rep. your going get the best deal, because if you don`t like it here at least you know that you saved money.) The hotel looked and sounded the best in the brochure for the Dom.Rep. If you want a quite, relaxing holiday this is the place to go. Dom.Rep was not my first choice of the Caribbean Islands to visit its just that it was all there was on offer. i don`t think i`ll be visiting again. But whilst i was here we did enjoy our stay. The flight was around 8 hours from the U.K and the Another hour and 10 mins. to the hotel. At the airport we thought the photo taking was for immigration purposes. its not, they try to sell you a jet lagged, anaemic looking photo of you when you depart. Immigration took a while as you needed to fill in paper work, so have a pen ready and $10.00 to enter. ($20 and second half of form to depart).Airport was a nightmare when we arrived, 4 luggage belts (of which one was broken) and a dozen incoming planes, The baggage halls can cope with one plane at a time, so expect a lot of angry people and reps.On to the hotel its actually two hotels joined as one the other being the Cocotal. The reps. tell you its the cheaper holiday side, this half of the grounds has all the benifits of the Tropical side, ALL INCLUSIVE. the only difference is that the rooms are not to the high standard as Tropical side. From what i seen there is very little between them. The hotel grounds are clean and very neat the only thing that lets it down is the central ponds and its fountains. The beach and the very large swimming pools ( with many depths throughout) are clean and well kept. You`ll notice a difference when you lay arond pool and the beach, There is a nice sea breeze on the beach and you`ll not realise how hot the sun is. So take large amounts of sun tan oil, you`ll need it. (Take it with you as it will cost the earth when you are there, also Note that May is the wet season and lasts for the month) If you want to lay around the pool you`ll need to copy the Germans and get there early with your towel, we noticed that the towels spent more time in the sun than the owner, many times not even seeing the owner. We arrived last week of April and hand ten days of great weather then it rained for three and a half days, a further day and a half of sun and another days rain. We noticed many persons arriving during these wet days and not seeing much sun. Our departure day the forcast for the next week was for more Rain. So there will be a few bad reviews to come on this site. The rooms were cleaned daily and the fridge filled with soft drinks. There is also a t.v with multi language channels. also air con. and bedroom fan. The resturants were okay, only thing annoying was that being from the U.K and Dem Rep being five hours behind we had to eat meals between set times which took time getting used to. Plenty of choice, but found that it does not cater for children very well. My daughter thought Christmas had arrived early when we got her home, she was into the food like there was no tomorrow. But then asked if we could go again. If you are taking a child take some treats with you. again not cheap in Dem Rep. The staff are friendly towards all, if your not polite and curtious dont expect the staff to be otherwise. Plenty of sport on offer if your in a group if not the animation team try there best to get every body involved, I don`t envy there task one bit. They do there best. On the whole a good, quite and relaxing break. I rate the hotel 3 star plus (if Dem Rep. standards rate 5 star i would hate to actually see a 3 star Dem. Rep standard)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good quality family vacation We stayed at this resort for two weeks with our two daughters aged 2 and 4 in April 2004. I thought it was a very good quality resort and we were more than happily satisfied with our stay. The resort is quite remote (an hour from airport or anywhere) and so we did not venture outside the resort the entire 2 weeks.We had a great time and the weather was really superb. Only a few days that were cool and cloudy but the sun always broke through. We stayed in Block B and had a one bedrm which was more than adequate for all of us. The rooms were clean and nicely decorated and we had a terrace. The TV reception was excellent, especially when the girls were tired and wanted to watch the Disney channel.Our bathtub was clogged and with one phone call it was immediately fixed. There are tiny mosquitos that come in at night but we solved that by keeping the light on in the bathroom at night so they all flocked in there and left us alone to sleep. (by morning the heat of the lights left them dead)The grounds were well kept and the beach area was very nice. The pools were excellent for kids. Two huge pools that have a gradual entry for little ones (you can even watch them as you eat lunch from the restuarant), swim-up bars, bridges and so on. The pool was amazing.The beach was golden sand (not the white we expected) but still soft and beautiful.We were generally late risers and ate breakfast around 9:30. By the time we made it to the pool, it was around 10:30-11 and we NEVER once had a problem finding a lounge chair! (or 2 for that matter) If you look around you could always find one or move a few to the area you wanted.Our 4 year old did the kids club a few times and enjoyed it. I don't think it's the best one going but entertains them and keeps them out of the sun. The mini-disco was what they liked best with songs and games for about 1/2 hr. They even participated in a kids show one night which was our daughter's highlight.I thought the evening shows were too late (to take kids to) but were excellent. Really entertaining and the dancers fantastic.The food was more than adequate. The main buffets were great with tons of selection. I can not imagine someone hating everything. Every evening was a different theme and always had a carved meat of the night. Really, the food was so good and perfect for families with kids who don't want what their parents are eating. Tons of fresh, made-to-order pastas, meat dishes, vegetables, fruits, desserts and so on. We tried a few a la cartes and they were ok. Creperie was not bad and a nice change. Chinese was about the same. Even the steak place was good. Only place I would not recomment is Italian...you can get better at the buffet.While there a few things happened...we ran out of diapers! Didn't think this would be a problem but the store on site is ridiculously expensive and does not stock much. Only size diapers were for newborns. So if you have little ones in diapers..bring as much as you need with you. We ended up getting a guy at the front desk (Robert) to buy some for us at a local town. We also ran out of suntan lotion and this costs $45-50 a bottle (CDN) at the local store! No kidding. We bartered on the beach down to about $20, so bring lots of that too.Also, our youngest did a stupid thing and stuffed a button up her nose. The doc on call didn't seem to be there but when my husband went to the front desk and they called, she was there. So sometimes late at night you need to actually announce your visit. Anyways, they got it out.We spent most of our time at the pool, everyday doing the same thing. I would definitely recommend this resort and rate it a 4 star, but suggest going for only one week due to its location. You really can't leave the resort once you're there.I think it's great for families and can't believe the bad reviews I've read. We have travelled extensively and I like to stay at nice places. This was good quality and good fun. You won't be disappointed.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>UNLIKELY TO RETURN My wife and I stayed at Sirenis Tropical Suites for two weeks from 24 March to 7 April 2004. We stayed in Block B next to the main building complex. Our experiences of this hotel are mixed to say the least. The majority of guests during our stay were French, or were French-Canadians. We found these people obnoxiously rude and bad-mannered. Nevermind, onto the review . . .The hotel is large with plenty of facilities and activities to keep you going for any length of stay. However the location of the hotel is somewhat isolated and we did not realise the hotel was literally one hour from the nearest town. The beach was quite picturesque after a short walk, and the pool areas were clean and well looked after. However we soon tired of the daily ritual of having to go to the pool area at 7.00 a.m. every morning in order to stand any chance of getting a couple of sun loungers or a 鈥榯iki umbrellas鈥? What annoyed us a great deal was that people would 鈥榬eserve鈥?their spot and then not even have the decency to show up until mid-afternoon. Our accommodation was spacious, clean and well maintained. No problems with plumbing or mosquitoes. The cleaning staff were friendly and worked hard to make our stay as comfortable as possible. A huge downside was the BIG bugs that entered the room under your door on a night. Keep a large shoe handy to hit them with, or stuff a towel under your door.The food was pretty reasonable and a decent choice on offer. The Gourmet restaurant was good (apart from 40 minute wait for coffee at end of meal). The Chinese received mixed comments from other guests but we found it was very nice. The buffet restaurants had a fair selection but we found this got boring and repetitive towards the end of the stay. We found the buffet restaurant in the main building was better than the one near the beach. The Mexican, Steakhouse and Pizzeria were ok. The Mediterranean (dodgy seafood) and Creperie were absolutely terrible due to the lack of any quality in the food and the diabolically poor service. We found the service in most restaurants to be poor. No matter how much we were polite, or smiled, said 鈥榩lease鈥?and 鈥榯hankyou鈥? or even tried to converse with the odd bit of Spanish, the service in some of the restaurants was appalling. I have found in most countries politeness and a smile go a long way to getting good service 鈥?it counted for nothing here. The hotel was by no means full or busy but waiters, who were usually downright miserable, often ignored us and the service was VERY slow. I have experienced 鈥淒ominican Time鈥?before, but never like this. We lost count of the times we were overlooked by the drinks waiters, or the occasions we had to wait thirty or forty minutes before someone took our order. However, the bar staff were excellent. The bars were well stocked, with several international brands and you did not wait long to get served. The staff always had a smile and made you feel welcome.During our stay we booked ourselves on three excursions. The first was the Outback 鈥楽afari鈥?which was excellent and well worth it. It gave you a flavour of real Dominican life in the countryside and the guides were informative and very amusing. We were entertained all day. We also booked to go on a boat trip to Saona Island but it was cancelled due to poor weather/choppy sea. We were given the chance of going on the next scheduled trip (next day) but had other things planned and got our money back. The last excursion was a shopping trip to the nearest 鈥榣arge鈥?town of Higuey, which was interesting enough and at least got you out of the hotel for a few hours. We鈥檝e been to the Caribbean (and the Dominican Republic) on numerous occasions in recent years and this hotel is definitely not of 4/5 star standard. We enjoyed our holiday and the time together, and at the end of the day a holiday is what you make of it. We are not moaners or have unrealistic expectations - it's just that we've been to a few places, stayed in 'good' hotels and experienced 'good' service in the past. I know this hotel is relatively new and it would have been a 4 or 5 star rating perhaps five or six years ago. However i feel it certainly should not be given such a rating when you consider there are better hotels in the Dominican Republic, with a better location, better accommodation, better food, and far better staff. It is unlikely we would return to this hotel or recommend it to our friends and family.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Nice Trip We just returned from the Serenis Tropical on April 16 after a one week stay. Let's start with the basics, this is not North America, if you want gourmet food stay in Florida where you can dine at the Ritz (and probably pay the same amount for one dinner that you would for a week's stay at this resort). How was the food at the Tropical? By picking and chosing you can generally find something you like in the buffet style cafeteria (I think I ate more fruit during the week I was down there then I have in the last six months). If possible, make a few reservations when you arrive at the a la carte restaurants (I tried the steak house, which was surprisingly good, and the Chinese food restraunt, which I found so,so). If you wait too long to make reservations, they are booked up most nights. We also tried Il Giardinetto (which is a pay as you go, $20 US pp, for a lobster dinner), this was also decent.I must say the serving staff was always very pleasant and try their best to provide good service. Were they always beaming with big smiles, no, but when you work in a huge hotel cafeteria feeding thousands of people a day who can expect that? We do advise tipping the serving staff. They really appreciate the gesture and will provide attentive service in return.The resort itself was gorgeous, very well maintained and groomed each morning. The room was clean and generally had all the amenities required for our North American lifestyles. (Note, the remote for the television has to be obtained at the front desk). We had a slight problem with our airconditioning not working properly when we arrived, I reported it and 10 minutes later the problem was fixed.As we arrived late (10:30 p.m), we were unable to get a key for the room safe until the next morning as the office at the front desk was closed.Before we left, my wife gave the maid some shoes and clothing that she no longer wanted. The maid was extremely appreciative, but it was necessary for my wife to fill out a form and sign it, indicating what items she was giving to which maid. I guess this is to ensure that they are not accused of stealing. (So if you wish to leave any articles of clothing behind for the maid, make sure you see her and get the form, if not, she won't be able to accept it.)The beach is nice, a fair amount of topless sunbathers (old and young), so if you're uptight about these things it may not be the place to stay. There is no doubt that if you want a good spot on the beach with some shade you have to get out there early in the morning and mark your spot with towels on the chairs (7-7:30). The breeze on the beach was fantastic, swept in from the ocean and made sitting in the 30+ degree heat pleasant. There were quite a few kids, my wife and I do not have children, but we never really found this an issue. On the whole, the kids seemed to stay by the pool.My wife did the stretch and aquafit class daily. She enjoyed it, but noted that, like the dancers in the nightly shows, the instructors/dancers are self-taught, not professionals. She also went snorkelling daily. There are some coral reefs in the water (not spectacular, but fun none the less).The only real problem we encountered was regarding late checkout. We had to be out of the room by noon, but were not leaving the resort until 6:00 p.m., so we paid $40US for late check-out (which only gives you an additional 4 hours - to 4 p.m.) Make sure they re-activate your room key. We found out the hard way when we came back at 3 p.m. from the beach to get ready, and could not get in the room. It took 30 minutes to sort it out with the front desk, then they refused to give us additional time for 4 of us to get ready. They advised that if we took longer we would have to pay more. As the clock was ticking, we decided not to argue at that point and get ready. However, we took it up with our Signature rep, Franklin, when he arrived at 5:30. In the end, we got our $40 back.On the whole, we had a wonderful time and would go back again. Just keep in mind that while this is a 4-5 star resort in the Caribbean, that does not translate to a 4-5 star North American hotel. They do the best they can with what they have. If you keep expectations realistic you'll have an enjoyable vacation.

Thats all I will say about that, I would like this review to make it to print. On April 1st seven of us booked a Taxi and went shopping in Higuey, the cost for the taxi was $65 which wasn't bad considering one that was offered at the resort was $25 per person. The food was really good and the service at both the buffets and the restaurants was really good, they were friendly and always had a smile. I had taken a list of Spanish sayings and tried using them whenever possible. The staff were always impressed that we tried to comunicate in their language. I found a lot of people didn't realize we were going to their country and we should try and speak their language. After all if Spanish speaking people came to tour our tourist areas, I'm sure they would try and learn our language.  The bar staff were great. This is the first resort I've been to that the main lobby bar had 7 bar tenders working. I've been used to seeing 2 at a time at most other resorts. It didn't matter if it was 10:00 a.m. or 10:00 p.m. they always made jokes and laughed and carried on with everyone. The pool bar and the other bars always had a full range of drinks and lots of staff. This resort was one of the first I've seen with a bar menu and I'm sure there were over 30 speciality drinks on it.  There were shows at the out door theatre and some nights there was also enterainment at the main entrance. This was a nice gathering place. The ladies waiting tables were a nice touch. They would come by clear the tables and take drink orders.  We also dropped by the on site casino, I tried to stay clear of it as much as possible. We also did our shopping at the shops on the beach, it's a lot of fun to haggle with the local vendors,they tend to expect it. We met up with Yimmey(Jimmy) cheappy, cheappy. Would do your heart good to check them out.  The pool is really nice and there is some deep areas, some places over 6' ( 2 meters) deep . Lots of shaded areas. The beach was nice the shaded areas were gone by 7:00 a.m. You had to be up early to capture one of these places. The ocean at the beach had a bit of an under tow on rough days, not a good place to leave a young child unattended. As well there was no life guard at the beach, however there was one at the pool.  The animation staff tried there best to keep everyone entertained during the day, anything from dancing to arobics and all types of games. both at the pool and the beach.  Like all good things our trip came to an end on Sunday. We left for the airport at 8:30 a.m. the ride took about 50 minutes. When we arrived we couldn't believe the line ups, it took from 9:30- 11:30 to get our tickets and go through customs. Air Transit Flight 867 was delayed 30 minutes but other than that the flight was great. There was around 100 empty seats, once the head count was completed we were able to sit where ever we wanted. Once again the flight crew were really friendly, we had a great flight.  I would be glad to answer any questions.

I couldn't ask for anything more. They truely surprised me and this shows that they are good-hearted people. I can't imagine why anyone would ever have complaints regarding them. We had an amazing vacation here and would recommend it to anyone. We would definitely come back!

<Content>Punta Cana Vacation March 2004 I went to Punta Cana, Dominican Republic in March 2004 for one week and my stay there was very relaxing and peaceful. I will start from the beginning. The airplane ride is tight and a little uncomfortable but really what do you expect. I thought the food was decent with plenty to eat, I mean you can't expect a hot cooked meal on the plane. The flight attendents were very kind and helpful. The bus ride to the hotel was not what I expected, from reading previous reviews I was expecting a rusted out old bus with no a/c, however it was a very large newer bus the tinted windows and a/c and it even had a bathroom. I thought the ride itself was very peaceful a few bumps here and there but nothing we are not used to in Regina, Sask. They were actually fixing lots of the roads. Checking in to the hotel was very quick all of the workers there are very friendly. we checked in they gave us a map and explained where our room was and within half an hour of being in our room our luggage was there. The rooms were very large and clean, we got oceanview just like we requested. We were on the Sirenis tropical side the Cocatol is the sister hotel only it dosen's have a living room. The ocean is beautiful very aqua bluey-green with palm trees on the beach (there is reefs in the water but there is also lots of open space to swim). There are lots of chairs to suntan on but if you want some shade you do have to get up around 7:30 to put a towel under it (but who wants to sleep in anyway). The pool was very clean and it was never packed because it is so large. The grouds are kept immaculate I couldn't believe it there is literly not a wilted flower around or a rock out of place they have gardeners everywhere cleaning up. The ponds and statues are georgous to admire. The lobby is large with plenty seating. There are two buffets with a wide variety of food and I think around 7 or 8 a la cartes I recommend the steak house, seafood, and Italian I also tried the mexican and chinese and they were good to. I was prepared with pepto, immodium and tums because of reviews I read before I went and I never once got any stomach pain (it still dosen't hurt to bring medicine just in case). I also brought bug spray and I never saw one mosquito. I really enjoyed the theatre we went every night. The animation team there are so crazy. They are very easy to understand most of them speack spanish, english, french and a few other languages. The one guy sang an eminem song that was just awesome. All the staff was very nice. I never travelled with kids but the kids club was great, watching them with the children was just amazing they were so good with them. They have may activities by the pool for example spanish lessons, or you could learn there dance the meranga and much more. There are markets on both sides of the beach and some in front of the hotel the are expensive, but you can talk them down pretty good. I wanted there two ceramic hand painted suns for me and my cousin and they wanted 30 dollars for two and we got them for 12 dollars for two. I enjoyed my stay and the Sirenis tropical and recommend it. Some tips I do have is when bargaining at the market pay what you think its worth start walking away and they will run after you and finally give in. Bring lots of sunscreen and lotion, you are so much closer to the equater there that the sun is that much more intense and the lotion is for after you go in the sun so you don't peel. Bring americaln money or pesos thy usally don't take canadian and exchange it before you come because you will get a better rate. Bring a plug adapter there outlets are different (I think you can buy them at the market in front of the lobby for 3 dollars). The food is good but it is still different, the have lots of veggies and fruits but the dressings are bland so bring your own salad dressing the also only have butter so bring peanut butter of jam belive me its the little things you miss the most. Make sure you luggage isn't over skyservice charges 5 dollars for every pount you are over (which you can't blame them I still had 10 pounds to spare in my suitcase). This is a relaxing resort there is not much to do out of the resort unless you want to spend quite a bit on a cab ride. There is not much partying, they do have a disco but it is not very wild in there. So if you are looking to shop and explore and party hard don't come to this resort. Also if you want a small resort don't come here this resort is huge it took us 15 minutes to walk from our room the the theatre (of course our room was all the way on the other end). I would recommend getting a massage at the market on the left side the charge 15 dollars for half an hour and it was awesome. There are lots of topless girls and guys in speedos all shapes and sizes and don't worry about how your going to look in you bathing suit. Take lots of pictures there are lots of little lizards, bats at night, peacocks and flimingos and most of all enjoy a great trip of relaxation and getting served.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hola Hola, Coca Cola!! We (Me, Wife and 2 kids aged 15 and 12) spent 2 weeks here between 11/2/4 and 25/2/4, and had a very relaxing time - just what we were looking for.The ride from the airport was something like 75 minutes. I agree the roads are bad but that is just a 20 minute section for the worst bit - still better than all the roadworks and heavy traffic back in London!The general roads are difficult - and I would only recommend the most adventurous hire a car.The actual resort area is huge, and very well landscaped. Check-in was smooth. Rooms are good - fairly spacious.Pool is massive - never felt crowded, as you could move to different areas.Food was OK. All 4 of us found something we liked 3 times a day - and the buffet is well presented with a fairly good choice.A La carte restaurants are OK too, but not as special as some others I have been to. However, makes a nice change to be brought all the food, as opposed to the buffet system.Drinks: red and white wines served with meals are awful. They may be watered down - as I have never tasted bottled wine that poor. Local spirits are poor if you drink them as shots/shooters, but are great in cocktails. If you want straight drinks, they do keep the good international brands under the counter. I suggest a small tip to your barman as a courtesy. Just ask nicely and he will serve you Dewars, JB, Baileys, Cointreau, Smirnoff etc etcStaff/Locals: We thought the people were lovely. It's a shame to read so many reviews saying howrude they are -it's just not true. Regrettably, it is fellow guests that are rude. I saw many examples of guests barking orders to staff in very rapid English, and expecting an instant 'perfect' response. This was also accompanied without any 'please' or 'thank you' If you want to get on, try a smile first. Learn some very simple Spanish words (hello, goodbye, please, thank you, how are you?, I am well thanks, Beer, White wine, Red wine, etc etc) Speak a little slower, and remember this is the Caribbean, not London, Chicago or Winnipeg. Lastly, we are all on holiday to enjoy the manana culture - so worry about things tomorrow!!We thought trips were expensive, but the resort is very remote - and it's good to see new things. Saona Island trip was Ok - very beautiful beaches and sea, nice boat trip. Outback Safari (or Bavarro Runners equivalent) was also OK - if you want to see some of the real Dom Rep. Some trips will take you out for a brief trip to a local school. Consider taking some exercise books/A4 pads/pencils as gifts (the local parents have to buy these - so it's a nice gesture)Sea by the resort is a little disappointing, but remember this is this is the Atlantic side, not the Caribbean. Lots of little reefs to look at fish etc compensate a little. Water is warm, and reasonably safe for kids too. Beach is good, and you can walk a long way in either directionResort is huge, so get used to walking a lot! Not a bad thing when you are eating so much, and why be in a hurry anyway - you are on holiday!Weather was great. We went in dry season, so mozzies were not a problem either.Would we go again? Yes. Probably prefer to visit a resort on the south (Caribbean) side. I would not rate this resort as 5 star. The buildings and grounds are 4 to 5 star, but the overall effect is nearer to 3 or 3+ stars for me.I am very glad we went - and hope you enjoy your time.

<Content>Wonderful resort..go back in a heart beat My wife and I just returned from our vacation at the Siernis Tropical. Many are shy and do not speak good english...perhaps those who complained mistook that for a bad attitude or perhaps were the ones who were really being rude. The beach is very clean and you can walk barefoot for miles and miles. The food, well lets just say we don't eat that good at home. We never ate in any of the sit down restaurants preferring to stick with the buffets. There is a wonderful variety of food and the offerings are very tasteful. Snacks are always available, you just can't go hungry at this place what so ever. Those who complained about the food on here really and truthfully have a weak case. The bars offer a wide assortment of cocktails and blender drinks. You'll have trouble deciding what to order next. The beer tastes remarkably like ours in Canada and is a wonderful compliment to the afternoon heat. You will be surprised how quickly you get your drinks with a $1 tip here and there. There are activities all day on the beach and if you find yourself being able to stay up past 10 pm (beer, heat and food seem to make this task next impossible) there is entertainment nightly.I could go on and on with the accolades. If you booked here and have some reservations after reading some of the reviews on here...don't...you'll love it.

<Author>Amanda253
<Content>Great Holiday My boyfriend and I just returned from a one week stay at the Sirenis Tropical. (Before we left, we were unclear on the relation between the Sirenis Tropical and the Sirenis Cocotal - the Tropical and the Cocotal constitute one resort - the Tropical rooms having one bedroom suites and the Cocotal having standard rooms).Positive:The grounds were very impressive, especially at night. The rooms were large and clean. The staff were very friendly.Beach: beautiful and well kept. Great snorkling just a few meters into the water. Walk to Secrets (a nearby resort) and body surf (the water is much more wavy there).Food: We ate 6 of our 7 dinners at a la cartes. We found most of these to be very enjoyable, particularly the Mexican resturant, the Creperie, the Pizzeria and the Italian restaurant. The Vegeterian restaurant has good food but was in a brightly lit room within the main buffet itself, and as such I found the atmosphere unpleasant. We did not find the Steakhouse food to be very tasty. We did not eat at the Chinese, Mediteranean, or Giardinettos resturants, mostly because they were always booked up when we tried to reserve them. Advice: eat as many dinners as you can at the a la cartes. We ate one dinner at the buffet - it was crowded and we anticipated that it would get repetitive and boring were we to eat there every night. If you're willing to take later reservations (ie 9:30), you shouldn't have a problem getting reservations - we never rushed to get into the reservation line up.Santo Domingo: we went on the day trip to Santo Domingo and it was well worth it. Santo Domingo is a large and interesting city, with history I did not know about (ie its connection with the Columbus family).Negative:The house wine is absolutely awful (both red and white). Advice: Bottled wine is available for purchase with your meal; however, during the week we were there the resort was sold out of the more reasonably priced red wine. Important: If you do buy wine, do not pay in US dollars, as you will be charged a very poor conversion rate (worse than the front desk exchange rate). Either charge the wine to your room and then pay on your credit card or pay in pesos.Front desk never had any change, ever. Advice: bring lots and lots of small US bills, as well as pesos. If you run out, go to the bell boys, who have lots of change on them and will happily break your larger bills for a small tip.Watersports staff: There is a $15 snorkling trip the hotel offers, where you get taken out to the middle of the ocean to snorkle. You go to a hut by the watersports section to sign up. Our trip was supossed to leave at 1:00 - we did not leave until after 2:00. Further, we were given no advice on how to select and put on our equipment, nor were we given any instruction regarding safety. Our boat driver could not speak English at all, and when I saw how wavy the water was where he took us, I became concerned for our safety. When we finally snorkled, there wasn't much to see (it was better at the resort beach). Overall, I was unimpressed with the organization of this trip. Advice: this is not a trip for beginner snorklers. Be assertive with the staff.Lounge chairs: In our experience, we could not go out after 8am and expect to get adjustable lounge chairs. These are highly desirable, because the flat lounge chairs the hotel has are uncomfortable. Advice: go out early in the morning - no later than 7am - and put some of your belongings (towels are sufficient) on some chairs to reserve them for later). I don't regard this as playing fairly, but it was necessary to get chairs at this resort.Road to resort: very bumpy road that takes about an hour to negotiate - made me motion sick. Advice: take some Gravol - travelling the road is worth it.Meal times: For people facing a time change (ie Vancouverites lose 4 hours), the first few breakfasts at the resort may be difficult to attend, because the main buffet closes at 10am (6am Vancouver time). While there is a snack buffet open shortly thereafter, it has a very limited selection. Advice: The buffet breakfast is worth it to attend, so try to make it.

<Author>GuntherMeister
<Content>A Great Week Away Well, after reading so many reviews about this place prior to our trip, we had to laugh. We just came back from a great week away and can understand most of the comments made about the resort. Ultimately we recognized the fact that a lot of people like to complain about things and make mountains out of molehills... The key to an enjoyable time here is to go in with the right expectations - if you know what you've signed up for, it can be easier to accept. Here is our take:(1) Skyservice provided a safe and on-time flight, despite the fact that you will be crammed into the plane and will have to pay for any beverages. Unfortunately this is becoming all too common with airlines... (2) The bus ride from the airport to the resort is very bumpy and entertaining to say the least. I thought that the hour went by quick because you get a chance to see the country. It makes the streets in Toronto seem like you're driving on glass... (3) The resort itself was well kept and the rooms were great. We felt right at home and thoroughly enjoyed the pools. Yes, if you want a good seat at the pools, you have to wake up early - but well worth the effort. For whatever reason, we did not experience the muskito problem that everyone else seemed to encounter... (4) Yes, the food is good but not great. By the end of the week we were ready for a home cooked meal. But isn't it always that way after a vacation?Overall the service was excellent - they always tried to go that extra mile to help out and were not at all slow paced or rude as some had suggested. They went out of their way to have fun with our 3 year old son and always had a smile to offer. It was clean, nicely maintained and well run. We would recommend this resort to anyone with a family or who just want to get away for a great week of sun and swimming. Enjoy!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>definitely not 4, 4+ or 5 star rating My husband, myself and out daughters (18 and 14) returned from the Sirenis today. We were extremely disappointed. Firstly, we flew with Skyservice, extremely crammed, have to pay for all extras including water or snacks. The ride from the airport to the resort is a good one hour long and extremely bumpy, huge, huge potholes. The resort is clean, well maintained and most of the staff is friendly and try hard to communicate. We had trouble with our shower and they fixed it right away. The beach is dark sand with lots of tree roots exposed, and not very well maintained. Lots of loungers on the beach but it is also very crowded. The water is rough and not a nice aqua blue colour. The pool is huge and clean. Very limited seating around the pool unless you get up really early to reserve your chairs. There are lots of different places to eat however the food is not really that good. We did enjoy our dinners at the Italian and Chinese restaurants though. The buffet is pretty simple with very limited choices. Even after three days you get tired of the same things. For the most part the entertainment was pretty good. Had a couple of shows they could do without. The activity crews try really hard to get people to participate in things like spanish lessons, aerobics (beach and water), volleyball, dancing and silly games. Actually, quite entertaining. This was our first time to Punta Cana and we'll definitely think twice before we go again. If we do go again I will definitely stay in the Bavara Beach area. We went on a snorkeling excursion there and we were quite impressed. I do realize everyone has different likes and dislikes and some people are definitely very impressed with this resort but if you have been to 4+ and 5 star resorts you know this definitely isn't one.

<Author>boobooboo
<Content>Great Holiday We travelled to Punta Cana on January 15th for a two week stay.First off if you have a choice travel by any other airline instead of Skyservice. The flight was very uncomfortable. As in an earlier review sardine packed states it all. Also they charge you for absolutely everything including water.The resort itself is wonderful. Sheets changed daily, and our maid made us so many animals and birds out of towels that we could have opened a zoo.There are alot of mosquities so do bring some bug repellent. Also they spray for the bugs at some very strange times so if you hear what sounds like a lawn mower be prepared to evacuate the area.The beach is beautiful and well kept. Good swimming areas, but some rocks deeper in the water. Most days were very calm, but there is a reef so some waves can be expected.The pool is huge and very clean, but they do use a lot of chemicals to keep it that way so if you have sentivive skin beware.Food was very good although it got to be a bit too repetitious after the first week. There is a little beach restrauant located next to the resort on the beach. Treat yourself and have a lobster dinner there, well worth the price.Staff was very friendly, a small tip here and there goes a long way in securing good service.Lots of tours and excursions offered. We did the Sonana Catamaran tour. It is 1 1/2 hours on a bus to get there, but this also gives you a small glimpse into some of the small villages and the larger town of Higuey. The beach that the catamaran takes you to is gorgeous.Also don't forget that you can order international drinks at no additional charge. Just be sure and ask for it by name, Barcardi, Dewars etc.All in all a very enjoyable holiday with just a few quirks.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic value We stayed at the Tropical Suites from 7th to 21st Jan. We've read lots of the reviews on the Sirenis on this website and our overall opinion was suprise, did some people expect? Its obviously not a real 5 star property like you would get in Europe or North America, but it is a very good all-inc resort. Yes this is a very remote location upto 90 minutes from airport on very bumpy road, but when you get there you have got literally miles of unspoilt beachfront with only 'Secrets Excellence' resort to share it with and they're 1 mile away. Their is a wide choice of restaurants and the buffet changes daily along with the quality, but remember this is allinclusive if you dont like something about your meal go and get a different one its free!!! The grounds, pool and beach areas are huge but still immaculately maintained. All the bar staff are great but like any place some speak better English than others. Be patient and polite and they'll do anything they can. There is proper organised beach activities, kids clubs and entertainment every night plus a Casino on site you've just got to read the notice boards to find it all. Don't believe the brochure the Sirenis isn't on the Caribean side of the island but the sea was warm and clear and the beach was fine golden sand. If you really want to see the true Caribeean side go on one of the boat trips to Saona island, everyone we spoke to loved it. Best tip is if your there when its busy take your pool towels (that the hotel provides) back to your rom at night so that you can put it out early. The pool towel attendant doesnt start till 9a.m. so if you've not bagged your sunlounger by then all the best spots are gone. 2nd tip, book for 3 or 4 days at a time for the 6 A'La Carte restaurants, is saves you queing 45 minutes each morning. Last tip take US dollars and Dominican Pesos, some thing you get a great deal for USD but a lot of things are charged in Pesos especially at the airport and hotel and their conversion rate to Dollars is criminal. We had no complaints and would recommend this resort to anyone who wants good value. If you want proper 5* go somewhere else but you'll have to pay a lot more though.

Nylon netting is much more appealing.The beach is nice -- it was difficult to tell about the the water, as it was fairly windy while we were there, so we didn't spend much time in the water. It is a holiday destination to relax at, do nothing read a few books and recharge your batteries. If you want fun and excitment and lively atmosphere then don't book a holiday here it is the opposite.It is not a 5 star resort, in Europe, with a little bit of work, it may just about get 4 stars. The size of the pool has to be seen to be believed. The grounds of this hotel are shared on the same site as the Serenis Cocatel Beach but it is run as one hotel. We found that the main al a cart restaurant was better than the other restaurants on the site Steak House and Mexican were OK. The one that you have to pay 11 dollars for Giardinettos was excellent, the lobster delicious.For us Brits one failing was the lack of tea in a morning, they ran out on our 3rd day and never restocked so take you own tea bags to breakfast. I did manage to find a plentyful supply behind the top bar in reception, but keep that to yourself.
