<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent Resort We just returned from a wonderful two week holiday at the Sirenis Suites in Punta Cana. The resort was excellent in all respects from the happy, helpful staff, beautifully maintained grounds, picture perfect beach lined with palms, to the lovely clean and spacious rooms. The food was outstanding in variety, taste, selection, and presentation.Our daughter was married at the gazebo on site in a simple beautiful ceremony. We all enjoyed our stay and have incredible memories and photos.We felt very safe and were not bothered by anyone trying to sell us anything on the resort. This was a pleasant difference from our experience in Puerto Plata.This is a family oriented facility where one can really relax and enjoy the sand, surf and sun. The bus ride to and from the resort was an experience but gives you a sense of the way the people really live, especially if you travel by daylight.The airport was lovely and surprising to arrive at; however, leaving was a different story. It was hot, crowded and frustrating. Departures were very unorganized and we had more than one anxious moment. At one point, the board said our flight had already departed causing a flurry of panic!The only downside to our trip was the outrageous excess baggage charges by Skyservice and uncomfortable cramped flying conditions.If you are travelling Skyservice, beware! You are only permitted 20 kg of luggage per person which includes the weight of the luggage itself! It doesn't matter if you stay one week or two, it is all the same allowance. Also, your carry on luggage is subject to overweight charges! Take out that bottled water and leave anything you don't need to bring back if you are close to the limit!Liquor is included in the weight allowance so it might be best to purchase it after you check your bags at the airport. We have travelled with many airlines throughout the world for years and never had a problem previously.Domestic flights within Canada on other carriers allow 70 kg per bag and allowed 2 pieces each!We bought school supplies, chocolate, candy, personal hygiene products etc. for the children and workers. On top of the $140 Cdn dollars in overweight charges, it was very expensive. Skyservice was the grinch that stole Christmas.We like to visit different places so likely wouldn't return to Sirenis Resort in Punta Cana, but do highly recommend it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>mixed feelings Went to sirenis tropical suites on 05/11/2003 for a two week holiday after previously going to the dom rep the two previous years.First and foremost I have to say I do not agree with sirenis rating of 5* due to the previous hotels I have been to. Sirenis has a lovely quiet beach where you may walk a good 15 minutes either way without seeing another hotel,the sands are golden and sea is blue but this hotel lacks that special carribean something I've had before. Although suites are spacious, they are dark,and we were so near to palm groves that every night the mosquitos would come under the door to attack! Pool is kept mostly clean, only draw back being the matresses for the sunbeds being sponge and once wet, never dry. In comparison to the other hotels food is good, although buffet is not the best.You can usually find a piece of pizza or have a chef make a basic pasta if there is nothing that takes your fancy.Themed restaurants are good-italian, steak house, mexican, fish and chinese. They say you are allowed to each once a week but we got there nearly every night! be early to reserve though(especially the steak house which is filled quickly).I would say of the three hotels I've been to this accomodated my fussy stomach the best, plus theres snacks at the pool bar all day long. Only thing I would comment on is the service of the wait on staff at buffet lunches and dinner. They are slow to serve and often make you feel like you are rude for asking for a drink with your meal. on more than three occasions we had finished our meals before the drinks had arrived!! All in all nice holiday if you've never experienced the dominican flavour before, but, if you're not first timers to the island I'd say you'll miss that magic you become accustomed to. I personally wouldn't go back to this hotel, but I'm looking forward to looking for a hotel with the beautiful lay outs you can get elsewhere, and the friendly staff who can't do enough for you, BUT I WILL be looking for somewhere that can be on parr with the food of the sirenis tropical suites.

<Content>See you next year!!!!!!! plane journey and airport. Me and my sister have recently returned from a two week visit to sirenis, this has been our 2nd year here and would go back time and time again. our holiday started on the 13th October the plane touched down around 5pm (dominican time) from Gatwick after a long 9hr journey sadly it was raining when we arrived but we were determined that would not put us off. As we walked into the airport we were greeted by friendly airport staff who persisted on trying to take our luggage to the coach for us but experience from the previous year reminded us not to as they want tipping but the walk to the coach is literaly centimeteres away.Coach journey and first impression. I must admit the coach journey to the hotel is hell, as after a nine hour flight the last thing you want to do is get on a coach for a following two hours, maybe this was because it was dark and wet and we couldn't see the real dominican life and friendly waves and blowing kisses as you travel through their poor but friendly towns. When we arrived at the hotel (wow!) we had tears in our eyes as it was so fantastic. we were welcomed with a complimentary drink, the cases were left for the porters to take to your room a small tip is appreciated. After check in we made our way to our room. We were tired from the long journey so decided to have a quick look around to see if we recognised any of the animation team from the previous year and to see if everything was still as wonderful. Food is available 24/7 but to be honest we just wanted a good night sleep.The hotel. If you are expecting the Ritz then this is the place for you everything is immaculate and you wouldn't believe the size of the place! The room had two double beds a bath/shower, mini bar stocked daily with soft drinks and colour tv. We were lucky enough to have a sea view but most importantly it was very clean. The lobby is huge with marble flooring and has a double sided bar in the middle so you drunks don't have to worry about queuing for your all inclusive drinks. This is where our favourite bar staff Mario and Fidor worked. This is also where the main restaurant is im not joking there is food to suit everyone! not all to our taste but we soon found out what we liked by the end of the holiday.The pool and beach and Entertainment. The pool opens at nine but people are in there from seven. This is the biggest pool i have ever seen in my life and contains two pool bars, say hi to Esteban for us he works in the cocotal side poolbar bar if you give him a small tip he will make sure you are well looked after he never stops smiling and dancing. If you have any cds you want him to play round the pool he will be happy to, and by the end of the day will know all the words. All the entertainment takes place around the pool 9 o clock spanish lessons with the lovely Manuel and stretches on the beach with the beautiful Carmen Electra! Crazy games are at 10 o clock on the beach with MC Jesus you must take part as it could entail a medal and certificate in the evening shows and were also very funny. At 11:00 there will be a merengue lesson on the beach with all the entertainers followed by the club dance i can guarantee you will know this by the end of your stay. Lunch is between 12:00 and 3:00 so you can either relax by the pool or on the beach or go and stuff your faces. The beach is better than you can imagine and is like being in paradise you can take part with the watersports or swim in the turquoise waters. If you are taking small children then there is a fantastic kids club entertainer called Angelica who will take care of your naughty naughty children (as she says, )she is the sweetest person and is very funny. If you fancy going to the gym Ishmel will look after you and he also does the aerobics on the beach on an afternoon (a very sweet guy) .Evening Entertainment. After filling your faces or boozing at the bar! its show time folks! Entertainment starts at 10:00 in the theatre BEWARE to put on your mosquito sprays as these could ruin your holiday and cost you a bomb at the doctors. The theatre is where you meet all the entertainers Ricky Martin(very funny) Manuel. Jesus, Naomi Campbell, Carmen Electra, Henry, Roberto (great dancer), Ronald, Eminiem (dont know his real name but he is very good at doing the languages and he Loves-his-job. Mimi, mira, and Condorito the clown (shorts dude). After the show you can either go back to the lobby until 12:00 thats when the bar closes or hot foot it down to the disco untill 2:00am no doubt the entertainers will be in there dancing the night away they never get bored of it.There is also a sports bar in the resort this is where Antonio works behind the bar he is very friendly and has a lovely smile. there is a pooltable and foozball in here.I would recommend this hotel to anyone and will see you next year back at the Sirenis Hotel!!!Jade and Kelly. Sorry my friend as pleasant and effective as you were yourself it was your task to ensure that your front desk staff met your requirements.Food:We found the 2 restaurants we went to a mixed bag. You had to reserve you dinner location between 8:00-10:00 am or eat in the buffet, and you had to go down each day to do so. Your received one advance booking for a restaurant of your choice which you could make any day between 4:00 and 8:00 PM, but only in person. Ironically the person who handled the bookings had the best customer service skills. We also found out they take very seriously the warning that unless you show up within 5 min of your appointment it will be cancelled. This was for me one of the more unpleasant aspects. When Im on vacation I dont want to live by the clock.We used our advanced reservation of the Seafood restaurant, which was quite good, and we made one appointment for the steak house, which was passable. In the end I would say the buffet was the superior experience. If you go I recommend using your reservation for the seafood restaurant and not bothering with the rest, though I do have to admit that we didnt try them all mainly because we didnt want the hassle of booking appointments.However the buffet offered a reasonable selection of items with some variation on certain dishes coming up everyday but with new main courses. Personally I found the fruit and fish dishes to be the best. Though the pasta we often very good and was made to order in a skillet with a choice of varying ingredients. The mango was probably the best fruit I had ever had with the pineapple being the next best. It probably helped that my companion showed me how to select the best pieces of Mango.I particularly enjoyed the Monte Alto coffee that was served at the bar as a latte. It was a smooth yet flavorful coffee.Once we settled on the buffet we enjoyed our dinning.LandscapeThe landscapers were hard at work on the resort every morning. I found for the most part it was a very nice effect that was created. I noted a number of people mentioned the stagnant ponds in the middle of the causeway. I found as general rule almost all the ponds and pools in the resort we visited had the green sandy muck at the bottom of the pools. Some of the fountains were under construction when we were there and it looked like the eventually plan was to have the water roll down towards the beach end.The beach was fairly well groomed and that is where I spent most of my time, though the pool was very enjoyable as well. The sand on the shore was reasonably free of debris and the one morning I went early I was pretty certain they had taken some effort to rake the beach as it was clearer and much more fluffy.Despite some of the in my opinion minor issues we ran into the whole stay was quite pleasant. I would recommend this for people who are looking for a reasonably priced vacation and are willing to forgo the restaurants and live with the occasional hassle with the front desk. I personally had an excellent time and would go back if the opportunity presented itself.Another word of warning. If you dont like a road trip from the airport dont go. Its about an hour from the airport because of the horrible condition of the road. If you want to go somewhere other than on the sponsored tours I recommend staying somewhere other than a Punta Cana resort.If you want to go to Punta Cana but you want a more upscale resort (at a higher price) I recommend Secrets Exclusive, which you could get to in about 5 minutes by taxi for $5 US from where we were. Its a five star and I was VERY impressed by their staff and sales manager.

<Content>Ola! What to say. Well, this was my first visit to a resort so maybe my expectations are different from others (like the people i went with). When we got to the airport it was a little straw hut basically! The bus ride took forever! But it was cool to see the towns lit up at night (which is when we arrived). The line to check in took a while, but we didnt get there until about 11 at night, so they didnt have a lot of staff up front to accomindate the 3 bus loads of people. After we checked in we headed for the buffet. Which is open about 24 hours a day! The beach is great at night to! The first day we took to look around and find out the time when breakfast ended and suck (breakfast ends at 10 am which kinda sucks, but the restaurants by the pool are open for lunch from 12-5 with breakfast from 8-12 so there is always food). the pool was huge! and at some arears to deep for even me, and i can swim pretty good. but it was always clean and fairly empty. Other than by the pool bar. which seams to always be packed. Domingo was an amazing bar tender, we wanted to tip him but didnt see him when we came back with money. The bar staff is more polite and can speak more english than the front service staff. I found them a little rude, even when i tried to speak spanish and make it a little easier for them to understand me. we took a taxi into town with Nicolas. who is really a nice man but cant speak any english, so take a dictonary to translate with. We wanted to go to Heguay which is where the restaurants and shopping is, but the frount service man told him to go to Sabo. which is 2 hours away from the resort, and there is nothing there. so dont waste the day going there! honestly. there is a market about 5 minutes to the left of the beach, just at the atv and lobster stand. they are really nice people. and if you want to get your hair braided, maria braids hair for 25 american dollars while the resort wants 45! i would rather pay the cheaper price, and give the business to the locals! just me though!. there is another market 30 minutes to the right. same stuff as at the other market but the poeple will try to suck you in. i suggest go the the front gift shop and jewlery store before you go the market. get an idea on prices, and you can talk them down, or understand their quality. the front gift shop and jewlery store are really expensive, but their stuff is ok. the markets you cant be sure of quality and dont get a receipt, so you can get screwed over. the mamajuana works! that is all i have to say about that! the food was ok, almost the same very night, and they used a lot of pork, which was a down side for the people i was with. i didnt get sick at all. maybe i was just lucky. they do have the internet their, 7 american dollars get you 30 minutes, 10 dollars get you an hour. their are 2 computer in the lobby, and 2 in the games room out front. I really enjoyed my stay. But there was one downside. their wasnt really anyone looking out for your stuff if you left your cd player under your stuff, wrapped in a towel someone may steal it! that is what happened to a friend of mine. also, someone had 60 dollars stolen from their wallet in their room! and another person walked into their room to find someone trying on their watch! so please be careful. it is worth the money to get the key to the inroom safe! well, i hope you enjoy your stay if you are going, and i recomend it if you are looking to go!

<Content>Amazing, amazing, amazing! Well where do I even begin....Punta Cana, D.R. is absolutly beautiful. I went there about a week ago with my mom, aunt and cousin and we had an amazing time at the Serenis resort. First of all you should know that the Serenis Tropical and Cocotal are mirror images of each other and share facilities. The only difference between the two is that the suits side has a little sitting room that we barely used. If your planning on stayign at this resort here are a few things you should know to make your stay more enjoyable. First, for a good spot by the pool, wake up early and put your towels on the chairs. There are plenty of chairs to be found, but if you want a nice spot under the shade of the little huts surrounding the pool go early! Secondly, tipping goes a long way. After the first couple days we found a great bartender, Domingo and gave him $5 US and told him there would be more coming at the end of the week, this resulted in amazing service at the swim up bar. We would call him from across the pool, jesture for our drinks and theyd be waiting on the side for us. Also if you dont get an ala carte reservation have no fear, if you go to the resaurant anyway an slip them a five they're more than willing to accomidate you. I would recomend the Italian (get the pizza) and mexican. We weren't too impressed with the steakhouse or the lobster at the mediterainian ...definatly dont order the lobster its gross, the shrimp and chicken (there dea of surf and turf) as well as the salmon are tastey. Thirdly, there is great shopping on the beach, especially to the left of the resort, good old Joe was there to give us the best deal on everything. Just remember to hagel! They expect it so dont feel bad or you'll just be ripping yourself off. Beware of the cigars though. The cohibas are fake, we didn't find that out until we got back, so unless your a real cigar conisur and know what's real and whats fake dont buy cigars. Also if your gettign your hair braided go to the ladies on the beach they charge 10-15 dollars lessi have really long thick hair and mine was only $25 US. Fourth, if your young and want to have a good time (i'm 18 and my cousin 20) MEET PEOPLE the nitelife isn't huge there, more of a family place but chilling in the lobby with other young people drinking until the bar closed was great then heading over to the disco. The music at the disco was suprisingly not bad. They played Top 40 stuff and merengue. There was an even amount of both, but dont be suprised if you hear some strange 50-Cent/merengue remix's. Fifth, bring pepto and imodium, tums, gravol everything but pepto is key because although most of the food was recognizable its still a little different. If you have a sensitive stomic expect one day of being sick. Everyone we talked to had one day of being sick and for all the other days you should be okay with pepto. I was told when I came back that they supposedly use non- pasturized milk so that could be one factor and anything that is fried , is fried in coconut oil which is a serious laxcidive. So other than that everyone is really friendly, the grounds are breathtaking, very clean, the weathers great even when it rain because it rains for about 5 minutes then drys up in about another 5 minutes, Overall staying at the Serenis resort you'll have an amazing vacation!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Have a Great time! August 2003Just got back from the Sirenis Tropical and a one week fabulous vacation.Traveled as a family of 4 with 2 boys ages 11 and 13.Airport Arrival The Punta Cana airport is a big straw hut. Arrival was on time and customs/baggage/boarding the bus was efficient and took in total about 45 minutes. We had no problem with the baggage carriers harassing us to take our bags. They can see that if you have small wheely bags that you don't need a porter. The bus ride is about 1 hour and 15 minutes and although you just want to get there, it is fine and air-conditioned.Hotel Arrival We were impressed with the front of the resort and the lobby. Big and beautiful. Clean and shiny marble floor. You are greeted with an non alcoholic drink (good for the kids) and check in was pretty organized and went as fast as expected. They had a lot of staff on the desk. Language was no problem, they spoke English better than I thought at the reception desk. We had requested 2 rooms side by side and both on the 2nd floor. We got exactly what we wanted! This was really important to me as the boys had there own room. Tropical and Coccotal are one and the same. Tropical has suites and Cocotal has hotel rooms.Hotel Room Clean, clean clean. The Tropical side of the resort are suites with a small living room that you really don't use. The bedroom had 2 double beds that we just pushed together. No problem. Pillows were better than I thought. I have neck problems so I was a little worried about that. Beds were firm but not hard. Best sleeps I have had in a long time. Air-conditioning worked just fine. Very nice room. Bathrooms were marble/ceramic. Clean. Water pressure and temperature was good too. No complaints. Maid service was just fine and we left $5 the first day and $2 every other day. However, I don't think the same person cleans your room every day so if you want to tip the maid, just leave a dollar or two every day.The Beach Beautiful!!!!!!!!! White sand, teal blue water. Lots of palm trees for shade. Yes, topless women. They mostly stuck to the beach when baring the boobs but the odd set at the pool too. It just became normal to us as the week went by.The Pool Huge!!!! For the most part kept very well. It may get a little cloudy near the swim up pool bars but not too bad. Please clean up your own cups when you are finished as there was some on the edge of the pool in the afternoon. Ladies, take a bikini! There were women of all sizes and ages wearing them. Don't give it a 2nd thought. Even if you don't think you'll wear one, take one anyway and decide when you get there. Swim up bars are great and were steady in the afternoon. Be patient and you will get served. Also an Hola to get there attention there and in any bar or restaurant will help. There is a lot of activities that you can participate in. There is a main board at the pool outlining the ones for the whole week. Or like us, you just snooze, swim, read and drink your day away!Saving Loungers If you need shade during the day, this is important. There are straw cabana huts at the pool and on the beach. If you want to claim one for the day, you will need to get up early. I was up by 7:30 am and down to the pool to save our loungers under a hut. You can put a towel on them, or a book or something. Once you do this you can leave it for any period of time. No one will take your chair. This obviously is hard for those who like to sleep in, but you can always catch up on your sleep on the lounger.Food Not as bad as I thought. Buffets had a lot of variety. Even picky eaters/kids can find something to make them happy. Lunch was down at the restaurants by the pool. Again a lot of selection and you can always default to fries and pizza. They have the BEST tomatoes I have ever tasted!!Dinner buffet was good too. We ate at the ala carte 4 times in the week. The Italian 2 times because they have the best pasta I have ever had. No kidding!!!! The BEST!. The steakhouse was good too. I have had far worse steaks at home. Mexican was good too. No problem in getting drinks here. Service was a bit slower than at home but not by much. We tipped $5 US at every ala carte meal. You are allowed 1 guaranteed reservation per week. The other you have to sign up for from 8-10 am. If the resort is busy, get there early (guest services in the lobby).Excursions Lots to choose from. we took the Kontiki snorkeling tour. A 1/2 day trip, lots of fun for kids and adults. Also if you want to go to the casino, there is a free shuttle to the Secrets resort. Worth the trip to see the lobby. BEWARE though as the table games are VERY fast. We won $30 US however!Tipping We did tip. Not because you get faster service but because we wanted to. These people are very friendly, happy and very poor. I took down some t-shirts my kids had grown out of and gave them to a lady there. Also I gave my toiletries I didn't use (hairspray, shampoo, body spray). We tipped when we felt like it. Take a lot of $1 US as they may not give change.Airport Departure This was a long hot irritating process for us. Really the only downfall of the whole trip. Take $20 Us per person departure tax, a personal fan from the dollar store, and lots of patience. It is a Hot and Crowded wait.Overall A terrific holiday. Relaxing and enjoyable. We would go back anytime! Have a great time!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great hotel and wonderful staff! Hola! We (my sister and I and our 18 and 20 year old daughters) just returned from Punta Cana, D.R. yesterday morning and I wanted to add my two cents worth to the list of reviews about the Sirenis Tropical Suites Hotel. It is infact, a complex that includes the Sirenis Cocotal Hotel- both hotels are practically a mirror image of each other and share the grounds and facilities. Our experience here at this hotel was wonderful. I too read all the reviews I could find about this place and with the exeception of a few minor complaints from some reviewers , all said excellent things about this place and we found them all to be true. The grounds and beach are absolutely beautiful!- lush tropical foliage everywhere. The grounds are kept immaculately clean. When you look through the coconut grove to the ocean view it looks like a tropical paradise-exquisite and breathtaking! The hotel rooms/suites are of the standard variety but clean and nice. The food and drink selection at the hotel is plentiful and varied. I worried about the food because I am a picky eater, but the buffet dinners and lunches and breakfast have a vast selection of things to choose from- and many normal things that you would likely eat back home can be found on the buffet tables- so don't worry about not finding something to eat. We found the food at the ala carte restaurants to be really great. We ate at 4 of the 5 ala carte's and really loved the Mexican and Italian ones especially. Some of the dishes (the salmon and the chicken  shrimp) at the seafood restaurant were excellent but the lobster dish and appetizers here, were not good. For a fantastic lobster dinner, try the local seafood restaurant wich is located right on the beach next to the hotel-very quaint and charming and freshly caught lobster can be had here for $10.00 U.S. per pound- we thoroughly enjoyed our dinner here for a total cost of $44.00 U.S for 4 people - four 1lb lobsters came complete with a huge plate of hot delicious french fries and large salad per person , with a soft drink each. The best thing, in my opinion about this hotel is the staff- staff from waiters to room maids to security were all extremely friendly and nice as were all the Dominican people that we met and encountered here in the Dominican Republic. They are just so darn nice!!! If I were to go back to the D.R. ( which I probably would again) the only thing that I might change is the choice of hotel simply for the fact that this is a very family- oriented hotel. We found that there were just too many families with young children here, for our liking. So for families, this is a great place but for us, who didn't necessarily want to be around so many children splashing around all day at the pool areas, next time I would choose an adults only hotel such as the 5 star Secrets Excellence Hotel, next door to the the Sirenis. P.S. - great deals can be had for souvenir shopping at the hut on the beach beside the hotel (hut on the left side of the hotel). Joseph the vendor there is a young local who is always ready to bargain and will give you a great deal. A tip about bargaining- always start at much less than half of what they are asking and then work your way up to half, otherwise you will be paying way too much. Hasta luego!

<Rating>5	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Truly wonderful We returned from Sirenis Tropical on July 13 and wanted to submit a review. Like many others, we read all the reviews here beforehand and, although many were good, there were a number of complaints about the resort that worried us ... This was really a shame because the worries were completely unfounded!!! ----- The service was great - the personnel was wonderful, always smiling, singing and dancing! I have a VERY hard time understanding how complaints were made about the staff - the barmen (and women!), cleaning ladies, garden workers, entertainment staff, waiters etc... always great! And yes, they may not all be fluent in English, but let's not forget that we're the tourists in their country - they made great efforts to speak English to us, and adored it when we tried to learn some Spanish phrases!! (Don't forget that although us North Americans in general tend to think we're the most important people on the planet and that the world revolves around us... it does NOT! Over 80% of the tourists at this resort are European - most of whom do indeed know basic Spanish and of course French!!) ---- As for food - you'd have to be a REALLY picky person to complain about this, honestly. For anyone who does NOT want to try 'different' food, there's always the staple salads, veggies, pasta (which they make right in front of you), pizza, hot dogs and fruit. Admittedly, there wasn't a great deal of variety at each meal, but the food menu was changed every day, so it more than compensated! (After all, no matter how much choice there would be at one meal, you can only eat so much in one sitting anyway!). ----- Drinks - The indoor bars are surprisingly well stocked in alcohol - even if you don't see your particular choice of liquor on the menus, just ask for it and chances are they'll have it! (They even stock champagne back there!!) ----- Entertainment was far better than we expected - particularly their team of dancers!! - one evening we were actually presented with a condensed version of Cats ... which was excellent! Yes, there were 2 evenings where the entertainment was quite 'amateurish', but I would hardly complain! ----- Overall, we had a wonderful time and can't complain about anything. The hotel was impeccably clean (you could see your face reflected on the marble floors of the lobby!) and the grounds and pools VERY well kept. We stayed at the Suites .... and the rooms there were clean and very spacious (each suit had a bedroom with a king sized bed or 2 double beds, a large bathroom and a decent sized living room or lounge area with a mini-bar that is refreshed daily. Another nice plus is that, although the resort was almost at it's fullest capacity, we never had problems finding nice shaded areas to set up on at the beach or the pool (i.e. you won't have to get up at 6am to get a spot on the beach) --- Final words .... Go for it!! This place is beautiful! BUT a word to the wise, if you're going here and expecting partying, loud music and booming night life, lots of shopping and nearby cities... it's NOT the place for you. The resort is very secluded with only one other resort fairly close by... If, on the other hand, you're looking for peace, relaxation, long private beaches to walk on ....a getaway from your daily stresses... then by all means you'll truly enjoy this resort.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved it, a great place to chill out! We stayed at the Sirenis Tropical Suites for 2 weeks in May. It was really excellent value for money  an overall great place to chill out  do nothing much. Food was really good, if anything the buffet better than some of the a la carte's. Best ALC was the steakhouse, we went twice  really enjoyed it there except for the mozzies!The complex is huge, but somewhat in the middle of nowhere so you are a little restricted if you want to go to lots of shopping malls etc. Some Brits we spoke to that took taxis into town for shopping said that it was pretty much a waste of time anyway! There are a few huts down the beach that sell cigars, rum, sarongs, film, suncream etc that seem to offer much better value than the official on-site shops. We took the day trip to Saona Island which was without doubt the highlight of the holiday. A leisurely catamaran trip (very big, very nice, not packed at all) drinking rum  coke, Carribean sea lapping your toes, plenty of photo's, sitting on the front of the boat watching the flying fish, speedboat to the island, more rum  cokes, beautiful beach (they filmed the bounty ads there apparently!), excellent BBQ, bit of sunbathing, more rum  coke (they do do beer or just coke as well!), speedboat to a nearby lagoon for a spot of swimming. Get the picture? A remember it for a lifetime experience. Take a disposable/waterproof camera on this trip, save dropping your expensive one in the sea! The hotel was very well kept, groundsmen working day  night keeping everything tidy. Rooms were clean,  spacious, no problems there. OK some of the staff were a little laid back, some didn't speak brilliant English, we were guests in their country after all, what do some people expect? OK, maybe it isn't a 5* hotel by European standards but hey, how much would 14 nights all inclusive in a UK 5* hotel cost? A darn sight more than this. We would definitely recommend it, maybe more of a couples place than one for kids. Its a 9 hour flight are only 2 or 3!! There were some kids there even younger than that! We didn't join in with the evening entertainment (not our thing), so can't comment on that. Every couple of nights there was a boy band on in the main bar area who were pretty good, singing to backing tapes, Backstreet Boys sort of stuff plus some Spanish songs. Not a club 18-30 sort of a place, if that's what you want, throbbing night-life, loads of shopping, this isn't the place for you. If however you just want to chill by the pool, join in with a few activities if you want, good food served all day, good quality drinks (try the lemon slush for a refreshing nice non-alchoholic daytime drink) served all day, read a book, have a snooze then you could do a hell of a lot worse than here.PS the local 151 Rum is said to be excellent for soothing those mozzie bites (applied externally that is)!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel in the sky The Hotel Sofitel is situated on the top 20 or so floors of a 50 level building. Lobby on the ground floor is in the grand style with high roofs , hidden lighting and floor to ceiling windows looking out either onto the shopping plaza (checkin) or driveway (lounge/bar). Fast lifts take your to the rooms which are set around a atrium. Ground floor of the atrium (but about level 35 I think) has another bar in the centre and a cafe on the edge of one side and a french restaurant on the other. All these share along with the rooms fantastic views over Melbourne suburbs, parks and the MCG (football ground). Rooms are generally done in dark wood overtones with olive/cream carpets and bedding. All are good size. Windows have blinds and wooden shutters but part of the attraction is to sleep in bed with the blinds up for the view. This hotel also has the best toilets with a view in town with floor to ceiling windows (who is going to see you on level 35). Rooms service is fast and prices are as expected of a 5 star hotel. Afternoon tea on sundays in the ground floor lounge is great - about AUD$29 for a buffet with coffee/ tea/ cakes, scones/ cream/ sandwiches and hot nibbles. its help your self so getting money worth is not a problem (just your weight). Small shopping centre attached (in part catering to office workers) as is a arthouse cinema and for those that can't do without, a Macdonalds across the road. Its on a tram/ trolley car route, around the corner from Parliament Underground station and about 10 minute walk from the main shopping area of the city. Location is up near Parliament House at the top of Collins Street. All in, a great treat for a weekend away.

<Rating>5	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Pleasant overall I spent 7 days at Sirenis Cocotal Beach Resort in Punta Cana DR with my best girlfriend. We are both living in Canada, and wanted to take a break from our jobs and just go on vacation. For the most part we enjoyed our stay at the hotel. The beach, and ocean was very lovely. Sirenis is a very clean hotel. The maid service was also very good. Sirenis is more like a 4* hotel. The grounds were pleasant enough, and very clean. We did not care for the stagnant greenish wading water that dotted the landscape. A couple of nice running water fountains would have been nice. The flamencos treading in the wading water didn't seem to mind however. I actually enjoyed the food. I love fish of all kinds and the had a variety everyday. My only complaint - some of the chicken and lamb were too under-cooked for my tastes. Not everyone enjoys rare meat, but if you were willing to wait a couple of minutes they would cook the meat on the grill to suit your tastes. I also did not care for the hamburger at the poolside. Not you typical beefburger. The main entertainment stage was comparable to even 4* star hotel. I did not care for some of the pre-show entertainment using audience members. If you sat upfront you would require a excellent sense of humor if they got you up on stage. Once the real shows got underway at 10:00pm they were very good. The disco was fun, if you like techno, and lots of meringue, with a sprinkling of rap and hip hop. Friday to Sunday was well filled up with staff and guests. The hotel staff was very amenable to showing dance steps and having a good time with the guests in the disco. Most of the staff was quite pleasant (especially if we smiled or spoke in Spanish or French). We had some trouble communicating that we wanted wash cloths or face cloths, but they understood and supplied us with some in short order (it is not regularly supplied). We do have some tips and recommendations that we think would help make you vacation more fulfilling: 1. Take a light plastic ra almost everyday on and off. The rain was mostly followed by the hot sun. When the sun was out she was out in full force. I recommend not staying out for more than an hour on your first day, work in your tan gradually, because nearly everyone ended up peeling, and there were lots of nasty looking sunburns. Apply lots of sunscreen to you forehead , nose and shoulders. Better yet wear a hat. The sun is hottest between 12 noon and 2 pm. 2. Take money to tip. One US dollar is = to 20 DR pesos. They'll do a one way US to pesos change at the Check in Desk (so don't change ALL of your money). Tip your room cleaner if they do a good job. Tip at the restaurant and bar if you like the service. Tip the bus driver if you like his driving. Tip the bar tenders if you want. Tip the guy who carries you luggage to your room if you like the service. By all means you don't have to do it all the time, but it is nice to do it sometimes. 3. Go on an excursion, just to take a break from the resort routine. We went to Saona for the day, and enjoyed it. We also went to Higuey and visited a couple of bars. Your tour rep might be amendable to taking you, wouldn't hurt to ask. If you go to another beach away from the hotel, take some practical shoes you can walk in the water with. We saw several people cut their feet or fall on rocks and hurt their shins in the water at the two above places. 4. If you speak even a little Spanish or French it will help immensely in getting what you need. 5. If you have a sensitive stomach, take some Imodium, and/or Gravol. The food is well seasoned, and if you are only used to bland food, you might find yourself just eating French fries and hamburgers (hence the Imodium). ALL the alcohol is inclusive, hence the Gravol, and maybe some Advil. 6. Take a few long sleeved tops and pants, as it may get cool after it rains, before turning crazy humid at night. Speaking of humid, take some mosquito repellant because after the rain falls the little buggers come out. 7. Take some goggles to se hotel of course, is on the Atlantic side, and has waves - it also gets deep rather quickly from shore. But the water was lovely, and the beach fabulous. 8. At certain times of day they do not allow you to saunter into the poolside restaurant in your wet bathing suit, so bring a sarong, shorts and T-Shirt. As expected at NO time can you go to the main restaurants in swimsuit gear. Dress nicely for the evening time. Try out one of the A La Carte restaurants as well - it's all inclusive. 9. If you like to work out the gym is clean and has just the right amount of equipment. It is also built so that it lets outdoor air in, making for a wonderful workout experience. There are also several tennis courts that you can book a day ahead of time. We went for a morning run on the beach 5 out of the 7 days we were there - it was blissful. Go on and enjoy yourself! Andrea
